Walker v. Campbell


Supreme Court case no. 17S03-9911-CV-670


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


719 N.E.2d 1248; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 1090



November 24, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Court of Appeals case no. 17A03-9806-CV-279. DeKalb Circuit Court case no. 17C01-9710-AD-016.



DISPOSITION: Appellants' motion to dismiss granted, and appeal dismissed.

 

2 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Weinberg v. Bess


Supreme Court No. 45S03-9503-CV-307


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


717 N.E.2d 584; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 934



October 8, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT, ROOM TWO, The Honorable Morton B. Kanz, Judge. Cause No. 45D02-9207-CP-689. Court of Appeals No. 45A03-9309-CV-311.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff petitioned to transfer the order of the Court of Appeals (Ind.) which held that plaintiff's claims for medical malpractice against defendant were time barred under Ind. Code § 34-18-7-1(b).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought suit against defendant for medical malpractice. The basis of her claim was that defendant gave her silicone based breast implants even though he had represented to her that the implants were saline based. Defendant moved for summary judgment contending that plaintiff's claims were time-barred by the two-year statute of limitations for medical malpractice, Ind. Code § 34-18-7-1(b). The trial court denied defendant summary judgment, but on appeal the order was reversed and remanded. On transfer, the court held that the two-year medical malpractice statute of limitations was unconstitutional as applied to plaintiffs who are unable to discover their medical malpractice claims before the expiration of the limitations period. Even though plaintiff did not discover her claim until eight years after her operation, she still brought it within the limitations period.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision holding that plaintiff's claims were time barred, since the statute of limitations was unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff since she was unable to discover her claim before the expiration of the limitations period.

 

3 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Halbe v. Weinberg


Supreme Court No. 45S03-9506-CV-692


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


717 N.E.2d 876; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 935



October 8, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended on Denial of Rehearing of January 7, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ind. LEXIS 2.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT, ROOM ONE. The Honorable Jeffrey J. Dywan, Judge. Cause No. 45D01-9204-CT-452. Court of Appeals No. 45A03-9310-CV-344.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed decision by the Lake Superior Court, Room One, Court of Appeals that affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant in plaintiff's suit for medical malpractice.


OVERVIEW: Defendant performed breast implant surgery on plaintiff. Plaintiff requested saline implants. The implants were replaced three times. Saline implants were used in the first two surgeries, but defendant used silicone implants in the last without informing plaintiff. Several years later, plaintiff discovered that the implants were silicone. Plaintiff brought suit against defendant. Defendant filed a motion for summary judgment that was granted by the trial court and affirmed by the court of appeals. Plaintiff appealed. The court held that the two-year medical malpractice statute of limitations should not have been applied to plaintiff because plaintiff was unable to discover the claim before its expiration. Plaintiff had no reason to suspect that defendant used silicone implants in the third surgery and she used reasonable diligence in pursuing her claim upon discovering the silicone implants. Therefore, the court reversed and remanded the case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed because medical malpractice statute of limitations did not apply to plaintiff until she discovered or should have discovered that defendant had used silicone breast implants instead of saline implants as requested by plaintiff.

 

4 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Huffman v. State


49S00-9704-CR-260


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


717 N.E.2d 571; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 924



October 4, 1999, Decided  
October 4, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Huffman v. State, 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 2550 (Ind. Ct. App., Dec. 28, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Paula Lopossa, Judge. Cause No. 84004843.
State v. Huffman, 643 N.E.2d 899, 1994 Ind. LEXIS 186 (Ind., 1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the sentence imposed by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), after defendant pleaded guilty to charges of murder and conspiracy to commit robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant participated in beating a man to death. After pleading guilty, he challenged the trial court's imposition of the maximum sentence of 60 years for murder and 30 years for conspiracy to commit robbery, to run concurrently. On appeal, the court held the sentencing court was not obliged to consider defendant's extreme voluntary alcohol and drug intoxication as a mitigating factor in sentencing. Since evaluating the extent of intoxication is a factual matter, it was best left to the sentencing court's discretion. Even though this case resulted after a post-conviction reversal and retrial, the current sentencing court was not bound by the previous sentencing court's determination that defendant's intoxication did serve as a mitigating factor. The sentencing court was permitted to consider defendant's prior juvenile adjudications as an aggravating factor, except for a juvenile proceeding that ended without disposition. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court upheld defendant's maximum sentence for murder, because whether to regard defendant's extreme voluntary intoxication as a mitigating factor was a factual determination within the sentencing court's discretion.

 

5 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Richardson v. State


67S01-9910-CR-506


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


717 N.E.2d 32; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 918



October 1, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM PUTNAM CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Diana LaViolette, Judge. Cause No. 67C01-9609-CF-74.



DISPOSITION: Conviction and sentence vacated. Cause remanded to the trial court for disposition consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Putnam Circuit Court (Indiana) entered judgment convicting defendant of robbery and battery. Defendant was then sentenced to eight years imprisonment for the robbery and one year for the battery. The sentences were to run consecutively. The Court of Appeals affirmed and defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his battery and robbery convictions, claiming a violation of Indiana's Double Jeopardy Clause, Ind. Const. art. I, §14. The court limited its review to the "same offense" facet of double jeopardy jurisprudence. The court superseded many earlier decisions by adopting the actual evidence test and the statutory elements test, holding that both must be analyzed to determine if two or more convictions are of the same offense. The court applied the Indiana Constitution, noting that it afforded broader double jeopardy protection that did the U.S. Constitution. The court found that defendant demonstrated a reasonable possibility that the evidentiary facts used by the jury to establish the essential elements of robbery were also used to establish the essential elements of the battery. Holding that both convictions could not stand, the court vacated the conviction and sentence with the less severe penal consequences, the battery conviction.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's battery conviction and sentence because of a double jeopardy violation.

 

6 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Benefiel v. State


Cause No. 84S00-9207-PD-590


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


716 N.E.2d 906; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 859



September 29, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied October 2, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5249.
Rehearing denied by Benefiel v. State, 1999 Ind. LEXIS 1202 (Ind., Dec. 27, 1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Benefiel v. Indiana, 531 U.S. 830, 148 L. Ed. 2d 45, 121 S. Ct. 83, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5249 (2000)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Benefiel v. Davis, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 1415 (7th Cir. Ind., Jan. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE VIGO SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Frank M. Nardi, Special Judge. Cause No. 84D01-8705-CF-34.
Benefiel v. Indiana, 504 U.S. 987, 119 L. Ed. 2d 591, 112 S. Ct. 2971, 1992 U.S. LEXIS 3599 (1992)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of post-conviction court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgment of the Vigo (Indiana) Superior Court, which denied defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminal confinement, rape, and murder, and sentenced to death. Subsequent to affirmance of the conviction and sentence on his direct appeal, defendant filed for post-conviction relief. Defendant argued his trial counsel was ineffective, his right to be present at trial was violated when he refused to enter the courtroom, and the jury's role in recommending a penalty was depreciated in jury instructions. The court applied state's applicable two-part test in determining ineffective assistance of counsel, and held trial counsel's actions did not, either separately or cumulatively, rise to the level of ineffective assistance. The court then held defendant failed to prove he did not voluntarily waive his right to be present at his trial when he refused to reenter courtroom. Applying prior case law, court held jury's role was not depreciated by trial court's instructions informing jury of its advisory role in determining defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, as post-conviction relief was not warranted.

 

7 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Wooley v. State


Supreme Court Cause No. 61S00-9806-CR-354


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


716 N.E.2d 919; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 861



September 29, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Wooley v. State, 1999 Ind. LEXIS 1197 (Ind., Dec. 15, 1999)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Without opinion by Wooley v. State, 897 N.E.2d 541, 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 3251 (Ind. Ct. App., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE PARKE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Ronda R. Brown, Judge. Cause No. 61C01-9608-CF-82.



DISPOSITION: Wooley's conviction for murder affirmed and remanded for new sentencing consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Parke Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant, after a jury trial, of murder, sentencing him to imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder, attempted murder, and attempted arson. Defendant moved for a continuance four times. The state moved for a continuance as well. The trial was reset upon each motion. Defendant was ultimately held for 383 days before trial. Defendant was found guilty of murder and sentenced to 65 years imprisonment. The trial court found no mitigating circumstances, but three aggravating circumstances, a prior conviction for drunk driving, defendant's need of correctional or rehabilitative treatment best provided by incarceration, and the circumstances of defendant's crime. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed conviction, but remanded for new sentencing, finding that although the trial court found one proper aggravating circumstance, the circumstance of defendant's crime, it relied on two that were improper. Therefore, the court could not conclude trial court would have imposed maximum sentence if it considered the nature and circumstances of the crime alone as the sole aggravating circumstance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed conviction, but remanded for new sentencing, finding although trial court found one proper aggravating circumstance, it relied on two that were improper. Therefore the court could not conclude trial court would have imposed maximum sentence if it considered nature and circumstances of crime as sole aggravating circumstance.

9 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Harris v. Raymond


Supreme Court No. 71S05-9805-CV-276


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


715 N.E.2d 388; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 716



September 2, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] INTERLOCUTORY APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Terry A. Crone, Judge Cause No. 71C01-9506-CT-26. Court of Appeals No. 71A05-9604-CV-162.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for summary judgment and remanded to the St. Joseph Circuit Court for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the order of the St. Joseph Circuit Court (Indiana) denying defendants' motion for summary judgment based on defendants' allegation that plaintiffs' dental malpractice action was barred by the statute of limitations under the Medical Malpractice Act, Ind. Code § 34-18-7-1(b) (1998).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, husband, wife, and insurance commissioner, filed an action against defendants, dentist and professional corporation, for malpractice concerning implants in plaintiff wife's jaw. The malpractice was discovered five years after the devices were implanted when plaintiff wife was injured by the implants' shattering. Defendants' motion for summary judgment based on the two-year statute of limitations for medical malpractice actions was denied. Defendants appealed. The court affirmed and held that plaintiffs were required to file the action within two years of discovering the cause of action, which they did. The medical malpractice statute of limitations applied to dental malpractice because defendants were health care providers. Defendants' duty to warn and adequately explain the risks extended to former patients. Plaintiffs had two years from discovering the malpractice to file the claim because plaintiffs would have otherwise been foreclosed from filing an action before they knew of the malpractice or any injury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendants' motion for summary judgment and held that plaintiffs had not filed their medical malpractice action after the statute of limitations had passed.

 

10 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Van Dusen v. Stotts


Supreme Court No. 03S00-9711-CV-631


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


712 N.E.2d 491; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 417



July 8, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE BARTHOLOMEW SUPERIOR COURT II. The Honorable Norman D. Curry, Judge. Cause No. 03D02-9609-CP-193.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the decision below granting plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment and denying defendants' motion. Remanded for further proceedings not in consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of an order from the Bartholomew Superior Court II (Indiana) granting summary judgment to appellees and denying summary judgment to appellants in an action brought by appellees for medical malpractice.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, husband and wife, brought suit in 1996 against appellant physicians and appellant hospital for medical malpractice after appellant physicians misread a biopsy in 1992 and did not discover appellee husband's cancer. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees. The court affirmed the trial court's decision. The two-year statute of limitations did not begin to run until appellees received information that there was a reasonable possibility that his injury was caused by appellants' acts. Thus, the statute of limitations began to run in 1995 when appellee husband consulted another physician who informed him he had incurable cancer and told appellees that the biopsy might have been misread.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting summary judgment to appellees because appellees filed their claim within the two-year statute of limitations for medical malpractice. The court also remanded for further consistent proceedings.

 

11 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Richey


Supreme Court No. 53S04-9805-CV-271


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


711 N.E.2d 1273; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 418



July 8, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 9, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MONROE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Douglas R. Bridges, Judge. Cause No. 53C05-9505-CP-585. Court of Appeals No. 53A04-9603-CV-104.



DISPOSITION: Reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant and remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion and with opinion in Van Dusen also decided today.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant physician appealed the decision of the Court of Appeals of Indiana, Fourth District, which reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in his favor in plaintiff's medical malpractice action, holding that the two-year statute of limitations of Indiana's Medical Malpractice Act, Ind. Code § 34-18-7-1(b) (1998), was unconstitutional under Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 and Ind. Const. art. I, § 12.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed suit alleging that defendant, her physician, negligently failed to diagnose and treat her breast cancer in a timely manner. The trial court granted defendant summary judgment because plaintiff did not file suit within the two-year statute of limitations of Indiana's Medical Malpractice Act, Ind. Code § 34-18-7-1(b) (1998). The court of appeals reversed, holding that the fraudulent concealment doctrine allowed plaintiff to avoid the statute of limitations and that, in any event, the statute of limitations was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court agreed with the result reached by the court of appeals and reversed the trial court's judgment. However, the court upheld the facial constitutionality of the statute of limitations and concluded that it was unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff under the Privileges and Immunities Clause of Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 because it was not uniformly applicable to all medical malpractice victims and barred plaintiff's claim due to the long latency period of her disease. The court also concluded that the statute of limitations was unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff under the Open Courts Clause of Ind. Const. art. I, § 12.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant physician and remanded for further proceedings. The appellate court concluded that the statute of limitations of the state's medical malpractice act was not facially unconstitutional, but that the statute of limitations was only invalid as applied to plaintiff under applicable clauses of the state constitution.

 

12 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Baldwin v. Reagan


Supreme Court No. 32S00-9812-CV-767


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


715 N.E.2d 332; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 413



July 6, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended July 23, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE HENDRICKS SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable David H. Coleman, Judge. Cause No. 32D02-9810-CP-212.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of trial court declaring the Seatbelt Enforcement Act unconstitutional is reversed and permanent injunction with respect thereto is dissolved. Judgment of trial court holding Good Faith Belief Act constitutional is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, prosecutor and sheriff, appealed the judgment of the Hendricks Superior Court (Indiana) declaring the Indiana Seatbelt Enforcement Act, Ind. Code § 9-19-10-3, unconstitutional and permanently enjoining enforcement of the statute.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed suit against defendants, the sheriff and prosecutor of a county in Indiana, contending that the Indiana Seatbelt Enforcement Act, Ind. Code § 9-19-10-3, authorized the police to stop motorists in violation of their state constitutional rights against unreasonable searches and seizures. The trial court held that the statute violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 11 and permanently enjoined defendants from enforcing it. On appeal, the court agreed that the police may not enforce the seat belt law in violation of the state constitutional rights against unreasonable searches and searches and held that an Indiana police officer may not stop a motorist to enforce the seat belt law unless the officer observes circumstances that would cause an ordinary person to agree that the driver or passenger is not wearing a seat belt. However, the court determined that the statute could be applied in conformity with its holding and concluded that the statute was constitutional. The court further concluded that the statute did not violate the Good Faith Belief Act, Ind. Code § 34-28-5-3. Accordingly, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and dissolved the permanent injunction.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment, which declared the state seatbelt enforcement statute unconstitutional and dissolved the trial court's permanent injunction. The appellate court concluded that the police could not enforce the statute in violation of the state constitutional rights against unreasonable searches and seizures, but that the statute could be applied in a constitutional manner.

 

13 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Brownsburg Area Patrons Affecting Change v. Baldwin


Cause No. 94S00-9803-CQ-144


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


714 N.E.2d 135; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 406



June 23, 1999, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Certified question answered in the affirmative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court addressed a certified question from the U.S. Court of Appeals, Seventh Circuit, regarding the definition of a political action committee under Ind. Code § 3-5-2-37.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was a small association for educating citizens on political, economic, and social issues. The county election board chairman asserted that if plaintiff spent over $ 100 on its hotline recording message it would be required to follow the rules for political action committees (PACs). The district court denied plaintiff's motion for a preliminary injunction, holding that plaintiff was not a PAC under Indiana law. Ind. Code § 3-5-2-37 did not apply to organizations engaged only in issue advocacy, and plaintiff by its own definition engaged only in issue advocacy. Plaintiff appealed, contending that the district court erred in holding that the PAC definition applied only to express advocacy groups. The court of appeals certified a question regarding whether the statutory definition of a PAC included only those organizations which make contributions or expenditures for communications that in express terms advocate the election or defeat of a clearly identified candidate or a public question. The court construed the statute narrowly and answered in the affirmative.


OUTCOME: Certified question was answered in the affirmative because the definition of political action committee under the Indiana Code should be narrowly construed to include only organizations that make contributions for express advocacy of the election or defeat of a clearly identified candidate or public question.

 

14 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Journal-Gazette Co. v. Bandido's, Inc.


Supreme Court No. 57S03-9709-CV-00495


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


712 N.E.2d 446; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 409; 27 Media L. Rep. 2089



June 23, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied November 15, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7548.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NOBLE CIRCUIT COURT. Court of Appeals No. 57A03-9407-CV-248. The Honorable Howard E. Petersen, Special Judge. Cause No. 57C01-8901-CP-007.



DISPOSITION: Both private individuals and public figures must prove actual malice to recover in defamation suit involving matters of public or general concern. Bandido's has failed to prove that Journal-Gazette acted with actual malice. Judgment of trial court reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff restaurant sought review of an order of the court of appeals (Indiana), reversing the trial court's entry of judgment for plaintiff and entering judgment for defendant news service in plaintiff's action for defamation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant newspaper published a story reporting the health violations of plaintiff restaurant. The headline of the story read: "Inspectors find rats, roaches at local eatery." However, the article did not report that inspectors had found rats at the restaurant, but did accurately report that rodent droppings were found. Alerted to the discrepancy, defendant printed an apology although the headline did not indicate that the apology was a retraction. Plaintiff sued defendant for defamation. The trial court entered judgment for plaintiff. The court of appeals reversed, finding that plaintiff did not produce clear and convincing evidence of actual malice. On appeal, the court affirmed. Where the alleged defamation addressed a subject of public concern, the actual malice standard was required in cases involving private individuals, in addition to public figures. Plaintiff's evidence was insufficient to meet the clear and convincing evidence standard. The use of the word "rats" in the headline rather than "rodents" did not indicate actual malice because defendant was not shown to have known of the inaccuracy before publication.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of appeals and reversed the judgment of the trial court; plaintiff failed to show by clear and convincing evidence that defendant's publication of the headline featured actual malice, which was required to sustain a defamation suit regarding comments of public interest.

 

15 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Dible v. City of Lafayette


Supreme Court No. 79S02-9710-CV-619


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


713 N.E.2d 269; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 397



June 9, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Joseph W. Carey, Special Judge. Cause No. 79C01-9406-CP-209. Court of Appeals No. 79A02-9610-CV-619.



DISPOSITION: Previously granted transfer, thereby vacating opinion of Court of Appeals. Affirmed trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the City.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of a decision of the Tippecanoe Circuit Court (Indiana) entering summary judgment in favor of defendant city, in action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief requiring defendant to remove sewage and drainage structures it had built on a city easement on plaintiffs' property. Action was before the court on a previously granted petition to transfer, which thereby vacated the opinion of the lower appellate court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant city, which held a sewer and drainage easement on plaintiff's property, commenced building sewage and drainage structures within its easement. Defendant's project created a concrete drain in a natural ravine, although a recorded covenant prohibited the alteration of the ravine. Plaintiffs sought an injunction requiring defendant to remove the structures. Defendant filed a motion for summary judgment, and the motion was granted. Plaintiffs appealed, and the appellate court reversed with directions for the suit to proceed as a public lawsuit. Defendant's petition to transfer was granted and the court affirmed the trial court, holding that declaratory and injunctive relief was unavailable to plaintiffs. According to the court, equitable relief was not available to enjoin an alleged taking of private property for a public use, duly authorized by law, when a suit for compensation could be brought against the city; and the lower appellate court erroneously declared the plaintiffs' lawsuit a public lawsuit because the plaintiffs had not brought suit in their capacity as taxpayers, but rather, were seeking an injunction to protect their private property rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed trial court's summary judgment for appellee in action brought seeking declaratory and injunctive relief requiring defendant to remove sewage and drainage structures it built on a city easement on plaintiffs' property. Summary judgment was proper because correct remedy was a suit for compensation. Action was not a public lawsuit as plaintiffs had not brought suit as taxpayers and were seeking to protect private property rights.

 

16 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Conner v. State


49S00-9207-PD-00591


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


711 N.E.2d 1238; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 344



May 25, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied October 2, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5230.
Rehearing denied by Conner v. State, 1999 Ind. LEXIS 1061 (Ind., Nov. 10, 1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Conner v. Indiana, 531 U.S. 829, 148 L. Ed. 2d 43, 121 S. Ct. 81, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 5230 (2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James K. Coachys, Special Judge. Cause No. 49G01-8801-CF-08449.
Conner v. Indiana, 504 U.S. 936, 118 L. Ed. 2d 600, 112 S. Ct. 2006, 1992 U.S. LEXIS 3063 (1992)
Conner v. State, 580 N.E.2d 214, 1991 Ind. LEXIS 197 (Ind., 1991)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the post-conviction court's denial of the defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of murder in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) and, upon denial of post-conviction relief, appellant sought review and asserted errors involving ex parte jury communication, non-disclosure of exculpatory evidence, jury instructions, admission of confession, assistance of counsel, mental health evaluations, death penalty issues, exclusion of evidence, and violation of due process.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and received the death penalty. Upon the denial of post-conviction relief, appellant asserted multiple errors. The court found that evidence submitted regarding an alleged ex parte communication to the jury did not lead unmistakably and unerringly to a conclusion contrary to the post-conviction court's decision. An exculpatory evidence claim was without merit where review of the record demonstrated that the information was available to appellant through the exercise of reasonable diligence. The court held there was no error in jury instructions where the jury was clearly instructed to acquit in the presence of reasonable doubt. As to a claim that a confession was improperly admitted, the court found that there was nothing to indicate that the confession was unreliable or involuntary. In addition, the evidence did not show ineffective assistance of counsel at trial or on appeal. The court also declined to find constitutional infirmity, and rejected appellant's claim that his conviction and death sentence were unreliable and fundamentally erroneous. The court accordingly affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's petition for post-conviction relief. The court held that appellant failed to show any substantive, procedural, or constitutional violations after the jury convicted him of murder and sentenced him to death, and appellant was not denied effective assistance of counsel at trial or on appeal.

 

17 of 1699 DOCUMENTS



Rondon v. State


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 45S00-9403-PD-229


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


711 N.E.2d 506; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 345



May 25, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Richard J. Conroy, Judge. Cause No. 2CR-186-1084-760.



DISPOSITION: Remanded for a new penalty phase and sentencing hearing. In all other respects, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) where he was convicted of murder and felony murder and was sentenced to death. Appellant asserted that the mental retardation exemption from the death penalty applied, that he received ineffective assistance of trial and appellate counsel, that he was denied a fair post-conviction forum, and that an accumulation of alleged errors warranted relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and felony murder and was sentenced to death. Appellant sought review and contended that the mental retardation exemption from the death penalty applied, that he received ineffective assistance of trial and appellate counsel, that he was denied a fair post-conviction forum, and that an accumulation of alleged errors warranted relief. On review, the court found that appellant was not a mentally retarded individual within the meaning of Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9. As to appellant's arguments of ineffective assistance of counsel, the court examined the record and determined that it would not substitute judgment on strategic decision made by appellant's counsel and that there was no showing that the performance fell below an objective standard of reasonableness. The court found that mitigation evidence was available but never presented to the jury or the sentencing court and held that in such a situation the death sentence imposed would be unfair and unreliable. The court reversed in this regard and remanded for a new penalty phase.


OUTCOME: The appellant's convictions were affirmed because appellant did not meet the definition of a mentally retarded individual and because his counsel's performance did not fall below an objective standard of reasonableness. However, the court reversed and remanded for a new penalty phase because mitigation evidence was available but never presented, thus making the death sentence imposed unfair and unreliable.


 

18 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Goliday v. State


49S00-9709-CR-500


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


708 N.E.2d 4; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 163



March 19, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Z. Mae Jimison, Judge. Cause No. 49G20-9604-CF-047573.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for dealing in cocaine in violation of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-1, a class A felony; possession of cocaine in violation of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6, a class C felony; possession of marijuana in violation of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-11, a class A misdemeanor; and two counts of resisting law enforcement in violation of Ind. Code § 35-44-3-3, both class A misdemeanors, from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of dealing in cocaine in violation of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-1; possession of cocaine in violation of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6; possession of marijuana in violation of Ind. Code § 35-48-4-11; and two counts of resisting law enforcement in violation of Ind. Code § 35-44-3-3. He appealed, arguing there was insufficient evidence for the conviction and that the trial court erred in failing to suppress improperly seized evidence. Here, the trial court proved that defendant had constructive possession of the drugs by showing that defendant had both the intent to maintain dominion and control and the capability to maintain dominion and control over the drugs. Defendant's exclusive possession of the vehicle when police stopped it was sufficient to raise a reasonable inference of intent. As for defendant's argument that the trial court erred in failing to suppress evidence secured during a police inventory search of the vehicle incident to impoundment, Ind. Code § 9-18-2-43(a) (1993) required the officer to take the vehicle into custody because it bore a stolen license plate. An inventory search was required before the vehicle could be towed. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for dealing in cocaine, possession of cocaine, possession of marijuana, and two counts of resisting law enforcement, because there was sufficient evidence for the conviction and because the trial court did not err in failing to suppress evidence secured during a police inventory search of the vehicle incident to impoundment.

 

19 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Rouster v. State


Cause No. 45S00-9304-PD-408


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


705 N.E.2d 999; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 66



February 19, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 28, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ind. LEXIS 863.
Rehearing denied by Rouster v. State, 718 N.E.2d 737, 1999 Ind. LEXIS 914 (Ind., 1999)
Rehearing denied by Rouster v. State, 718 N.E.2d 737, 1999 Ind. LEXIS 863 (Ind., 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Richard J. Conroy, Judge. Cause No. 2CR-133-886-531.
Rouster v. State, 600 N.E.2d 1342, 1992 Ind. LEXIS 233 (Ind., 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a Lake Superior Court (Indiana) decision that denied his postconviction relief petition challenging his jury conviction of felony murder and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged the trial court's denial of his postconviction relief motion that challenged his jury trial felony murder conviction and death sentence. The appellate court affirmed the decision of the trial court. Appellant received effective assistance from both his trial and appellate counsel because appellant was unable to show deficient counsel performance or resulting prejudice. Counsel did not err by failing to file a motion to have appellant tried separately from his co-defendant. Appellant had no absolute right to separate trial and even if a motion for separate trials had been filed, the trial court judge would have been within his discretion if he denied it. The jury was within its discretion in sentencing appellant to death because the trial court gave the jury sufficient and nonconfusing instructions. There was sufficient evidence that appellant formed the required mens rea and that he was able to appreciate the criminality of his conduct, because no mental disease or defect prevented such a formation. Aggravating factors outweighed mitigating factors beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court decision, after a jury trial, which convicted appellant of felony murder and sentenced him to death. Appellant received effective assistance from both his trial and appellate counsel and was not entitled to be tried separately from his co-defendant. Jury instructions regarding sentencing were proper and there was sufficient evidence that aggravating factors outweighed mitigating factors.

 

20 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. State


Cause No. 45S00-9303-PD-397


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


706 N.E.2d 149; 1999 Ind. LEXIS 67



February 19, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied May 15, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3248.
Rehearing denied by Williams v. State, 718 N.E.2d 737, 1999 Ind. LEXIS 862 (Ind., 1999)
Rehearing denied by Williams v. State, 718 N.E.2d 737, 1999 Ind. LEXIS 915 (Ind., 1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Williams v. Indiana, 529 U.S. 1113, 146 L. Ed. 2d 800, 120 S. Ct. 1970, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 3248 (2000)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Williams v. Anderson, 174 F. Supp. 2d 843, 2001 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 19290 (N.D. Ind., 2001)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Richard J. Conroy, Special Judge. Cause No. 2CR-133-886-531.
Rouster v. State, 600 N.E.2d 1342, 1992 Ind. LEXIS 233 (Ind., 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), denying defendant's petition for post-trial relief following the entry of his convictions for felony murder and sentence of death. Defendant claimed denial was improper where he received ineffective assistance of counsel, the trial court failed to give instructions on sentencing options and an intoxication defense, and the post-trial court improperly denied expert testimony.


OVERVIEW: Denial of defendant's post-trial conviction was affirmed where defendant received effective assistance of counsel, sentencing options instructions were properly denied, and the post-trial court properly denied expert testimony. Defendant was convicted of murdering his foster parents during a robbery. Defendant brought a post-trial petition, claiming over 60 errors regarding his trial counsel's ineffectiveness. The petition was denied, and defendant again appealed, claiming ineffective assistance of counsel, that the trial court failed to give jury instructions regarding sentencing options, and the post-trial court improperly refused admission of expert testimony. The reviewing court affirmed, holding defendant's trial and appellate counsel rendered effective assistance. Where trial counsel failed to fully review discovery materials, this was harmless error where defendant was convicted of felony murder and disputing the evidence would not have changed the verdict. The sentencing jury instruction was not improperly denied where the law at the time of trial did not support the instruction. Where post-trial expert testimony was cumulative or irrelevant, it was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court affirmed the post-trial court's denial of defendant's post-trial petition for review and affirmed defendant's convictions for felony murder and sentence of death. Where trial counsel failed to fully review discovery materials, no ineffective assistance of counsel occurred where the materials were not exculpatory. The post-trial court properly denied expert testimony where it was cumulative and irrelevant.

 

21 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State Bd. of Tax Comm'rs v. Mixmill Mfg. Co.


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 49S00-9805-TA-308


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


702 N.E.2d 701; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 607



December 7, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended by Order of the Supreme Court February 5, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ind. LEXIS 61.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA TAX COURT. The Honorable Thomas G. Fisher, Judge. Cause No. 49T10-9701-TA-61.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee taxpayer filed a petition to challenge its property tax assessment. Neither the county board of review (county) or the appellant state board of tax commissioners (state board) responded. The taxpayer filed an original appeal in the Indiana Tax Court. The state board moved to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction. The tax court denied the state board's motion and granted leave to file an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: The state board argued that the tax court lacked jurisdiction because it had never received the taxpayer's petition and never issued a final determination. The supreme court held that two questions emerged from the arguments: (1) whether the legislature intended to permit taxpayers to appeal to the tax court if the county did not act before the next reassessment; and (2) whether an omission of clear guidelines for county action effectively denied a taxpayer's right to review of an administrative determination to the extent that the scheme raised constitutional issues. A duty to act on a petition was imposed by the state's tax laws and any suit to enforce it had to be brought in the tax court. The proper party, however, was not the state board but the county officials who were charged to be in default of that duty. The tax court did not have jurisdiction to hear a direct appeal by a taxpayer against the state board when the county failed to act on a petition within the statutory time frame. But, the tax court could entertain a mandamus action by the taxpayer to compel the county to act. There was no breach of due process under the statutory scheme.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded with direction to grant the state board 's motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction.

 

22 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State Bd. of Tax Comm'rs v. Town of St. John


49S10-9806-TA-340


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


702 N.E.2d 1034; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 603



December 4, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Town of St. John v. State Bd. of Tax Comm'rs, 729 N.E.2d 242, 2000 Ind. Tax LEXIS 20 (Ind. Tax Ct., 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM INDIANA TAX COURT. The Honorable Thomas G. Fisher, Judge. Cause No. 49T10-9309-TA-70.
Town of St. John v. State Bd. of Tax Comm'rs, 690 N.E.2d 370, 1997 Ind. Tax LEXIS 38 (Ind. Tax Ct., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part. Remanded to the Tax Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayers brought an action against respondent Indiana State Board of Tax Commissioners (the Board), alleging that Indiana's statutory system of property taxation was unconstitutional. The Indiana Tax Court consolidated the petitions and after a bench trial found in favor of the taxpayers. The Board appealed the decision. On remand, the Tax Court entered its final judgment of unconstitutionality. The Board again appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Board contended that the trial court erred in finding that Ind. Code § 6-1.1-31-6(c) and the cost schedules used to determine property value were unconstitutional. The Board further argued that it should not be required to consider evidence of wealth in assessing property value. The court found that 1) § 6-1.1-31-6(c) was not unconstitutional because it did not limit property valuation to "fair market value," but instead allowed tax assessors to consider other factors than those prescribed by the Board; 2) the Property Taxation Clause of the Indiana Constitution, Ind. Const. art. X, § 1, required a system of assessment that and taxation based on uniformity, equality, and just valuation based on wealth; 3) the Property Taxation Clause did not require absolute and precise exactitude as to the uniformity and equality of each individual assessment; 4) the Board's existing cost schedules lacked any meaningful reference to property wealth and resulted in significant deviations from substantial uniformity and equality, and thus was unconstitutional; and 5) the trial court erred in requiring the Board to consider "real world evidence "in its future property tax assessments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order in part and reversed in part. The court remanded the cause to the trial court with instructions to modify its order, which required the Board to consider "real world evidence" in its future property valuations, and for further proceedings.

 

23 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Board of Zoning Appeals v. Leisz


Supreme Court Cause No. 53S01-9806-CV-345


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


702 N.E.2d 1026; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 597



December 2, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MONROE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Marc R. Kellams, Judge. Cause No. 53C02-9506-CP-789. Court of Appeals Cause No. 53A01-9703-CV-82.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, a board of zoning appeals, sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Indiana). The court of appeals affirmed the trial court's judgment, which reversed respondent's denial of a request by petitioner landlords for an exemption from a city ordinance for petitioners' properties as pre-existing lawful nonconforming uses.


OVERVIEW: A city passed a zoning ordinance that limited the occupancy of dwellings in certain neighborhoods to three unrelated adults. The existing owners of two rental properties failed to register their nonconforming use. Respondent, a board of zoning appeals, denied a request by petitioners, the new landlords, for an exemption. The trial court reversed, and the court of appeals affirmed the trial court. The court reversed, holding that the ordinance was not an unconstitutional taking and that petitioners' due process rights were not violated. The ordinance, even though it provided for the forfeiture of unregistered nonconforming uses, was not a physical invasion and did not deny all economically productive use of the property. The registration requirement and the forfeiture sanction advanced a legitimate state interest; the city needed a mechanism to monitor nonconforming uses so that it could implement its development plan. Petitioners' property continued to have an economically viable use, even if that use was diminished. The court overruled the holding of Ailes v. Decatur County Area Planning Comm'n, 448 N.E.2d 1057 (Ind. 1983) that amortization provisions were per se unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court held that a city ordinance, which provided for the forfeiture of a prior nonconforming use if the property had not been duly registered, did not violate the takings clause or the due process clause of the Federal Constitution. The court thus reversed the court of appeals' judgment. Petitioner landlords were properly denied an exemption from the ordinance because their predecessors had not registered the nonconforming use.

 

24 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Ragucci v. Metropolitan Dev. Comm'n


Supreme Court Cause No. 49S02-9805-CV-299


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


702 N.E.2d 677; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 598



December 2, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable John L. Price, Judge. Cause No. 49D11-9510-CP-1772. Court of Appeals Cause No. 49A02-9607-CV-463.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of summary judgment affirmed in part. Case is remanded to the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff commission brought an action against defendant owner alleging that his building was in violation of the Marion County, Ind., Dwelling Districts Zoning Ordinance (1966). Both parties moved for summary judgment. The Marion Superior Court, Indiana, held there was a violation of the ordinance and granted the commission's motion. A divided court of appeals reversed. The supreme court granted a transfer of the case.


OVERVIEW: A transfer was granted to consider the legal standards for evaluating changes in a legally established nonconforming use under a zoning ordinance. The supreme court held that the interpretation of ordinances that restricted the expansion of nonconforming uses turned in the first instance on the specific language of the relevant ordinance, giving its words their plain, ordinary, and usual meaning. Each municipality was, subject to constitutional limitations, free to enact an ordinance that limited the expansion of nonconforming uses in the manner and to the degree that it deemed appropriate. Here, the ordinance clearly demonstrated the intent of the county council to constrain the expansion of nonconforming uses. Under the federal constitution, the ordinance was not an unconstitutional taking as applied to the building. The superior court properly granted summary judgment in favor of the commission. Injunctive relief was appropriate in this case; however, the superior court was required to determine whether it was necessary to order that the building be remodeled, rather than simply enjoining the building's use.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was affirmed in part. The case was remanded for reconsideration of the proper scope for relief.

 

25 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Rogers v. State


Supreme Court No. 45S00-9608-CR-568


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


698 N.E.2d 1172; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 252



September 8, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James L. Clement, Judge. Cause No. 45G04-9502-CF-00056.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) which convicted him of murder, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-1-1; felony murder, in violation of § 35-42-1-1; and confinement, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-3-3. Defendant also appealed his sentence of life imprisonment without parole for the murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant requested the court to determine whether the clear and convincing standard of proof required by Ind. Code § 35-36-9-4 for a showing of mental retardation violated due process, and whether the trial court erred in finding defendant not to be retarded within the meaning of Ind. Code § 35-36-9-2. The court held that the standard of proof set forth in Ind. Code § 35-36-9-4, although arguably permitting the same type of erroneous determination of absence of mental retardation, did not offend a fundamental principle such as the right of a defendant not to stand trial while incompetent. Given that the clear and convincing standard of proof of Ind. Code § 35-36-9-4 did not affect the fundamental procedural fairness of a defendant's trial, and that the U.S. and Indiana Constitutions did not prohibit the execution of a mentally retarded defendant, the court could not conclude that defendant's due process rights were violated. Upon review of the record, the court could not conclude that the trial court abused its discretion in finding defendant not to be mentally retarded within the meaning of the statute, and the court would not disturb the trial court's finding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentence of life imprisonment without parole.

Willsey v. State


Supreme Court Cause No. 83S00-9702-CR-113


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


698 N.E.2d 784; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 248



September 1, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denid January 19, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 649.
Rehearing denied by Willsey v. State, 1998 Ind. LEXIS 613 (Ind., Dec. 2, 1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at Willsey v. State, 908 N.E.2d 710, 2009 Ind. App. LEXIS 1407 (Ind. Ct. App., 2009)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Willsey v. McCauley, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 48757 (S.D. Ind., May 5, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE VERMILLION CIRCUIT COURT. Cause No. 83C01-9510-CF-48. The Honorable Bruce V. Stengel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of murder and the Vermillion Circuit Court (Indiana) sentenced her to 60 years imprisonment, which included a 20-year enhancement. Defendant appealed her conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended on appeal that her statements to police during her custodial interrogation should have been suppressed and that the State made an impermissible use of her invocation of her Miranda rights. She also contended that the victim's bank records were inadmissible, her counsel rendered ineffective assistance, and her sentence was manifestly unreasonable. The court held that, although there were no findings on the record as to the denial of defendant's motion to suppress her statements, the trial court clearly found that defendant's testimony that she had requested counsel was not credible. Defendant's invocation of her right to counsel after her statement was recorded was not used by the State to create an inference of guilt. The State used the remarks as an implication of sinister knowledge. The bank records were properly offered and admitted as evidence of defendant's relationship with the victim. The defense counsel's representation was not ineffective. Finally, there was no showing of a manifest abuse of discretion by the trial court in its sentencing enhancement, which was based the trial court's determination of aggravating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Harrison v. State


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 18S00-9712-CR-687


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


699 N.E.2d 645; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 231



August 24, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE DELAWARE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Robert Barnet, Judge. Cause No. 18D01-9612-CF-70.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's conviction and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence from the Delaware Superior Court (Indiana) for murder after he shot the victim several times.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was 17 years old, gave money to the victim so that the victim could purchase a pack of cigarettes for defendant. Defendant and the victim later met in a parking lot, and defendant asked the victim to return the change. The victim replied that he did not have the money. The victim then hit defendant. Defendant pulled out a pistol and shot the victim. Defendant chased the victim while shooting him. The victim fell to the ground, and defendant shot him again. The victim was unarmed and died of five gunshot wounds. Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to 60 years. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting photographs of the victim taken after the murder. The court reasoned that the pictures were highly probative of defendant's claim that he acted in self-defense. The court also found no error in admitting a witness's pre-trial statement to police that she saw defendant running from the scene to impeach her testimony at defendant's trial. The court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to rebut defendant's self-defense claim and that defendant's sentence was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for murder.

Klein v. State


Cause No.49S00-9708-CR-452


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


698 N.E.2d 296; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 233



August 24, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Robert York, Special Judge. Cause No. 49G02-9504-CF-056069.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted and sentenced him for murder under Ind. Code Ann. § 35-42-1-1 (1998), criminal gang activity under Ind. Code Ann. § 35-45-9-3 (1998), and possession of a sawed-off shotgun under Ind. Code Ann. § 35-47-5-4.1 (1998).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the criminal gang activity statute, Ind. Code Ann § 35-45-9-3 (1998), was unconstitutionally vague under the United States Constitution and the Indiana Constitution. The court held, however, that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because the law put individuals on active notice of what the legislature considered to be a criminal gang, and that participation in those groups was prohibited. Additionally, the statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad and it did not violate defendant's freedom of association guaranteed under Ind. Const. art. I, § 9, 31, and U.S. Const. arts. I, XIV. The court stated that the statute did not prohibit the mere association of five or more persons, did not criminalize the mere status of gang membership, and only applied to criminal associations that were not protected by U.S. Const. amend. I. Finally, the court held that the trial court considered both aggravating and mitigating factors and imposed a reasonable and appropriate sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

Brown v. State


Supreme Court No. 45S00-9212-PD-939


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


698 N.E.2d 1132; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 107



July 17, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied April 5, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2437.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Richard J. Conroy, Judge. Cause No. 1CR-203-1184-842.



DISPOSITION: Denial of post-conviction relief affirmed with respect to Debra Denise Brown's convictions for Murder and Attempted Murder and sentence of death.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which denied post-conviction relief to her after her convictions for murder and attempted murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and attempted murder and sentenced to death. Defendant sought post-conviction relief asserting that she was denied both exculpatory materials known to the State and effective assistance of counsel at trial and on appeal. The superior court denied relief. Upon review, the court noted that the State had an affirmative duty to disclose evidence favorable to defendant. However, the post-conviction relief process was not to be used for investigating possible claims but as a means to vindicate actual claims. The court found that the materials relating to defendant's IQ could not be reasonably taken to put the whole case in such a different light as to undermine confidence in her conviction. The court found that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel where defendant failed to show deficient performance and resulting prejudice from the actions of her counsel. The court reiterated the fact that counsel was expected to use professional judgment, and the court would not conclude that a fair trial was denied unless the conviction or sentence resulted from a breakdown of the adversarial process that rendered the result unreliable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying defendant post-conviction relief.

 

30 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. State


Cause No. 10S00-9606-CR-432


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


697 N.E.2d 466; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 108



July 17, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Wilson v. State, 1999 Ind. LEXIS 843 (Ind., Sept. 21, 1999)
Post-conviction relief denied at Wilson v. State, 2010 Ind. App. LEXIS 1136 (Ind. Ct. App., June 24, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE CLARK CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Daniel F. Donahue, Judge. Cause No. 10C01-9406-CF-86.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Clark Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him of one count of murder under Ind. Code § 35-42-1-1, and two counts of attempted murder under Ind. Code §§ 35-42-1-1 and 35-41-5-1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-1-1 and attempted murder in violation of Ind. Code §§ 35-42-1-1 and 35-41-5-1. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that defendant's retrial following a mistrial did not violate his right to protection against double jeopardy. The court determined that there was no evidence that the prosecutor intended to cause a mistrial. The court noted that although the prosecutor asked the officer open-ended questions about their conversations with defendant, he did not appear to solicit their testimony about defendant's request for an attorney. The court further found that there was no evidence of sudden heat that would have entitled defendant to an instruction on the lesser-included offense of voluntary manslaughter. The court also ruled that defendant's assertion of the insanity defense did not create a serious evidentiary dispute about defendant's level of mens rea. The court reasoned that because a successful insanity defense would have acquitted defendant of any offense he may have committed, the defense did not entitle defendant to an instruction on the lesser-included offense of reckless homicide.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and held that defendant's retrial did not violate the proscription against double jeopardy because the record supported the conclusion that the prosecutor did not intend to cause a mistrial. The court also determined that defendant was not entitled to any instructions on lesser-included offenses because there was no serious evidentiary dispute as to which offenses defendant had committed.

 

31 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Minnick v. State


47S00-9008-PD-497


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


698 N.E.2d 745; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 102



July 13, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Order on Denial of Rehearing in Capital Case February 5, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ind. LEXIS 60. Certiorari Denied November 15, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7562.
Rehearing denied by Minnick v. State, 705 N.E.2d 179, 1999 Ind. LEXIS 60 (Ind., 1999)
Rehearing denied by, 02/05/1999
Writ of certiorari denied Minnick v. Indiana, 528 U.S. 1006, 120 S. Ct. 501, 145 L. Ed. 2d 387, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7562 (1999)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAWRENCE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Richard D. McIntyre, Sr., Judge. Cause No. 47C01-8507-CF-00039.
Minnick v. State, 544 N.E.2d 471, 1989 Ind. LEXIS 299 (Ind., 1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Lawrence Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of murder, robbery, and rape. The trial judge ordered the death penalty imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed error related to (1) prosecutorial misconduct, (2) ineffective assistance of counsel, and (3) various challenges to the facial validity of the death penalty statute. The court held that a claim of denial of counsel required proof not only of attorney deficiency, but also of fundamentally unfair and unreliable result. Because the alleged prosecutorial misconduct in failing to disclose the serology evidence did not present significant evidence in favor of defendant, the result was not unfair and unreliable. Furthermore, the issue of ineffective assistance of counsel was forfeited by the failure to raise it on direct appeal, and the court found no fundamental error. Additionally, it was apparent that the legislature's choice to allow death penalty defendants to present every conceivable mitigator required that the sentencer not be precluded from considering as a mitigating factor, any aspect of a defendant's character or record. Therefore, the statutory "catch-all" mitigator did not violate constitutional requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the post-conviction court.

 

32 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Seay v. State


Supreme Court No. 82S01-9701-PC-26


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


698 N.E.2d 732; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 96



July 8, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Richard L. Young, Judge. Cause No. 82C01-9009-MI-2477. Court of Appeals No. 82A01-9604-PC-139.



DISPOSITION: Denial of post-conviction relief affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Indiana Court of Appeals, which affirmed the judgment of the post-conviction court denying relief from the determination that defendant was a habitual criminal.


OVERVIEW: In a bifurcated proceeding, defendant was convicted of two counts of dealing in drugs and then found to be a habitual offender under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-8 (Supp. 1986). During the habitual offender phase, the trial court instructed the jury that it was the judge only of the facts, and that it was restricted to determining the facts only and not the law. Defendant was found guilty of being a habitual offender, causing his sentence to be enhanced by 30 years. The post-conviction court denied relief and the Indiana Court of Appeals affirmed. On transfer of the appeal to the Supreme Court of Indiana, the court held that Ind. Const. art. I, § 19, which provides that the jury had the right to determine the law and the facts, was applicable to habitual offender proceedings. Thus, the jury was entitled to make a determination of habitual offender status as a matter of law independent of its factual determinations regarding prior unrelated felonies. However, because the error in the instruction of the jury was not fundamental, the court affirmed the denial of post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of post-conviction relief, even though the trial court's instruction to the jury on the law was error.

 

33 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Barker v. State


Supreme Court Cause No. 49S00-9411-DP-1107


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


695 N.E.2d 925; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 76



June 12, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Barker v. State, 1998 Ind. LEXIS 278 (Ind., Aug. 31, 1998)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by State v. Barker, 768 N.E.2d 425, 2002 Ind. LEXIS 341 (Ind., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable John R. Barney, Jr., Judge. Cause No. 49G03-9308-CF-95544.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed and remanded for a new sentencing phase.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of two counts of murder, and one count each of kidnapping, confinement, burglary, and carrying a handgun without a license. The trial court also imposed the death penalty for the murders.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed his ex-girlfriend's grandparents and then kidnapped his ex-girlfriend, their child, and his wife and forced them to accompany him on his getaway. The trial court imposed the death penalty after defendant was convicted of murder and other charges. The court affirmed the convictions, but reversed the sentence, finding that the admission of prior bad acts under Ind. R. Evid. 404(b) was harmless error where there was no substantial likelihood that the erroneously admitted evidence contributed to the jury's conclusion that defendant killed the grandparents or that the jury would have found that defendant was guilty of reckless homicide and not murder. The trial court did not err in refusing to give a voluntary manslaughter instruction, as there was no evidence of provocation. Defendant waived his objection to jury voir dire questions by failing to object, and the prosecutor's discretion to seek the death penalty without a "probable cause" requirement or an adversarial hearing was constitutional. However, the court held that the trial court erred by failing to instruct the jury that defendant could be sentenced to life without parole for the murders.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, but remanded for a new sentencing phase.

 

34 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Indiana Wholesale Wine & Liquor Co. v. State ex rel. Indiana Alcoholic Bev. Comm'n


Supreme Court No. 49S02-9609-CV-606


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


695 N.E.2d 99; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 65



May 28, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended June 11, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James S. Kirsch and The Honorable David L. Rimstidt, Judges. Cause No. 49D05-9108-CP-871. Court of Appeals No. 49A02-9406-CV-384.



DISPOSITION: (1) adopt and incorporate by reference that portion of the Court of Appeals' opinion dealing with the issue of standing as discussed in part I, supra; (2) vacate the remainder of the opinion of the Court of Appeals; and (3) defer to the Commission's prior reasonable interpretation of the Residency Statute.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, Alcoholic Beverage Commission and wholesalers, sought review of a decision of the Indiana Court of Appeals, entered in favor of appellant wholesaler, which reversed the decision of the trial court in a declaratory judgment action involving the interpretation of the residency statute for wine and liquor wholesalers, Ind. Code § 7.1-3-21-5 (1997).


OVERVIEW: After issuing a wine and liquor wholesale license to appellee wholesaler, appellant Alcohol Beverage Commission filed a declaratory judgment action against appellee and appellant wholesalers seeking judicial guidance on the meaning and application of a residency statute, Ind. Code § 7.1-3-21-5 (1997), with respect to appellee. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and vacated in part the appellate court decision entered in favor of appellee. The court held that appellant commission had standing to bring the action pursuant to Ind. Code § 7.1-2-8-3 (1993). Further, the corporate structure of appellee comported with the literal language of the § 7.1-3-21-5 because Indiana residents owned 60 percent of the common shares of appellee. The court found that there was no control requirement in § 7.1-3-21-5 and that appellant commission's interpretation of § 7.1-3-21-5 was reasonable. However, the appellate court erred when it addressed the constitutionality of § 7.1-3-21-5 because the case could be resolved on nonconstitutional grounds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that portion of the appellate court's opinion dealing with the issue of standing. The court vacated the remainder of the appellate court's opinion and deferred to appellant Alcohol Beverage Commission's prior interpretation of the residency statute because that interpretation was reasonable and appellee wholesaler's corporate structure comported with the requirements of the residency statute.

 

35 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Wisehart v. State


Supreme Court No. 48S00-9005-PD-378


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


693 N.E.2d 23; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 26



March 19, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied March 29, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 2251.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MADISON SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Thomas G. Wright, Special Judge. Cause No. 3SCR-82-204.



DISPOSITION: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE DENIAL OF POST-CONVICTION RELIEF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of an order of the Madison Superior Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief with respect to his convictions for murder, robbery, burglary, and theft and his sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted on the theory that he acted alone. The prisoner alleged that new evidence showed he had accomplices. The court held that the prisoner did not satisfy three of the nine requirements for relief for newly-discovered evidence. The prisoner did not establish that (1) the evidence was not available at trial, (2) due diligence was used to discover the evidence before trial, and (3) the evidence would produce a different result on re-trial. The court applied a two-part test to the prisoner's ineffective assistance claims of his trial and appellate counsel. The prisoner's assistance at all phases of his trial, sentencing, and direct appeal was not ineffective because the evidence did not show both deficient performance and resulting substantial prejudice to the prisoner. Trial counsel effectively employed the prisoner's mental condition to support his innocence defense. The jury was properly instructed regarding mitigating and aggravating circumstances regarding the death sentence. The state did not violate its disclosure obligations because the evidence did not clearly establish the existence of an agreement with a witness to dismiss charges for his testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's denial of the prisoner's petition for post-conviction relief.

Ajabu v. State


Cause No. 71S00-9512-CR-1377


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


693 N.E.2d 921; 1998 Ind. LEXIS 19



March 6, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Ajabu v. State, 722 N.E.2d 339, 2000 Ind. LEXIS 27 (Ind., Jan. 21, 2000)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Ajabu v. State, 873 N.E.2d 207, 2007 Ind. App. LEXIS 2173 (Ind. Ct. App., Sept. 11, 2007)
Related proceeding at Ajabu v. Hamilton Cnty. Prosecutor's Office, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 15084 (S.D. Ind., Feb. 2, 2017)
Related proceeding at Ajabu v. Hamilton Cnty. Prosecutor's Office, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 76401 (S.D. Ind., May 19, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Sanford M. Brook, Judge. Cause No. 71D02-9409-CF-963.



DISPOSITION: Kofi Modibo Ajabu's convictions for three counts of murder, three counts of criminal confinement, three counts of robbery, and one count of burglary, affirmed. Remanded for further proceedings in trial court consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of three counts of murder, three counts of criminal confinement, three counts of robbery, and one court of burglary. The St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana) sentenced him to life in prison without parole for each murder conviction and to a term of years for the other convictions. Defendant appealed his convictions, alleging that his right against self-incrimination pursuant to Ind. Const. art. I, § 14 was violated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted after three people were found dead at a house that had been ransacked. Defendant was arrested and advised of his Miranda rights. He confessed to the police without asserting his right to counsel, and he was not aware that an attorney retained by his father had requested that the police not question defendant. Defendant appealed his convictions. The court affirmed, holding that the admission of his voluntary confession did not violate his right to be free from self-incrimination under Ind. Const. art. 1, § 14, and that the police conduct in not honoring the attorney's unsolicited request did not violate his due process rights under the Fourteenth Amendment. However, the court held that while the trial court's finding of major participation in the crime satisfied the death penalty statute, particularly Ind. Code. § 35-50-2-9(b)(1) (1993), the trial court failed to enter specific findings that defendant committed an intentional killing as required by § 35-50-2-9(b)(1). Thus, the court remanded the case for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions but remanded for resentencing.

Wrinkles v. State


Supreme Court No. 82S00-9408-DP-741


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


690 N.E.2d 1156; 1997 Ind. LEXIS 240



December 31, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Rehearing Denied March 23, 1998.
Writ of certiorari denied Wrinkles v. Indiana, 525 U.S. 861, 119 S. Ct. 148, 142 L. Ed. 2d 121, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 5495 (1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at Wrinkles v. State, 749 N.E.2d 1179, 2001 Ind. LEXIS 596 (Ind., 2001)
Post-conviction relief denied at Wrinkles v. State, 776 N.E.2d 905, 2002 Ind. LEXIS 802 (Ind., 2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Wrinkles v. State, 2009 Ind. LEXIS 1520 (Ind., Nov. 3, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Richard L. Young, Judge. Cause No. 82C01-9407-CF-447.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana) convicted defendant of three counts of murder and sentenced him to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's wife went to live with her brother and his wife. Defendant broke into the house and killed his wife, her brother, and the brother's wife. The trial court convicted defendant of three counts of murder and sentenced him to death. On appeal, the court affirmed. Testimony regarding a telephone call from defendant's wife was improperly admitted, but the error was harmless because the testimony was merely cumulative. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting ballistics or serological evidence. The trial court did not err in refusing defendant's tendered jury instructions on accident or mistake of fact. The jury was not in fact misled by the jury instruction on reckless homicide. Although the instruction on prior inconsistent statements incorrectly stated the law, the error was harmless. The death penalty statute, Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9, was constitutional. It was constitutional to impose the death sentence for "knowing," as well as "intentional," murder. The trial court failed to instruct the jury on all the statutory penalties for murder, but the omission was not fundamental error. The aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of three counts of murder and sentencing him to death.

Stevens v. State


CAUSE NO. 79S00-9507-DP-828, )
