39 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Ben-Yisrayl v. State


64S00-9103-DP-00229


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


690 N.E.2d 1141; 1997 Ind. LEXIS 248



December 31, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE PORTER SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Thomas W. Webber, Judge. Cause No. 64D02-9102-CF-022.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of murder and felony convictions under Ind. Code § 35-42-1-1 (1993) and Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9(b)(8) (1993) in the Porter Superior Court (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his murder and felony murder convictions and imposition of the death penalty. The court affirmed the convictions, first rejecting the argument that appellant was entitled to severance of the offenses of the shotgun murder and robbery of a male victim, and the shotgun murder and robbery of a female victim two days later. The court found the lower court did not abuse its discretion in denying the severance motion under the statutory provisions at issue, Ind. Code §§ 35-34-1-9(a), -11(a) (1993), because the offenses were not joined solely based on their similarity. As a result, appellant was not entitled to severance as a matter of right. The court observed joinder was justified because the state could establish a modus operandi for the crimes which both involved shooting clerks at their place of business between the hours of six and eight at night by an assailant who drove a white Nissan Sentra. The court next rejected the argument that other crimes evidence was improperly admitted. The court explained that, assuming admission was error, it was nevertheless harmless due to the other overwhelming evidence against appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for murder and felony murder and the imposition of the death penalty because discretion was not abused in the denial of a severance motion. The offenses were not joined solely on the basis of similarity; prosecutorial comments were not improper; jury instructions were adequate; and the death penalty was properly imposed with sufficient aggravating circumstances.

Hough v. State


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 02S00-9305-PD-497


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


690 N.E.2d 267; 1997 Ind. LEXIS 246



December 30, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Rehearing Denied April 30, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Edward Meyer, Special Judge. Cause No. CR-86-185.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's conviction on two counts of murder and his sentence to death was previously affirmed on direct appeal. Defendant challenged a decision from the Allen County Superior Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief and granted respondent state's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The court held that defendant did not receive ineffective assistance of trial and appellate counsel; the post-conviction court did not err in failing to grant an evidentiary hearing on the state's motion for summary judgment; the trial court did not fail to consider relevant mitigating evidence; defendant was not deprived of a fair trial due to allegedly erroneous jury instructions; the alleged errors at trial did not act cumulatively to deny defendant a fair trial; and Indiana's death penalty statute was not unconstitutional. The court rejected numerous theories presented by defendant challenging the constitutionality of the statute. As to any ineffective assistance of counsel, defendant failed, in part, to show that that his counsel acted below an objective standard of reasonableness, and that the substandard performance was so prejudicial as to deny him a fair trial. Further, summary judgment was proper where the state's agreement removed disputed facts, and the only inquiry remaining was one of law. Errors that were alleged by defendant, which were not properly briefed and argued, were waived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the post-conviction court's grant of summary judgment to the state and the denial of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.

Roche v. State


Supreme Court No. 45S00-9305-PD-588


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


690 N.E.2d 1115; 1997 Ind. LEXIS 238



December 30, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Rehearing Denied May 27, 1998.
Rehearing denied by, 05/27/1998
Writ of habeas corpus granted Roche v. Anderson, 132 F. Supp. 2d 688, 2001 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 1657 (N.D. Ind., 2001)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Richard Conroy, Judge. Cause No. 45G04-9005-CF-00095.
Roche v. State, 596 N.E.2d 896, 1992 Ind. LEXIS 191 (Ind., 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief, after being found guilty of murder, claiming that he was denied the effective assistance of trial counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two participants lured victims into his home for a phony drug deal, where the victims were killed. Defendant was tried and found guilty of murder, and sentenced to death. Defendant challenged his conviction, and it was upheld on appeal. Defendant then filed a petition for post-conviction relief (PCR). The PCR trial court denied defendant's petition, and defendant again appealed the ruling, claiming ineffective assistance of counsel. The court held that under the Strickland standard, defendant was required to show that, in light of all the circumstances, the identified acts or omissions of counsel were outside the wide range of professionally competent assistance, and that he suffered prejudice as a result of the deficient performance. Defendant argued that his counsel did not introduce mitigating evidence during the penalty phase of the trial and put him on the stand. The court stated that defendant did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel, because counsel's actions were the result of trial strategy, and in any case, the result of the jury would have been the same. The court affirmed the convictions and upheld the denial of the PCR petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, and held that defendant was properly denied post-conviction relief by the trial court because he did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel, because his counsel's actions were based upon permissible trial strategy, and because defendant did not suffer prejudice or show that the result of the jury would have been different.

Indiana High Sch. Ath. Ass'n v. Reyes


Supreme Court No. 79S02-9605-CV-361


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


694 N.E.2d 249; 1997 Ind. LEXIS 237



December 19, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Donald C. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 79D01-9502-CP-46. Court of Appeals No. 79A02-9504-CV-175.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, high school and principal, sought review of a judgment from the Indiana Court of Appeals, which upheld the validity of the Restitution Rule of defendant Indiana High School Athletic Association (IHSAA). Plaintiffs asked the court to reinstate the trial court's prohibition against the IHSAA enforcing its Restitution Rule against plaintiff high school.


OVERVIEW: The Indiana High School Athletic Association (IHSAA) notified plaintiff high school that a student was not eligible to participate in interscholastic athletics due to the IHSAA's eight semester rule. After the student's request for a hardship exception was denied by the IHSAA, the trial court issued an injunction preventing the IHSAA from enforcing the rule against the student and prohibiting the IHSAA from sanctioning plaintiff for compliance with the injunction. The court of appeals reversed and plaintiff appealed only from the holding that the IHSAA's Restitution Rule was valid. The Restitution Rule provided that the IHSAA could sanction member schools by requiring them to forfeit awards and return funding in the event an ineligible student athlete participated in violation of IHSAA rules, but in accordance with a court order that was later stayed or reversed. On appeal the court affirmed and held that absent fraud, other illegality, or abuse of civil or property rights, it would not interfere in plaintiff's dispute with a voluntary association of which it was a member. Where the student did not challenge the IHSAA decision, the arbitrary and capricious standard did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that the Restitution Rule of the Indiana High School Athletic Association (IHSAA) was valid. Because plaintiff high school's challenge to the Restitution Rule did not allege fraud, other illegality, or abuse of civil or property rights, the court declined to interfere in plaintiffs' dispute with a voluntary association of which it was a member.

Bieghler v. State

SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA

Writ of habeas corpus denied Bieghler v. McBride, 389 F.3d 701, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 24072 (7th Cir. Ind., 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Bieghler v. State, 839 N.E.2d 691, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 1156 (Ind., 2005)
Stay granted by Bieghler v. Donahue, 2006 U.S. App. LEXIS 2451 (7th Cir. Ind., Jan. 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM HOWARD SUPERIOR COURT I. The Honorable Bruce C. Embrey, Special Judge. Cause No. 2436.
Bieghler v. State, 481 N.E.2d 78, 1985 Ind. LEXIS 920 (Ind., 1985)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the denial of post-conviction relief concerning his conviction and death sentence by the Howard Superior Court (Indiana), which upheld his conviction and death sentence for murder after defendant's unsuccessful direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: After defendant unsuccessfully appealed his conviction for murder and resultant death sentence, he unsuccessfully petitioned for post-conviction relief. On appeal, the court affirmed and found no reversible error in the post-conviction court proceedings. The court held defendant's claims regarding ineffective assistance of counsel at the appellate and trial levels failed because: (1) defendant was unable to show a reasonable probability that, but for counsel's purportedly unprofessional presentation, the outcome of his appeal would have been different; (2) the appellate court's ruling in defendant's direct appeal was res judicata to his claim that trial counsel was ineffective; (3) appellate counsel was not required to challenge trial counsel's failure to ask the court for a cautionary instruction regarding an accomplice's testimony because under Indiana common law, this instruction was improper; (4) the failure to challenge jury instructions was not prejudicial because the instructions given were not error; (5) there was no error in jury selection; (6) he could not assert cumulative error during the penalty phase because those claims should have been raised on his direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence of death because thorough post-conviction review of the proceedings leading to defendant's conviction and sentence revealed no constitutional error by the trial court or in the performance of counsel either at trial or in his direct appeal. In addition, the court found no reversible error in the proceedings of the post-conviction court.

Matheney v. State


CAUSE NO. 45S00-9207-PD-584


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


688 N.E.2d 883; 1997 Ind. LEXIS 198



November 24, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Rehearing Denied March 31, 1998.
Certiorari Denied February 22, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 1160.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Richard J. Conroy, Judge. Cause No. 45G02-9001-CF-22.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murdering his former wife. Defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief challenging his conviction and death sentence. The trial court denied his petition. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of murdering his ex-wife. Following the jury's recommendation, the court sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed his conviction and death sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed both. The court noted that in post-conviction proceeding the defendant had to show that the evidence, when taken as a whole, was unerringly and unmistakably to a conclusion opposite to that reached by the trial court. The court found that evidence that defendant was previously competent to stand trial was properly available to the post-conviction court about defendant's mental state. The court found that the denial of defendant's motion to order the jury commissioner to disclose the names of the jurors and alternates at trial was properly denied. The court held the magistrate act was constitutional as it operated in the case. The court found no bias or prejudice against the defendant by the magistrate. The court held that defendant was not denied the effective assistance of counsel. The court reweighed the statutory aggravators and mitigators, also without consideration of the contents of the psychological questionnaire, and found that the death penalty was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor challenged a judgment of the Hendricks Superior Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee Marion County Department of Public Welfare in a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action brought by the minor.


OVERVIEW: A minor brought a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against the Marion County Department of Public Welfare. The Department filed a motion for summary judgment, which the trial court granted, and the minor sought review. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the Department.

 

48 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Moss-Dwyer


Cause No. 45S00-9610-CR-657


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


686 N.E.2d 109; 1997 Ind. LEXIS 171



October 23, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] INTERLOCUTORY APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Richard J. Conroy, Judge. Cause No. 45G03-9308-CF-218.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state filed an interlocutory appeal from the decision of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which held that Ind. Code § 35-47-2-23, classifying the crime of giving false information in an application for a handgun license as a class C felony, was facially unconstitutional as a violation of the proportionality requirement of Ind. Const. art. I, § 16.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statute on the grounds that the penalty for giving a false address in an application for a handgun permit was the same as the penalty for actually carrying a handgun without a license. The trial court held that the statute was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed. The court noted that the separation of powers doctrine required it to take a highly restrained approach when reviewing a legislative prescription of punishment and that the statute began with a presumption of constitutional validity. In determining whether the penalty was disproportionate to the offense, the court compared it to the penalties for other crimes involving misinforming or deceiving public officials and found that it was consistent with the penalties in those cases. The court also held that the legislature may have regarded this as leading to the commission of two wrongs in that the offender first will have deceived a public official and second will carry a handgun without a valid permit. The court concluded that the trial court had impermissibly infringed upon the legislative prerogative when it held the statute unconstitutional on its face.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and held that Ind. Code § 35-47-2-23 did not violate the proportionality requirement contained in Ind. Const., art. I, § 16.

Allen v. State

SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


686 N.E.2d 760; 1997 Ind. LEXIS 147

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable John R. Barney, Jr., Judge. Cause No. CR87-194C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a decision of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted appellant of robbery under Ind. Code § 35-42-5-1, murder under Ind. Code § 35-42-1-1(1), and felony murder under Ind. Code § 35-42-1-1(2), and sentenced appellant to death. Appellant alleged 17 errors on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant for robbery under Ind. Code § 35-42-5-1, murder under Ind. Code § 35-42-1-1(1), and felony murder under Ind. Appellant was not denied his right to effective assistance of counsel during the guilt phase of his trial. Further, the court held that there was little evidence that appellant was mentally retarded, and none that showed him to be incapable of appreciating the criminality of his conduct or to conform it to the law. The court held that the aggravating circumstance outweighed the mitigating circumstance and that the penalty was appropriate to the offense and the offender.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which convicted appellant of robbery, murder, and felony murder, and sentenced appellant to death.

Polk v. State


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 79S00-9612-CR-748


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


683 N.E.2d 567; 1997 Ind. LEXIS 117



July 23, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Polk v. State, 2005 Ind. App. LEXIS 209 (Ind. Ct. App., Feb. 11, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable George J. Heid, Judge. Cause No. 79D02-9507-CF-66.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Tippecanoe Superior Court (Indiana) for possession of at least three grams of cocaine within 1000 feet of school property under Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6 (Supp. 1995), and for possession of a controlled substance within 1000 feet of school property under Ind. Code § 35-48-4-7 (Supp. 1995).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in a vehicle stopped by police for a traffic violation. The stop occurred within 1000 feet of a school. Defendant, after a consent search, was found in possession of drugs. Defendant also hid drugs in the back seat of a police car. Defendant appealed his conviction at trial, contending that the school-zone enhancement of his sentence violated his rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction because the school-zone enhancement was rationally related to the state's legitimate objective of preventing drug transactions from taking place around children. The court held that the language of the school-zone enhancement had provided defendant with clear and fair notice of what type of conduct was prohibited. The court found that contrary to defendant's arguments, the enhancement was triggered by the act of entering the school zone and that defendant's lack of knowledge as to the location of the school zone was irrelevant, because the school-zone element was a strict-liability enhancement. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, because the school-zone enhancement applied to defendant's conviction as a matter of statutory construction and the enhancement did not violate defendant's due process of law or equal protection rights under the Fourteenth Amendment.

In re Madison County Probation Officers' Salaries


Cause No. 48S00-9704-MF-239,


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


682 N.E.2d 498; 1997 Ind. LEXIS 88



June 26, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] The Honorable Barbara Arnold Harcourt, Special Judge. Cause No. 48D03-9612-MI-006.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the Madison County Unified Courts (Indiana) and the Madison Circuit Court (Indiana) (Court System), issued an order of mandate of funds, pursuant to Ind. R. Trial P. 60.5(B), to require respondent, Madison County Council (Indiana), to increase the salaries of Madison County probation officers. A specially assigned judge entered a decree sustaining the order of mandate. The proceedings were certified to the court.


OVERVIEW: Ind. Code § 11-13-1-8(b) authorized the Board of Directors of the Judicial Conference of Indiana to prescribe minimum salary standards for probation officers. Ind. Code § 11-13-1-1(c) authorized Indiana courts to fix the salaries of their probation officers. On appeal from the special judge's decree that confirmed petitioners' order of mandate, the County Council contended, among other things, that the Indiana legislature violated the principle of separation of powers, which was found in Ind. Const. art. III, § 1, when it authorized the Board to establish minimum salary standards for probation officers. The court found no constitutional infirmity in the legislature's action. Because courts were constitutionally obligated to be open and because the operation of a probation office was a court-related function, the Indiana courts had the corresponding constitutional power to pay probation officers at a level sufficient to attract and maintain qualified personnel. The process by which probation officers' salaries were determined illustrated that the coordinate branches of government were working together; specifically, county officials attended hearings on the proposed salary increase.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the special judge's decree.

 

52 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Calumet Nat'l Bank v. AT&T


Supreme Court No. 64S03-9706-CV-369


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


682 N.E.2d 785; 1997 Ind. LEXIS 84



June 19, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PORTER COUNTY. The Honorable Roger V. Bradford, Judge. Cause No. 64D01-9003-CP-593. Court of Appeals No. 64A03-9411-CV-409.



DISPOSITION: Transfer granted. Court of Appeals opinion vacated pursuant to Ind.Appellate Rule 11(b)(3). The trial court is ordered to grant summary judgment in favor of Trust on the issue of trespass, and remand for consideration of damages, if any.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trust appealed the decision of the Court of Appeals (Indiana), which affirmed the trial court's determination that defendant phone company was not guilty of trespass and granted summary judgment to defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff trust brought a trespass action against defendant phone company when it hired one of its subsidiaries to install and operate fiber optics along a railroad right-of-way. Both parties claimed that railroad transferred to them certain interests in the right of way. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of defendant, and the appellate court affirmed. The court reversed and remanded and ordered the trial court to grant summary judgment in favor of plaintiff and issue damages. The court concluded that under Ind. Code §8-4-35-5 where there was no language in any of the relevant deeds describing real property that included the right-of-way, the title of the owners of land abutting railroad rights-of-way ran to the center of the right-of-way. The court found that there was no language in any of the relevant deeds from which ownership of the right-of-way easement could have been inferred. The court concluded that prior to abandonment by railroad, the title of plaintiff's predecessors-in-interest ran to the center of the right-of-way, subject to the burden of the railroad's easement, and upon abandonment, that title was no longer subject to the burden of the easement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's affirmation of the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant phone company in plaintiff trustee's action against it for trespass because there was no language in any of the relevant deeds from which ownership of the right-of-way easement could have been inferred, and upon abandonment by railroad, the transforor, the easement was extinguished.

Williams v. State


No. 49S02-9706-CR-355


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


681 N.E.2d 195; 1997 Ind. LEXIS 71



June 6, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Patricia J. Gifford, Judge. Cause No. 49G04-9301-CF-3364. Indiana Court of Appeals Cause No. 49A02-9412-CR-763.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Indiana Court of Appeals reversed defendant's trial court convictions for deviate conduct and criminal confinement based on an alleged error by the trial court in excluding certain evidence. The prosecution appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by the trial court after the victim, who was a stripper with a history of prostitution and heavy drug use, testified that defendant kept her in a car against her will, ordered her to perform sexual favors at gunpoint, and attempted to forcibly remove her clothing. On appeal from the appellate court's reversal of defendant's convictions, the issues were whether the trial court properly excluded evidence of the victim's sexual history and prior drug use. The Supreme Court of Indiana agreed with the trial court that such evidence was not admissible. The victim testified that she had not used drugs the day at issue or the day of trial, and the court found that the fact that the victim had used drugs, in and of itself, was not relevant. As to sexual history, the court found that such the trial court properly excluded testimony from a friend of the victim that on prior occasions the victim had committed acts of prostitution in exchange for money or cocaine. This was properly excluded because no exceptions to Indiana's Rape Shield Rule, Ind. R. Evid. 412, applied.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the ruling of the appellate court and reinstated the trial court convictions.

Pierce v. State


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 54S01-9511-CR-01319


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


677 N.E.2d 39; 1997 Ind. LEXIS 16



February 28, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MONTGOMERY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Thomas K. Milligan, Judge. Cause No. 54C01-9311-CF-00060. Indiana Court of Appeals Cause No. 54A01-9501-CR-9.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded in part


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Indiana Court of Appeals, which affirmed his conviction after a jury trial on charges of criminal confinement and child molesting. Defendant challenged the admissibility of testimony of witnesses who reported the child victim's statements and a videotape of an interview with the victim under Ind. Code § 35-37-4-6.


OVERVIEW: A child became separated from her mother in a department store. When located, the child reported to witnesses that defendant had taken her to his car and molested her. The child later made a videotaped statement at the police station. Pursuant to § 35-37-4-6, the trial court conducted a competency hearing and held that the child was not competent to testify. The witnesses' testimony and the child's videotape were admitted into evidence at trial. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that: (1) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding sufficient indications of reliability under § 35-37-4-6 to support admission of the witnesses' testimony because the victim's statements were spontaneous and occurred shortly after the molestation; (2) the videotaped statement was cumulative of statements that she made to the witnesses following the incident; (3) defendant was not denied his right to confront the victim because she was available for cross-examination at the competency hearing but defendant failed to question her; and (4) given its safeguards against admission of untrustworthy evidence, § 35-37-4-6 did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, § 13.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower appellate court, which affirmed defendant's conviction on charges of criminal confinement and child molesting, and remanded to the trial court for entry of a sentencing order in conformity with the lower appellate court's order for a reduction of defendant's sentence.

Hunter v. State


Supreme Court No. 69S00-9407-CR-632


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


676 N.E.2d 14; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 192



December 31, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE RIPLEY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Carl H. Taul, Judge. Cause No. 69C01-9111-CF-814.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence in the Ripley Circuit Court (Indiana) for murder and burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to murder and burglary and received a 60-year sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed. Defendant's confinement with older, hardened criminals did not violate Ind. Const. art. 1, § 18. The only youths who were not subject to the general rule prohibiting their confinement to an adult correctional facility were those alleged to have committed the most serious and violent crimes. It was within the legislature's purview to conclude that this system better accommodated the purposes behind Ind. Const. art. I, § 18 and Ind. Const. art. 9 § 2, because it segregated younger and less violent offenders from the most violent offenders, regardless of age. The 60-year sentence was not an abuse of discretion. The record amply supported the finding that defendant could control his actions, there were several aggravating factors, and a sentencing court needed only a single aggravating factor to justify imposing an enhanced sentence. No manifest injustice resulted from the trial court's denial of defendant's request to withdraw his guilty plea. A misstatement regarding the possible sentence did not prejudicially influence defendant's decision to plead guilty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for murder and burglary.

Bayh v. Indiana State Bldg. & Constr. Trades Council


In the Supreme Court, no. 45S00-9511-CV-1259


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


674 N.E.2d 176; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 184



December 23, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James Danikolas, Judge. Cause No. 45DO3-9505-CP-01526.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rescinded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state officials appealed from the judgment of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which enjoined enforcement of the Prevailing Wage Act, Ind. Code ch. 5-16-7, as amended by 1995 Ind. House Enrolled Acts (H.E.A.) 1598, 1435. The trial court found that the 1995 amendments violated Ind. Const. art. IV, § 19, which confined all acts, except those codifying, revising or rearranging the laws, to one subject.


OVERVIEW: The legislature attached riders to 1995 Ind. H.E.A. 1598 (HEA 1598), a renamed environmental bill, to amend the Prevailing Wage Act. The legislature later passed 1995 Ind. H.E.A. 1435 (HEA 1435) to amend "Ind. Code § 5-16-7-1, as amended by 1995 Ind. H.E.A. 1598." On this appeal, the court did not address the trial court finding that HEA 1598 was unconstitutional under Ind. Const. art. IV, § 19, but rather held that the trial court erred when it held that HEA 1435 was invalid because it attempted to amend HEA 1598, an invalid law. The court held that HEA 1435 amended the existing Prevailing Wage Act, not HEA 1598, and that unlike HEA 1598, HEA 1435 dealt with only one subject and did not violate Ind. Const. art. IV, § 19 on its face. The court agreed that one purpose of Ind. Const. art. IV, § 19 was to prevent "logrolling," but held that the trial court erred when it considered the legislative history and negotiations behind HEA 1435 instead of reviewing the final act itself. The court held that HEA 1435 was valid and enforceable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that had held the last amendment to the Prevailing Wage Act to be invalid. The court rescinded the trial court's injunction that had prevented enforcement of the amendment by the state officials.

 

57 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Boehm v. Town of St. John


49S10-9608-TA-544


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


675 N.E.2d 318; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 183



December 23, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA TAX COURT. The Honorable Thomas G. Fisher, Judge. Cause No. 49T10-9309-TA-00070.



DISPOSITION: The Tax Court is affirmed in part and reversed in part. This case is remanded to the Tax Court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Indiana State Board of Tax Commissioners, challenged the decision of the Indiana Tax Court, which held that the state constitution required a system of property assessment and taxation based on market value and that, because the statutory system of taxation valued real property on a basis other than market value, the system was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Board contended that the statutory taxation systems was not unconstitutional because Ind. Const. art. 10, § 1 committed the design of a property taxation system to the legislative branch. The court found that the language of art. 10 § 1, along with the circumstances of its adoption, clearly demonstrated that the framers did not intend to give the legislature unrestrained discretion as to the laws of assessment and taxation. Therefore, the tax court did not err in undertaking to determine if the state system complied with constitutional prerequisites. However, the court agreed with the Board's contention that the tax court erroneously concluded that art. 10, § 1 required the state system of real property assessment and taxation to be based on a system which used market value as the measure of equality and uniformity. The court held that although this method of assessment came closest to constitutional requirements for uniform and equal rates and for just valuation, a system based solely upon strict fair market value was not expressly required either by the text of the constitution, by the purpose and intent of its framers, or by subsequent case law.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed in part and vacated and remanded in part.

 

58 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Van Cleave


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 49S00-9008-PD-541


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


674 N.E.2d 1293; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 173



December 19, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 28, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Paula Lopossa. Cause No. CR82-153D.



DISPOSITION: Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which granted postconviction relief to appellee inmate and vacated his guilty plea and conviction for felony murder on the ground that the inmate had been denied his constitutional right to effective assistance of counsel. The postconviction court also vacated the inmate's death sentence, but the state did not appeal that part of the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The inmate shot the victim when he and three companions attempted to steal a television, which the victim had set up in his yard so that he could watch the World Series while he caulked a window. After a lengthy sentencing hearing, the trial court sentenced the inmate to death. The postconviction court held that the inmate was denied effective assistance of counsel because his trial lawyer failed to uncover relevant evidence that, if discovered, would have caused the inmate to go to trial instead of entering a plea. The court reversed and held that the postconviction court erred as a matter of law in setting aside the conviction. The court held that in order to establish a constitutional claim, the inmate had to demonstrate a reasonable probability that he would not have been convicted at trial. The court held that the mitigating evidence the inmate's lawyer failed to uncover, although relevant to the inmate's intent to kill, did not establish a reasonable probability of a different result had the inmate gone to trial because his intent to commit the robbery was never in doubt and the state would not have been required to prove intent to kill to obtain a felony murder conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the postconviction court's order vacating defendant's conviction for felony murder, reinstated defendant's felony conviction, and remanded the case for a new sentencing hearing.

Peterson v. State


45S00-9103-DP-223


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


674 N.E.2d 528; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 167



December 13, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Rehearing Denied July 18, 1997.
Rehearing denied by, 07/18/1997
Related proceeding at Ben-Yisrayl v. State, 690 N.E.2d 1141, 1997 Ind. LEXIS 248 (Ind., 1997)
Writ of certiorari denied Peterson v. Indiana, 522 U.S. 1078, 118 S. Ct. 858, 139 L. Ed. 2d 757, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 520 (1998)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James L. Clement, Judge. Cause No. 45G04-9103-CF-00042.
Peterson v. State, 653 N.E.2d 1022, 1995 Ind. App. LEXIS 809 (Ind. Ct. App., 1995)



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of murder for the intentional killing of two brothers. After hearing evidence during the penalty phase of the trial, the jury recommended that the death penalty not be imposed. The Lake Superior Court (Indiana) declined to follow the jury recommendation and imposed a sentence of death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the shotgun introduced into evidence was obtained by an unreasonable search and seizure and should have been suppressed, that his statements to the police were inadmissible, and that it was an error to impose the death penalty. On appeal, the court held that (1) defendant had no standing to challenge the search because he had no expectation of privacy in his mother's home because he had moved out at her request and she gave consent for the search; (2) defendant had standing to challenge the seizure of the shotgun, but because it was in open/plain view, it was admissible; (3) defendant's warrantless arrest was legal because there was sufficient probable cause based on an informant's statements; (4) defendant's confession was admissible because it was the product of his own free will and his improperly prolonged detention did not invalidate the trial court's finding of voluntariness; (5) the imposition of the death sentence was not arbitrary, as the jury and the trial judge weighed both aggravating and mitigating circumstances; and (6) the trial court gave extensive consideration to the jury's recommendation against death before declining to follow it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's murder convictions and the imposition of the death sentence.

 

60 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sproles


Indiana Supreme Court Cause No. 47S00-9512-CV-1348


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


672 N.E.2d 1353; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 150



November 8, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAWRENCE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Andrea K. McCord, Judge Pro Tempore. Cause No. 47C01-9309-CP-612.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged an order from the Lawrence Circuit Court (Indiana) that issued a declaratory judgment finding that the Controlled Substance Excise Tax, Ind. Code §§ 6-7-3-1 to 6-7-3-20 (1993 & Supp. 1996), violated the double jeopardy clause of U.S. Const. amend. V.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state sought to collect taxes from appellee drug possessor under the Controlled Substance Excise Tax (CSET) and recorded a judgment lien against his interests including property he owned with appellee tenants-in-common. Appellee drug possessor later pleaded guilty to marijuana possession. Appellee tenants-in-common filed an action to partition the property, and appellee drug possessor filed a constitutional cross-claim. The circuit court found that CSET violated the double jeopardy clause of U.S. Const. amend. V, but on appeal, the court reversed, holding that a court of general jurisdiction lacked authority to entertain a constitutional challenge to a tax. The court concluded that the Tax Court's jurisdiction over such a claim was exclusive because the case arose under the Indiana tax laws and the original tax appeal was for a final determination that the tax was owed. Taxpayers were required to pursue all administrative remedies before seeking judicial review even if the review sought to challenge the constitutionality of a tax statute. Thus, appellee drug possessor could not bypass the Tax Court and seek a remedy directly in the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order declaring that Indiana's controlled substance tax law was a violation of the Fifth Amendment because the circuit court lacked jurisdiction to entertain a challenge to the constitutionality of a tax statute. The case was remanded to proceed on the merits of the partition action filed by appellee tenants-in-common.

Edgecomb v. State


Cause No. 46S00-9412-CR-1308


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


673 N.E.2d 1185; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 147



November 1, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellee's Rehearing Denied January 22, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LaPORTE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Robert S. Gettinger, Judge. Cause No. 46C01-9404-CF-034.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the LaPorte Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant upon a jury verdict of aiding in a felony murder in violation of Ind. Code Ann. §§ 35-42-1-1(2) (Supp. 1996), 35-41-2-4 (1986). Defendant also sought review of the sentence, which included a 40-year presumptive sentence and an additional 20 years for aggravating circumstances.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's friend killed the victim during a robbery after defendant gave her friend substantial information about the victim, who was defendant's neighbor, and the victim's house. Defendant did not accompany her friend to the victim's house. Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to establish that she aided her friend in robbing the victim and, therefore, she could not be held liable as an accomplice for the murder that arose out of the robbery. The court affirmed the conviction, concluding that a reasonable trier of fact could find that defendant aided her friend in robbing the victim. The court found that defendant's actions before, during, and after the commission of the crime suggested guilt. The court also rejected defendant's contentions that the use of an alias in the jury instructions was prejudicial error, that the admission of certain photographs was prejudicial, and that the jury instructions did not adequately inform the jury on the burden of proof. The court, however, remanded for resentencing, finding that the valid aggravating factors did not outweigh the mitigating factors as to justify the maximum sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that convicted defendant of aiding in a felony murder. The court, however, remanded the action to the trial court with instructions to impose only the standard 40-year sentence for murder and not the additional 20 years for aggravating circumstances.

 

62 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. State


Supreme Court No. 45S00-9210-DP-770


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


669 N.E.2d 1372; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 124



August 15, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 23, 1996.
Rehearing denied by, 12/23/1996
Writ of certiorari denied Williams v. Indiana, 520 U.S. 1232, 117 S. Ct. 1828, 137 L. Ed. 2d 1034, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 3161 (1997)
Post-conviction relief denied at Williams v. State, 724 N.E.2d 1070, 2000 Ind. LEXIS 149 (Ind., 2000)
Decision reached on appeal by Aki-Khuam v. State, 883 N.E.2d 228, 2008 Ind. App. LEXIS 609 (Ind. Ct. App., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James E. Letsinger, Judge. Cause No. 45G02-9207-CF-182.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his jury convictions for six counts of murder and the sentence of death imposed by the Lake Superior Court (Indiana)


OVERVIEW: Defendant murder several persons in order to eliminate witnesses to a robbery. The defendant challenged, inter alia, the trial courts denial of his peremptory challenges, the limitation on the employment of defense experts, the denial of his motion for a continuance. The court concluded that it was within the discretion of the trial courts to manage and control the proceedings to intervene to protect the jurors' rights to serve on the jury. As to the claim that the trial court abused its discretion by limiting the mitigation expert to 25 hours of investigation, the court agreed with the defendant that under Ind. R. Crim. P. 24(C), the trial court had no authority to limit the expert's time so severely. However, the court did not find the trial court's error in this regard to require reversal as defendant was able to effectively present mitigation evidence to the jury during the penalty phase and to the court at sentencing. Because it was not reversible error for the trial court to deny the mitigation specialist additional hours, it was also not reversible error for the trial court to deny the motion for a continuance for further investigation into mitigation evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and death sentence.

Holmes v. State


Supreme Court No. 49S00-9002-DP-00104


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


671 N.E.2d 841; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 100



August 7, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Rehearing Denied January 17, 1997. Certiorari Denied October 6, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5167.
Writ of certiorari denied Holmes v. Indiana, 522 U.S. 849, 118 S. Ct. 137, 139 L. Ed. 2d 85, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 5167 (1997)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Holmes, 728 N.E.2d 164, 2000 Ind. LEXIS 450 (Ind., 2000)
Post-conviction relief denied at Holmes v. State, 820 N.E.2d 136, 2005 Ind. LEXIS 8 (Ind., 2005)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Holmes v. Buss, 2007 U.S. App. LEXIS 25361 (7th Cir. Ind., Oct. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Cynthia S. Emkes, Special Judge. Cause No. 49G05-8911-CF-131401.



DISPOSITION: The sentence of death is affirmed. The conviction for conspiracy to commit robbery is ordered vacated. The sentence for Robbery, Class A is ordered set aside and a new sentence for Robbery, Class C is ordered imposed in its stead. The remaining convictions and sentences are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of murder, under Ind. Code Ann. § 35-42-1-1(1), attempted murder, and conspiracy to rob by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), and he was sentenced to death. He claimed multiple procedural, evidential, and legal errors on review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the prosecutor's conduct was improper, perjured testimony was elicited at trial, improper victim impact evidence was presented, the jury instructions were improper, and improper use of aggravating and mitigating circumstances by the trial court constituting reversible error of the death sentence. The court disagreed and held that the misconduct complained of was harmless as it had not affected defendant's right to fairness in the jury recommendation process, nor placed it in grave peril. The court said that although testimony was elicited at trial that was not presented to defendant's counsel before, a finding of perjury was not necessitated. The court held that any error in receiving the testimony or the victim impact evidence was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt, and it found mitigating and aggravating factors correctly applied. The court found that the jury was properly charged and that the sentences were not disproportionate. However, the court found that defendant was entitled to resentencing on the robbery count and that vacation of the conspiracy conviction was required under the principles of double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the conviction for conspiracy to commit robbery, and the sentence for robbery was set aside and a new sentence for robbery was ordered instead. The court affirmed the death sentence, as well as the remaining convictions.

Rynerson v. City of Franklin


Supreme Court No. 41S05-9603-CV-00209


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


669 N.E.2d 964; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 113



August 7, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE JOHNSON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable James E. Harris, Special Judge. Court of Appeals No. 41A05-9412-CV-00488. Cause No. 41C01-9006-MI-242.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer was discharged for misconduct by the works and safety board of appellee city and he sought judicial review. The Court of Appeals (Indiana) reversed the trial court and held that the provision in Ind. Code § 36-8-3-4(c) that permitted the city attorney to withdraw as a member of the board and prosecute a disciplinary action violated due process under the Fourteenth Amendment. The city's request for transfer was granted.


OVERVIEW: As required by § 36-8-3-4(c), a city attorney withdrew as a member of the board in order to represent the police chief in a proceeding against an officer charged with misconduct and neglect of duty. The officer argued that his dismissal was wrongful because the procedure denied him due process. The court of appeals held that the statute was fundamentally unfair because the board could be expected to give greater credence to the arguments of one of its members. The court held that the procedure did not violate due process. A presumption of honesty and integrity applied to the members of administrative bodies and there was no showing of bias or prejudice on the part of the members who made the decision to discharge the officer. The suggestion by the court of appeals that city attorneys should not serve on such boards was impractical because their legal expertise was needed in performing the myriad tasks assigned by statute to the boards. The police chief's suggestion that the officer take a polygraph examination did not constitute a stipulation that its results would be admissible and the trial court had not erred in excluding that evidence.


OUTCOME: The court held that the procedure did not violate due process and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

65 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Citizens Nat'l Bank v. Foster


CAUSE NO. 82S00-9408-CQ-760


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


668 N.E.2d 1236; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 123



August 7, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON CERTIFICATION FROM THE UNITED STATES DISTRICT COURT FOR THE SOUTHERN DISTRICT OF INDIANA, EVANSVILLE DIVISION. The Honorable Gene E. Brooks, Judge. No. EV 94-95-C.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee creditor challenged the exemption of individual retirement accounts from the assets of appellant debtors. The United States District Court for the Southern District of Indiana certified two questions to the court: Whether Ind. Code Ann. §§ 27-1-12-14(c), 34-2-28-1(a)(6) (Supp. 1991) violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 22, by failing to impose a cap on the exempt amount.


OVERVIEW: The debtors sought to exempt their individual retirement accounts (IRA) from their debtor estate and thereby make those monies unreachable by the creditor. These certified questions caused the court to revisit the constitutionality of statutes exempting a debtor's property from the pool of assets available to creditors. The court examined held that the Indiana Constitution required that the legislature fashion exemptions of a debtor's property from the pool of assets available to creditors in reasonably tangible ways designed to balance the interests of debtors and lenders. Ind. Code Ann. § 34-2-28-1(a)(6) (Supp. 1991) made explicit reference to an amount certain and readily ascertainable in the Internal Revenue Code, which was a reasonably tangible way to describe the amount of the exemption, and therefore complied with Ind. Const. art. I, § 22. Although the Ind. Code Ann. § 27-1-12-14(c) exemption on individual retirement accounts was constitutional, the Ind. Code Ann. § 27-1-12-14(c) exemption for life insurance was constitutionally suspect and may be claimed only upon proof that the exemption was required to afford the necessities of life.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the statutory exemption on individual retirement accounts was constitutional, but the exemption for life insurance was constitutionally suspect and may be claimed only upon proof that the exemption was required to afford the necessities of life.

 

66 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hoovler


79S00-9509-CV-1085


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


668 N.E.2d 1229; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 118



August 7, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Jeffrey R. Smith, Special Judge. Cause No. 79C01-9404-CP-125.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, State of Indiana and Department of Revenue (State), appealed the judgment of the Tippecanoe Circuit Court (Indiana), which held that Pub. L. No. 44-1994 violated Ind. Const. art. IV, §§ 22, 23. Plaintiff taxpayers had brought the action in the lower court.


OVERVIEW: One county in Indiana had received notice that it was a potentially responsible party (PRP) for a superfund landfill site and could be responsible for the expensive cleanup of the landfill. The General Assembly enacted Pub. L. No. 44-1994 which only applied to counties within a narrowly specified population range, and the only county with that population was the county that received the PRP notice. Pub. L. No. 44-1994 permitted the specified county to increase the economic development income tax rate. The lower court held that Pub. L. No. 44-1994 violated Indiana's constitution, and the court reversed. The court held that even though Pub. L. No. 44-1994 was a special law, it did not violate Ind. Const. art. IV, § 22 because the enactment did not authorize new property valuations. The court ruled that the specified county had a unique exposure to superfund liability, and, therefore, Pub. L. No. 44-1994 was not a matter necessarily subject to a general law uniformly applicable in all counties. Consequently, Pub. L. No. 44-1994 did not violate Ind. Const. art. IV, § 23.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court, which held that Indiana's Constitution prohibited the law which only permitted one county to raise its economic development income tax rate. The case was remanded for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

 

67 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


K.S. v. R.S.


Supreme Court No. 55S04-9602-CV-00162


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


669 N.E.2d 399; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 87



July 29, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MORGAN COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable James E. Harris, Judge. Cause No. 55C01-9401-JP-12. Court of Appeals No. 55A04-9502-CV-42.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movant mother sought to set aside an agreed entry stating that her neighbor was her child's father. The trial court denied the mother's motion. The Court of Appeals (Indiana) found the trial court lacked jurisdiction. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: While the mother was married, she had a sexual relationship with her neighbor. After her child's birth, the neighbor petitioned the trial court to establish his paternity. The child was not named as a party or represented by a guardian ad litem. The trial court approved an agreed entry stating that the neighbor was the child's biological father and arranging for joint custody and no child support at the time. The mother then moved to set aside the agreed entry pursuant to Ind. R. Trial P. 60(B)(6). The trial court denied the motion, and the appellate court found the trial court lacked jurisdiction. On further appeal, the court found the trial court had jurisdiction. Although the child was born while the mother was married, the child was born out of wedlock because the mother was not married to the neighbor. Thus, the neighbor could file a paternity action under Ind. Code § 31-6-6.1-2 (1993 & Supp. 1995). Although the child was not named in the paternity action and no guardian ad litem was appointed, the agreed entry was merely voidable, not void. The trial court did not err in refusing to set it aside. The agreement did not contract away the child's right to support from a parent.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appellate court's opinion that the trial court lacked jurisdiction. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the mother's motion to set aside the agreed entry establishing that her neighbor was her child's father.

Rider v. Rider


Indiana Supreme Cause No. 48S02-9510-CV-01137


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


669 N.E.2d 160; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 93



July 26, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 16, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MADISON COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT, Division 3. The Honorable Thomas Newman, Jr., Judge. Cause No. 48DO3-9210-DR-0727. Cause No. 48A02-9312-CV-680.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband sought review of a decision from the Court of Appeals (Indiana), which affirmed the judgment of the trial court that enforced part, but not all, of the antenuptial agreement entered into by appellant and appellee former wife just prior to marriage.


OVERVIEW: Appellee former wife and appellant former husband entered into an antenuptial agreement. The couple subsequently married and lived in the house owned by appellee until they separated. Appellant petitioned for dissolution of his marriage and sought to enforce an antenuptial agreement. The trial court enforced part, but not all, of the antenuptial agreement, and the appellate court affirmed. Appellant petitioned the court for transfer, which it granted in order to examine the issue of when a trial court could choose to disregard all or part of a no-maintenance provision of an antenuptial agreement. The court reversed and remanded. The court held that the trial court erred by not enforcing the antenuptial agreement in its entirety. Both the trial court and the appellate court failed to consider the relative financial positions of the spouses. The court held that the enforcement of the antenuptial agreement would leave appellee with virtually all of the real and personal property, while leaving appellant with a modest income stream. The court found that given appellant's limited financial position, the enforcement of the parties' own agreement was not unconscionable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court, which affirmed the order of the trial court that enforced part of the antenuptial agreement entered into by appellant former husband and appellee former wife. The court held that the antenuptial agreement was enforceable in its entirety and remanded to the trial court.

Sears v. State


Supreme Court No. 49S00-9407-CR-608


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


668 N.E.2d 662; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 82



July 9, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT Criminal Division, Room 5. The Honorable Gary L. Miller, Judge. Cause No. 49G05-9209-CF-120972.



DISPOSITION: The defendant's convictions and sentence are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) after he was convicted of, inter alia, murder under Ind. Code § 35-42-1-1 (1992 Supp.), robbery under Ind. Code § 35-42-5-1 (1993), kidnapping under Ind. Code § 35-42-4-2 (1993), and carrying a handgun without a license under Ind. Code § 35-47-2-1 and -23 (1993).


OVERVIEW: Defendant approached several men on a golf course, demanded their money, and shot one of them when they refused. Next, he called his girlfriend. While in her car, defendant pulled a gun on her when she attempted to turn the car around, threatening to kill her. After persuading defendant to stop at a gas station, the girlfriend asked a young woman in the restroom to call the police. When the police arrived, defendant was arrested and searched. Defendant argued that the trial court improperly admitted the evidence that was seized from his person. The court held that the trial court did not err, as the warrantless search was incident to a lawful arrest. Defendant was "arrested" because the police had reasonable caution to believe that defendant had, at minimum, committed a felony; namely, they received a call that a man was holding a woman against her will with a handgun, and the girlfriend asked the police for help when they approached defendant. The trial court did not err in admitting tapes from interviews that defendant gave to reporters after his arrest, as Miranda warnings were not necessary because the reporters were not acting as agents of the police.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Crawford v. State


Supreme Court No. 49S00-9406-CR-594


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


669 N.E.2d 141; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 66



June 28, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT, ROOM NUMBER ONE, Criminal Division. The Honorable Paula E. Lopossa, Judge. Cause No. 49G01-9005-CF-068039.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's conviction and sentence for First Degree Murder is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction and sentence for first degree murder entered in the Marion Superior Court (Indiana). He alleged in part that he had been denied his constitutional right to a speedy trial, and to trial within 180 days of filing his Interstate Agreement on Detainers (IAD) request for final disposition. The murder charge was nearly 30 years old. He had been in a Missouri prison following his conviction on a murder charge.


OVERVIEW: In 1965 defendant was arrested in Texas and admitted to killing a cabdriver in Indiana. He was transferred to Missouri because of his admitted involvement in a murder there. An Indiana warrant was issued. Nearly 10 years later a detainer was lodged with regard to a second Indiana murder. Defendant was then serving a life sentence in Missouri, and filed his IAD request for final disposition on that charge. In 1990 Indiana commenced the action regarding the cabdriver's murder and filed a detainer against defendant. In 1992 he filed a motion to dismiss, and in 1993 filed his IAD request for final disposition. The motion to dismiss was denied, and the trial was conducted after defendant and the state requested continuances. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and he appealed. The court held that he was not denied his right to a speedy trial because the right did not attach until the formal indictment or information was filed. His right attached in 1990, and he was tried in 1994. The delay was not prejudicial and did not impair his defense of the case. He was tried within the 180-day IAD requirement because his 1973 IAD notice did not pertain to the murdered cabdriver.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for first degree murder, and held that he had not been denied the right to a speedy trial.

A Woman's Choice-East Side Women's Clinic v. Newman


No. 94S00-9511-CQ-1270


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


671 N.E.2d 104; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 122



April 30, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Rehearing Denied December 30, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFIED QUESTION FROM THE UNITED STATES DISTRICT COURT FOR THE SOUTHERN DISTRICT OF INDIANA. The Honorable David F. Hamilton, Judge. Cause No. IP 95-1148C-H/G.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States District Court for the Southern District of Indiana certified certain questions about the medical emergency exception to Indiana's new abortion law, Public Law 187, 1995 Ind. Acts 3327, to resolve a facial challenge to the abortion law's constitutionality brought by plaintiff abortion providers.


OVERVIEW: The abortion providers argued that, based on the rules of statutory construction, the medical emergency exception to Public Law 187 should be construed very narrowly. Defendant attorney general claimed that the medical emergency exception was crafted to conform with the medical emergency exception in the Pennsylvania Abortion Control Act, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. §§ 3203-3220 (1980 & Supp. 1996) and that its language supported an interpretation consistent with federal court decisions on abortion. The court answered the certified questions as follows: 1) a woman may be excepted from compliance with the statutory informed consent provisions contained in Ind. Code Ann. § 16-34-2-1.1 when she faces significant and imminent threats to her life or health; 2) Public Law 187 allows only death or substantial and irreversible impairment to excuse compliance with its informed consent provisions, and severe-but-temporary conditions in which an abortion is not the medically necessary treatment was not covered by the exception; and 3) compliance with Public Law 187's informed consent provisions may be excused when compliance threatens to cause the woman severe psychological harm.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified questions relating to the Indiana abortion law, stating that the medical emergency provision permitted dispensing with the informed consent requirements where the attending physician deemed therapeutic abortion medically necessary. The court held that such exception applied to only serious and physical and mental health issues, not to temporary health problems.

Town Bd. v. Greenfield Mills, Inc.


Supreme Court No. 44S05-9507-CV-804


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


663 N.E.2d 523; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 18



March 18, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAGRANGE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Howard E. Peterson, Judge. Cause No. 44C01-9502-CP-16.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners brought an action against defendant town to obtain an injunction barring the town from constructing a sanitary sewer system. The LaGrange Circuit Court (Indiana) preliminarily enjoined the project. The town appealed.


OVERVIEW: Believing that the town's construction of a sanitary sewer system would cause environmental damage to a river, the landowners brought an action against the town to enjoin the town from building the system. The trial court granted a preliminary injunction, but the court vacated the injunction and ordered that the landowners' complaint be dismissed. The water pollution control and facility permitting statute, Ind. Code §§ 13-1-3-1 to 13-1-3-22, 13-7-5-2 to 13-7-5-8, gave the Indiana Department of Environmental Management (IDEM) authority to determine whether the town's project would comply with state water pollution standards. The court believed that, at the end of the permitting process, there would be no remaining issues to resolve. Therefore, the trial court lacked jurisdiction to grant the landowners' request for an injunction on the grounds of the public damage the project would cause. The trial court also lacked jurisdiction to grant an injunction on the grounds of the landowners' private property rights because the legislature had entrusted to IDEM the decision of whether to construct the project.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the preliminary injunction and remanded the action to the trial court with instructions to dismiss the landowners' complaint with prejudice.

 

73 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Howard v. Incorporated Town of N. Judson


No. 75S03-9504-CV-00442


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


661 N.E.2d 549; 1996 Ind. LEXIS 9



February 15, 1996, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE STARKE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable David P. Matsey, Judge. Cause No. 75C01-9308-CP-195. No. 75A03-9403-CV-90 Court of Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer brought an action against appellee municipality for wrongful termination. The trial court granted the municipality's motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The Court of Appeals (Indiana) reversed and remanded solely for a determination of the appropriate amount of damages. The municipality's petition to transfer was granted by the court.


OVERVIEW: In his action for wrongful termination, the police officer alleged that his termination without a hearing violated Ind. Code Ann. § 36-8-3-4, the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, and the police officer's rights under Ind. Const. art. I, § 12. The court found that the protections of Ind. Code Ann. § 36-8-3-4 were inapplicable because the police officer was offered an opportunity to request a hearing before his termination became effective but he declined. The court found that the police officer's due process rights were not violated because the police officer was given notice of the municipality's plan to terminate him, that notice informed him of his right to a hearing, and he chose not to request a hearing. The opportunity for a hearing was due process of law. Finally, the court also found that Ind. Const. art. I, § 12 did not mandate a pre-deprivation hearing even to protect admittedly important reputational interests.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the appellate court and affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the police officer's action for wrongful termination against the municipality.

 

74 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Clifft v. Ind. Dep't of State Revenue


Cause No. 49S10-9503-TA-331


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


660 N.E.2d 310; 1995 Ind. LEXIS 198



December 27, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Concurring and Dissenting Opinion Filed January 2, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA TAX COURT. The Honorable Thomas G. Fisher, Judge. Cause No. 49T10-9308-TA-64.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Indiana Department of State Revenue (department) assessed a drug tax against appellant taxpayers for possession of marijuana. The Indiana Tax Court found the assessment violated the double jeopardy protections of one taxpayer and reversed the assessment as to her. The taxpayers appealed, arguing equal protection and self-incrimination violations. The department appealed the ruling as to double jeopardy finding.


OVERVIEW: A police search of the home of the taxpayers, husband and wife, uncovered marijuana. Pursuant to the Indiana Controlled Substance Excise Tax (CSET), the department assessed a drug tax under Ind. Code Ann. § 6-7-3-6 (1994). The wife was then convicted of possession of marijuana. The taxpayers argued that the CSET violated the self-incrimination protection of the Fifth Amendment by forcing the wife to physically appear at the department's office to pay the fine. They alleged violation of the Due Process Clause because the property was seized without a hearing. The court held that the CSET was a punishment, and jeopardy attached at the time of assessment. The CSET did not violate the Fifth Amendment because the information could not be revealed to law enforcement or be used to facilitate prosecution. Moreover, the CSET did not require the payor's physical presence as anyone was entitled to pay the tax on behalf of the payor. As to the due process claim, the legislature properly found that the government's need to take immediate action justified the use of a post-deprivation hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's rulings that the taxpayers' equal protection, due process, and self-incrimination rights were not violated. The court reversed the trial court's ruling that the assessment violated the taxpayer's double jeopardy protections. The court found that the assessment was the taxpayer's first jeopardy, and it was the misdemeanor conviction that was barred. The court, thus, reinstated the assessment.

Mitchell v. State


Supreme Court No. 20S03-9503-CR-341


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


659 N.E.2d 112; 1995 Ind. LEXIS 188



December 15, 1995, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Stephen E. Platt, Judge. Cause No. 20D02-9209-CF-106. Court of Appeals No. 20A03-9312-CR-402.



DISPOSITION: The conviction and sentence are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Elkhart Superior Court (Indiana), which was entered pursuant to defendant's plea bargain, that convicted him of possession of cocaine, a Class D felony. The judgment prescribed a suspended one and a half year prison sentence, placed defendant on probation for a year, and suspended defendant's driver's license, license plates, and ability to register a motor vehicle pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-48-4-15 (1992).


OVERVIEW: After he was charged with the delivery of cocaine, a Class B felony, defendant agreed to a plea bargain and a judgment of conviction for the possession of cocaine was entered against him. The trial court's judgment prescribed a suspended prison sentence, probation, and the suspension of defendant's driving privileges. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that Ind. Code § 35-48-4-15(a) (1994) made clear that the trial court was obligated to suspend defendant's driving privileges. The court held that the trial court's discretion extended only to the length of the suspension. Further, defendant chose to dispose of the charge against him by accepting a plea bargain and agreed to leave sentencing to the trial court's discretion. In balancing the factors of private interest, risk of erroneous deprivation, and governmental interest, there was no violation of defendant's procedural due process rights. Defendant's substantive due process rights were also not violated because there was no fundamental right to drive and § 35-48-4-15(a) bore a rational relationship to the legitimate state interest in punishing lawbreakers and deterring lawbreaking.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of the possession of cocaine and that prescribed a suspended prison sentence, probation, and the suspension of defendant's driving privileges.

 

76 of 1699 DOCUMENTS



Steward v. State


Supreme Court No. 65S04-9506-CR-677


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


652 N.E.2d 490; 1995 Ind. LEXIS 91



June 23, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Amended June 26, 1995. Rehearing Denied February 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE POSEY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Donald E. Baier, Special Judge. Cause No. 65C01-9104-CF-9 & 65C01-9104-CF-10. Court of Appeals No. 65A04-9207-CR-251.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision by the Court of Appeals (Indiana), which affirmed his conviction on one count of child molestation and reversed his conviction on a second count of child molestation. He alleged that the lower court failed to address his argument that the state's expert testimony regarding the child sexual abuse syndrome was unreliable and unscientific, and thus, was inadmissible in his trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on one count of child molestation, a class C felony under Ind. Code Ann. § 35-42-4-3(c) (1986), and convicted on one count of child molestation, a class D felony under Ind. Code Ann. § 35-42-4-3(d) (1986). The court affirmed his conviction on the first count, reversed his conviction on the second count, and remanded the second count for a new trial. The court found that scientific evidence that child victims of sexual abuse exhibited unexpected behavior patterns apparently inconsistent with the claim of abuse was admissible under the authorization in Ind. R. Evid. 702(a) of specialized knowledge that would assist the trier of fact to understand the evidence. The court ruled that if defendant discussed or presented evidence of such child behavior, or if the child recanted a prior allegation of abuse, the trial court could consider permitting expert testimony based upon reliable scientific principles regarding the prevalence of such behavior. To be admissible, the scientific evidence would have to assist the factfinder in understanding a child's responses to abuse and satisfy the requirements of both Ind. R. Evid. 702(a) and Ind. R. Evid. 403.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed one of defendant's convictions for child molestation, reversed the other, and remanded the cause for a new trial on the reversed charge. Because research generally accepted as scientifically reliable recognized that child victims of sexual abuse could exhibit unexpected behavior patterns seemingly inconsistent with the claim of abuse, such evidence was permissible as specialized knowledge that would assist the trier of fact.
