Pence v. State


No. 49S00-9406-CV-579


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


652 N.E.2d 486; 1995 Ind. LEXIS 87



June 20, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 22, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James S. Kirsch, Judge. Cause No. 49D05-9302-CP-136.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer and plaintiff citizens' organization filed an action against defendant state seeking a declaration that Pub. L. No. 4-1992 violated the state constitution. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) granted the state's motion for summary judgment, and the taxpayer and the citizens' organization appealed.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted Pub. L. No. 4-1992, which brought state law into conformity with the Americans with Disabilities Act but included a provision that defined the word "salary" in a way that increased the state's obligation to contribute to the legislature's pension fund. The taxpayer and the citizens' organization claimed that the law violated Ind. Const. art. IV, § 29 because it increased the pay of members of the legislature while the legislature was in session. They also claimed that it violated Ind. Const. art. IV, § 19 because it concerned more than a single topic. The court upheld the grant of summary judgment in favor of the state. The court ruled that (1) the taxpayer and the citizens' organization lacked standing because they failed to demonstrate that they had an interest beyond that of the general public; and (2) the court therefore lacked jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the state.

 

78 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Indiana Dep't of State Revenue v. Fort Wayne Nat'l Corp.


No. 49S10-9406-TA-521


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


649 N.E.2d 109; 1995 Ind. LEXIS 60



April 10, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended April 13, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tax Court. No. 49T10-9204-TA-17. APPEAL FROM THE INDIANA TAX COURT. The Honorable Thomas G. Fisher, Judge. Cause No. 49S10-9204-TA-17.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee taxpayer sought a refund from appellant Indiana State Department of Revenue (department). The Indiana Tax Court granted summary judgment against department and granted taxpayer's request for a refund. Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer claimed that the refund sought represented tax either improperly levied upon or measured by municipal and federal bond income from municipal bonds or federal bonds. The taxpayer argued that the financial institution tax (FIT) was a direct tax on its federal and municipal bonds, as well as the income from those bonds, and that the application of the FIT was an impermissible retroactive tax. The department argued that the FIT did not tax the bond; rather, the FIT was an excise that taxes a financial institution's privilege of conducting business in Indiana. The court determined that based on the plain language of Ind. Code Ann. § 6-5.5-1-2 (1994) and its non-discriminatory formula for calculating the individual's tax liability, the FIT was not a direct tax but rather an excise tax on the exercise of the corporate privilege of operating as a financial institution in Indiana. Accordingly, the court determined that the tax court erred in its decision to grant taxpayer a refund.


OUTCOME: The court granted the department's petition for review, vacated the judgment of the tax court, and affirmed the department's denial of taxpayer's request for a refund.

 

79 of 1699 DOCUMENTS



Harrison v. State


Supreme Court No., 65S00-9105-DP-380


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


644 N.E.2d 1243; 1995 Ind. LEXIS 7



January 4, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended January 6, 1995. Appellant's Petition for Rehearing Denied April 10, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ind. LEXIS 28.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE POSEY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable James M. Redwine, Judge. Cause No. 65001-9104-CF-00008.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with arson, two counts of knowing murder, and felony murder. After a trial, he was convicted by the Posey Circuit Court (Indiana) of arson, one count of knowing murder, and felony murder. Defendant received the death sentence. He appealed his sentence and convictions for murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant brutalized an acquaintance and then set fire to her house, killing her and her children. The court held that the acquittal of one charge of murder and conviction on the others was not an inconsistent verdict because defendant's intent was independently proven for each crime. Defendant showed no prejudice from pre-trial publicity and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying his motion for judicial recusal. The trial court did err by failing to hold a hearing regarding the reliability of the DNA evidence, the qualification of the prosecution's expert witness, and the danger of unfair prejudice. However, the error was harmless because defendant failed to object. Because the DNA testimony involved precise measurements and testing, defendant was not entitled to a continuance or a court appointed expert to aid his defense. The trial court properly denied use of an alibi defense due to defendant's failure to timely notify the prosecution. The imposition of the death penalty was supported by the evidence and did not violate constitutional principles, however, the trial court failed to adequately provide its reasoning for the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the murder convictions, but remanded the action for a more specific sentencing order or statement of reasons for selecting the death penalty.

Lambert v. State


No. 18S00-9107-DP-544


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


643 N.E.2d 349; 1994 Ind. LEXIS 193



December 6, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Granted December 30, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Ind. LEXIS 189.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DELAWARE SUPERIOR COURT, DIVISION I. The Honorable Robert L. Barnet, Jr., Judge. Cause No. 18D01-9101-CF-02.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Delaware Superior Court, Division I (Indiana), which convicted defendant of the murder of a police officer.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of murdering a police officer, he sought review. On appeal, defendant alleged that the jury panel was improperly drawn and that the system used to obtain prospective jurors violated Ind. Code § 33-4-5-2(a), which required a list of prospective jurors be chosen from not only the list of legal voters in the county but also the latest tax schedules. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that many property owners were in fact registered voters and that there was no showing that the jury was made up entirely of registered voters only and excluded property owners. The court also held that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for change of venue because the jurors were questioned extensively concerning the knowledge they had gained of the case through news media or any other source. The court rejected defendant's argument that allowing the state to proceed to seek a death-qualified jury subjected him to a trial by a guilt-prone jury. The court concluded that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress his statement to the police because defendant knowingly and freely waived his right against self-incrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of murder.

Indiana Dep't of Envtl. Management v. Chemical Waste Management


No. 49S00-9310-CV-1143


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


643 N.E.2d 331; 1994 Ind. LEXIS 170; 40 ERC (BNA) 1652



December 1, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Kenneth H. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 49D02-9201-CP-9.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we reverse in part and affirm in part the trial court, and remand for further consistent proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, a waste facility operator, filed an action against appellants, environmental management department and commissioner, to challenge the constitutionality and retroactive application of Ind. Code § 13-7-10.2 relating to a permit to modify the waste facility. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) granted the operator a preliminary injunction and held the statute was unconstitutional. The department and commissioner filed a praecipe to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The facility, the only commercial one in the state to treat and dispose of hazardous waste, sought a permit to modify the facility. The environmental management department (IDEM) took no action and, two years later, Ind. Code § 13-7-10.2 (1990), which granted the commissioner broad powers to grant or deny permits, became law. IDEM stated that it intended to apply the statute in evaluating the application. IDEM argued the case was not ripe, the statute unconstitutionally distinguished between commercial and non-commercial waste disposal facilities, and it was entitled to a pre-deprivation hearing. The court held (1) the case was not ripe because it was unclear what rules would be promulgated and how to appeal therefrom; (2) in applying the rational basis test standard, Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 was not violated because there was no burdening of the fundamental right to reputation or any suspect classification as denial of a permit was rationally related to the state interest in regulating commercial waste disposal facilities and did not involve reputation; and (3) due process was not violated because a post-deprivation hearing was adequate to protect the reputational interests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment in part, reversed in part, and remanded to the superior court.

 

82 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Indiana Gaming Comm'n v. Moseley


64S00-9406-CV-560


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


643 N.E.2d 296; 1994 Ind. LEXIS 152



November 21, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE PORTER SUPERIOR COURT. Honorable Roger V. Bradford, Special Judge. Cause No. 64D02-9312-CP-2978.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Indiana Gaming Commission (commission) sought review of an order from the Porter Superior Court (Indiana), which found that the statute, Ind. Code Ann. art. 4-33 (1994) (act), that authorized riverboat gambling in the state violated the state constitution and enjoined the commission from issuing licenses, in appellee county residents' action challenging the act.


OVERVIEW: The act created the commission, which was authorized to issue up to 11 riverboat casino licenses if the local legislative body approved of the practice through an ordinance, and the voters of the area voted for the gambling in a referendum, Ind. Code Ann. §§ 4-33-6-18 to 20. The voting schemes differentiated between cities and counties. The county of the residents voted against gambling. The trial court found that the act violated Ind. Const. art. IV, § 23. On review, the court found that because riverboat gambling would only impact communities that bordered the water, the subject of the act was not amenable to a general law of uniform operation throughout the state. Because the referenda provided for in the act were intended as a means for the people, rather than the legislature, to determine for themselves whether to invite gambling operations into their communities, the court found that the ability to vote directly did not inherently convey a privilege or impose a burden and did not contravene § 23. The court found that the voting rules from county to county were rationally related to the legitimate state interest in ensuring votes from those most affected by the act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the finding that the act violated the state constitution and dissolved the injunction enjoining the commission from issuing licenses to riverboat gambling operations.

 

83 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Burris v. State


No. 49S00-9203-DP-187


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


642 N.E.2d 961; 1994 Ind. LEXIS 145



November 4, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 22, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT. CRIMINAL DIVISION IV. The Honorable Patricia J. Gifford, Special Judge. Cause No. 49G04-8001-CF-000166. CR80-53A



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed. The cause is remanded to the trial court for the establishment of a date of execution.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of felony murder after a jury trial. His death sentence was reversed on appeal. On remand, the Marion County Superior Court (Indiana) assembled a new jury to hear evidence and make a recommendation as to the sentencing. After the jury became deadlocked, the trial court discharged the jury and proceeded to enter a judgment ordering the death penalty. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred when it impaneled a new jury without any effort to determine if the original jury that had convicted him eleven years previously could be reassembled. The court affirmed the trial court's death penalty judgment. The court held that there was no error in assembling a new jury to make a recommendation to the trial court. The court stated that there was no practical purpose to be served by the trial judge ordering a search for the original jurors eleven years after their first decision in this case. The court noted that both the state and defendant were afforded the full opportunity to acquaint the new jury with the situation at hand. The fact that they were unable to reach a unanimous decision in no way indicated that they did not understand the facts of the situation. It merely meant they could not agree among themselves as to what recommendation to make to the trial judge. The court stated common sense and judicial economy dictated that the trial judge should have the latitude to assemble a new jury in a situation where substantial time had elapsed since defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The trial court's rulings on defendant's objections, which he made during the penalty phase of his prosecution for felony murder, were affirmed. The court also affirmed the trial court's imposition of the death penalty. The case was remanded for the establishment of a date of execution.

Bivins v. State


Supreme Court No. 06S00-9105-DP-00401


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


642 N.E.2d 928; 1994 Ind. LEXIS 146



November 4, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Order Amending Opinion March 9, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ind. LEXIS 34. Rehearing Denied May 26, 1995. State's Petition for Rehearing Granted May 26, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Ind. LEXIS 74.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE BOONE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Thomas K. Milligan, Special Judge. Cause No 06D01-9104-CF-24.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted following a jury trial of six crimes committed during a two-day crime spree. The Boone Superior Court (Indiana) sentenced him to death for murder, and consecutive terms of twenty years for one count of robbery, twenty years for one count of confinement, three years for one count of auto theft, and three years for each of two counts of theft. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised several arguments on appeal, which were regrouped and addressed as follows: 1) physical restraint at trial; 2) admissibility of defendant's statements; 3) loss or destruction of evidence; 4) evidence and instruction regarding escape; 5) merger of offenses; 6) constitutionality of Indiana's death penalty statute; 7) death penalty aggravator as double jeopardy; 8) penalty phase instructions; 9) failure to find and weigh mitigators; 10) use of nonstatutory aggravators including victim impact evidence; and 11) nature of relief to be afforded. Most of the arguments were without merit, but the court did make a new rule regarding the death penalty. The court held that when the death sentence was sought, the trial court had to limit the aggravating circumstances eligible for consideration to those specified in the death penalty statute.


OUTCOME: The court remanded to the trial court for revision of judgment, to merge the conviction for Count IV, charging theft of money and bank card, with that for Count I, charging robbery, and to vacate the separate sentence for Count IV accordingly. In all other respects, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and the sentences, including the death sentence.

Lowery v. State


No. 32S00-9008-PD-542


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


640 N.E.2d 1031; 1994 Ind. LEXIS 129

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM HENDRICKS CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Thomas K. Milligan, Special Judge. Cause No. 71D08-9102-CF-126.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and death sentence from the Hendricks Circuit Court (Indiana) for double murder and attempted murder during the course of an attempted burglary; defendant also appealed the judgment denying post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering an elderly couple during an attempted burglary. He was also convicted of attempted murder of a third person. Defendant was sentenced to death. This was an appeal from a judgment denying post-conviction relief. He challenged his murder and attempted murder conviction and the death sentence. The court held that the trial court committed fundamental error in convicting defendant of attempted murder. The trial court erred when it failed to instruct the jury on all the essential elements of attempted murder. It reversed the decision of the post-conviction court denying post-conviction relief with respect to the attempted murder conviction and the resulting sentence, and remanded to the post-conviction court. However, the court affirmed the post-conviction court's decision denying defendant's post-conviction relief petition challenging his conviction and death sentences for the double murder.


OUTCOME: The post-conviction court was instructed to grant post-conviction relief and reverse the conviction for attempted murder. The remainder of the judgment of the post-conviction court was affirmed, as were the convictions for murder and the sentence of death.

 

86 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Alcorn


No. 49S00-9305-DP-585


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


638 N.E.2d 1242; 1994 Ind. LEXIS 96



August 12, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] INTERLOCUTORY APPEAL FROM THE MARION COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT CRIMINAL DIVISION VI. The Honorable Carr L. Darden, Judge. Cause No. 49G06-9112-CF-170715.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged a decision of the Marion County Superior Court Criminal Division VI (Indiana), which allowed defendant's pretrial motion to instruct the jury concerning the alternative of life imprisonment without parole in the event he was found guilty of murder and that the Pub. L. No. 250-1993, § 3, violated the equal protection clauses of both the Indiana and United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: In 1991, defendant was charged with murder and the state sought the death penalty. In 1993, the death penalty statute was amended to provide for the alternative sentence of life imprisonment without parole; however, it only applied to murders committed after June 30, 1993. Subsequently, the trial court granted defendant's pretrial motion to instruct the jury of the sentencing alternative. The court reversed, finding that at the time of the offense alleged, the sentencing option was not available and defendant's crime must be governed by the law in effect when it was committed. It rejected defendant's contention that strict scrutiny must be applied as any interest defendant had in his life was curtailed by the procedures set out in the death penalty statute and then determined that the saving clause did not violate defendant's equal protection right as it was rationally related to the state's interest in determining under what circumstances the alternative sentence would be available. Further, there was no requirement that the appellate court compare the sentence of a case before it with the penalty imposed upon others convicted of the same crime or to be imposed in the future.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the death penalty statute did not violate the equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions and reversed the trial court's decision that allowed the jury to consider the alternative sentence of life without parole.

Natural Resources Comm'n v. Amax Coal Co.


No. 49S04-9408-CV-684


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


638 N.E.2d 418; 1994 Ind. LEXIS 95; 39 ERC (BNA) 1358



August 3, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 1, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Anthony J. Metz, III, Judge. Cause No. 49D02-9009-MI-1375. Cause No. 49D01-9008-MI-1286-001. No. 49A04-9112-CV-419


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Natural Resources Commission (commission), the Indiana Department of Natural Resources (department), and a property owner, sought review of a decision by the Court of Appeals for the Fourth District (Indiana), which granted appellee permit applicants' joint motion to consolidate the two cases for appeal and affirmed the trial court's judgment entered in favor of the permit applicants.


OVERVIEW: The permit applicants and the property owner petitioned for transfer to the court. The court granted the petition and vacated the judgment of the court of appeals. The court concluded that the department did have the express statutory authority to regulate and to control surface coal mining, including a surface coal mine operator's use of ground water. The court held that the department was acting within its statutory authority when ordering the permit applicants to revise its permits. The court recognized the restriction on the doctrine of absolute use of ground water. The department's actions were done pursuant to the enforcement of the Indiana Surface Mining Control and Reclamation Act, Ind. Code § 13-4.1. The court also held that such controls were within the realm of the state's police power, which was generally exercised to protect the health, safety, and welfare of the general populace. Because this was a legitimate exercise of the police power, the court found that the department's action constituted a public use in compliance with public use component of the Fifth Amendment Takings Clause. The department' action in both of the cases was valid and in accordance with law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment that was entered in favor of the permit applicants.

Pilarski v. State


No. 79S00-9212-CR-956


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


635 N.E.2d 166; 1994 Ind. LEXIS 66



June 8, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE SUPERIOR COURT I. The Honorable Donald C. Johnson, Judge. Cause No. 79D01-9204-CF-33.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Tippecanoe Superior Court (Indiana), which sentenced him to a term of 60 years following a jury verdict of murder. Defendant argued that the superior court erred when it refused to read his tendered instruction, and when it entered into evidence an inflammatory photograph and his statements obtained after he asserted his right to counsel and to remain silent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly struck a one-year-old girl, who died on her way to the hospital. He was arrested and advised of his Miranda rights. He told the officers that he did not want to talk to them and mumbled something about a lawyer. He was taken into custody and 90 minutes later was again advised of his rights. He then signed a waiver of rights form and gave his statement. He told a detective that he struck the child five or six times in the face because she was moaning and groaning. Defendant argued that the superior court erred when it allowed into evidence the statements that he made to the police. On appeal, the court held that he knowingly and intelligently waived his right to counsel and that his statements were admissible at trial. Defendant claimed the superior court erred by admitting a photograph showing the victim hooked to a life support system with bruises on her face because the photograph was prejudicial and inflammatory. On appeal, the court held that the photograph was illustrative of the nature and extent of the victim's injuries and was admitted properly during the testimony of the doctor who had examined her. The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court, which found defendant guilty of murder.

Walker v. State


No. 20S00-9212-CR-1040


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


632 N.E.2d 723; 1994 Ind. LEXIS 46



April 8, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM ELKHART CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Aldo J. Simpson, Judge. Cause Nos. 5621, 5622, 5623.

Original Opinion of September 28, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Ind. LEXIS 136.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in a trial court (Indiana), of two counts of first-degree murder and of one count of felony murder. Defendant filed a motion for rehearing of the court's prior opinion which disposed of his appeal from the trial court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: The bodies of the two victims, a husband and wife, were discovered. Defendant was arrested based upon information police received from his mother. Defendant was tried upon an indictment that charged three counts of first degree murder under the applicable homicide statute. The first count charged that defendant purposely and with premeditated malice killed the wife. The second count charged that defendant shot the husband while engaged in robbing him, thereby killing him. The third count charged that defendant purposely and with premeditated malice killed the husband. The jury returned separate verdicts of guilty on each of the three counts. In conformity with the then-existing law, the jury stated in each verdict that the punishment was life imprisonment. The trial court sentenced defendant to life imprisonment. On rehearing, the court agreed with defendant that the trial court's instructions employed an unconstitutional presumption aiding the prosecution with regard to the murder with malice counts and thereby denied defendant federal due process because a reasonable jury could have interpreted the instructions as requiring presumption of both purpose and malice.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion for rehearing. The case was remanded to the trial court with instructions to vacate the two convictions for the purposeful and malicious killing of the victims and any sentence thereon. The conviction for the felony murder of the husband was affirmed, and the trial court was instructed to modify the judgment to reflect a single life sentence.

Conner v. State


No. 21S01-9312-CR-1438


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


626 N.E.2d 803; 1993 Ind. LEXIS 213



December 30, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FAYETTE CIRCUIT COURT. No. 21A01-9205-CR-126. The Honorable Daniel L. Pflum, Judge. Cause No. 21C01-9109-CF-088.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Indiana) upholding his conviction for distributing a substance represented to be a controlled substance after he sold a fake substance to a police informant.


OVERVIEW: A sheriff's deputy arranged for an informant to purchase marijuana from defendant. During the transaction, defendant produced 16 small plastic bags of plant material, which he sold to the informant. No traces of marijuana were found in the planted material. Defendant was convicted of distributing a substance represented to be a controlled substance under Ind. Code § 35-48-4-4.6 and was sentenced to six years in prison. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction on appeal, but remanded for resentencing. Defendant filed a petition for transfer. The court granted transfer and affirmed defendant's conviction. However, the court vacated defendant's sentence, holding that defendant's penalty was out of proportion to the nature of his offense. The court reasoned that defendant's sentence was twice as long as the maximum penalty that he would have faced had the planted material contained traces of marijuana. The court concluded that in light of the lesser penalties that attached to marijuana offenses, relative to other controlled substances, the application of § 35-48-4-4.6 violated the constitutional requirement that all penalties be in proportion to the nature of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for distributing a substance represented to be a controlled substance. However, the court vacated defendant's sentence and remanded the case for resentencing.

 

93 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


In re Zumbrun


CAUSE No. 02S00-9304-CQ-422


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


626 N.E.2d 452; 1993 Ind. LEXIS 211



December 29, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE UNITED STATES DISTRICT COURT. NORTHERN DISTRICT OF INDIANA. Cause No. F-92-219.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we hold that Indiana Code § 34-2-28-1(a)(6) as it existed at the time of the Zumbrun bankruptcy was unconstitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States District Court for the Northern District of Indiana certified the question of whether Ind. Code § 34-2-28-1(a)(6) violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 22, by failing to impose any limitation upon the dollar value or amount of the property which could be exempted and/or by failing to contain any requirement that exempted property have a reasonable relation to the needs of a debtor for the support of himself and his family.


OVERVIEW: The bankruptcy petitioners contended that their individual retirement account was protected under Indiana's exemption law, which exempted an interest the judgment debtor had in a pension fund, a retirement fund, an annuity plan, an individual retirement account, or a similar fund, either private or public. The bankruptcy trustee objected to this claim of exemption and contended that Ind. Code § 34-2-28-1(a)(6) violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 22. The court held that Ind. Const. art. I, § 22 commanded the legislature to enact exemptions, that § 22 required statutes which defined the exemptions in reasonably tangible ways so as to balance the interests of lenders and debtors, and that statutes which created unlimited exemptions were inconsistent with the directive of § 22 and the balanced policy underlying it. The court concluded that Ind. Code § 34-2-28-1(a)(6) exempted an unlimited amount of intangible assets from execution to pay legitimate debts, making it possible to closet virtually every liquid asset possessed by a debtor simply through placing the assets in some form of retirement instrument.


OUTCOME: The court held that Ind. Code § 34-2-28-1(a)(6) as it existed at the time of the petitioners' bankruptcy was unconstitutional.

FGS Enters. v. Shimala


Supreme Court No. 75S00-9206-CV-483


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


625 N.E.2d 1226; 1993 Ind. LEXIS 202



December 21, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE STARKE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Marvin D. McLaughlin, Judge. Cause No. 75C01-9004-CP-168



DISPOSITION: The trial court's grant of summary judgment is reversed. This cause is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged a judgment of the Starke Circuit Court (Indiana) for appellee stockholders in their action seeking to have a reverse stock split declared ultra vires and void. The trial court had determined that retroactive restoration of the reservation of powers clause of the Indiana General Corporation Act (Act) years after it was ostensibly repealed was contrary to the Contracts Clause as applied to the instant parties.


OVERVIEW: The reserved powers clause of the Act was ostensibly repealed in 1978. The corporation was formed in 1983, when the Act did not authorize reverse stock splits. In 1986 the clause was purportedly restored, and in 1987 the whole Act was superseded by the Business Corporation Law (BCL), which authorized reverse splits. The corporation then declared the split at issue under Ind. Code § 23-1-38-2(4) and acquired the resulting fractional shares under § 23-1-25-4(a)(1). The stockholders' ownership having thus been eliminated, they filed the instant action to have the split be declared ultra vires and void. The trial court granted the stockholders summary judgment, finding that the repeal of the clause was intentional and that the later attempt to restore the clause was ineffective. Therefore, the clause had not been in effect when the BCL was passed, and its authorization of reverse splits was ineffective as violative of the Contracts Clause, U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10, as applied to the parties. The court reversed, holding that the repeal actually was a clerical error. The clause had thus been in effect the whole time, and the split under the BCL was valid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the stockholders and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings in the stockholders' action to have the reverse stock split declared ultra vires and void.

 

95 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Price v. State


Supreme Court No. 49S02-9311-CR-1197


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


622 N.E.2d 954; 1993 Ind. LEXIS 183



November 1, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION MUNICIPAL COURT. The Honorable William S. Mercuri, Judge. Cause No. 49F04-9101-CM-00199. Court of Appeals No. 49A02-9109-CR-378. On Petition To Transfer.

Original Opinion of September 14, 1992, Reported at: 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 1434.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed a petition to transfer after her convictions in the Marion Municipal Court for public intoxication and disorderly conduct pursuant to Ind. Code Ann. § 35-45-1-3(2) were affirmed. Appellant claimed that the trial court improperly denied her motion to dismiss because Ind. Code Ann. § 35-45-1-3(2) was overbroad and vague in violation of U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV as well as Ind. Const. art. I, § 9.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested for screaming profanities despite being warned to stop. Her conviction was affirmed. The court granted appellant's petition for transfer pursuant to her claims that the disorderly conduct statute was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague. The court reversed and remanded for acquittal appellant's conviction for disorderly conduct, holding that the statute was content-neutral on its face, provided fair notice, and was narrowly tailored to further a significant state interest but could not be applied to the content of appellant's expression. There was no persuasive precedent for application of federal overbreadth analysis to Indiana law. Appellant's screams were political speech, which was enshrined as a core value by Ind. Const. art I § 9. The court concluded that political expression became unreasonably noisy for purposes of Ind. Code Ann. § 35-45-1-3(2) when and only when it inflicted harm warranting tort liability against the speaker. The court found that any harm resulting from appellant's screams was a fleeting annoyance at most. Thus, there was insufficient evidence to establish that she violated the statute.


OUTCOME: The court granted appellant's petition to transfer. It affirmed appellant's conviction for public intoxication but reversed and remanded for acquittal appellant's conviction for disorderly conduct.

Miller v. State


No. 64S00-9012-DP-817


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


623 N.E.2d 403; 1993 Ind. LEXIS 173



October 26, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM PORTER SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Roger V. Bradford, Judge. Cause No. 64D01-9011-CF-181.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Porter Superior Court (Indiana), convicted appellant of murder, criminal confinement, rape, criminal deviate conduct, robbery, and conspiracy to commit murder. Appellant was sentenced to death on the murder charge, to 20 years on the confinement charge, to 50 years on the rape charge, to 50 years on the criminal deviate conduct charge, and to 50 years on the conspiracy charge. Appellant challenged his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimed that the prosecutor made improper comments during closing argument, that the state's capital sentencing structure, Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9, was unconstitutional, that he was denied a fair trial because the voir dire of the jury was conducted in group form, that there was insufficient evidence of conspiracy to commit murder, and that the trial court erred by allowing evidence of prior criminal conduct. The court rejected appellant's contentions. In reaching its decision, the court found that the prosecutor's expression of his personal opinion during closing argument was not improper because he was commenting on the credibility of the evidence and there was no implication that he had access to special information outside the evidence presented to the jury. The court further found that Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9 was not constitutionally infirm, appellant had no absolute right to individual voir dire, ample evidence supported the conspiracy to commit murder conviction, and the State had the right to present evidence to rebut appellant's expert medical testimony that he had no tendency to be sadistic and that there was no indication of profound psychological disturbance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and his sentence.

Campbell v. State


No. 71S03-9310-CR-01157


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


622 N.E.2d 495; 1993 Ind. LEXIS 169



October 25, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM ST. JOSEPH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable R.W. Chamblee, Jr., Judge. Cause No. 71D08-9102-CF-126. No. 71A03-9109-CR-269 in the Court of Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Third District Court of Appeals (Indiana), which affirmed his convictions for burglary in violation of Ind. Code § 35-43-2-1 and battery in violation Ind. Code § 35-42-2-1, but remanded for resentencing.


OVERVIEW: The victim alleged that she was assaulted by defendant, with whom she had a prior relationship and a child. When defendant filed a notice of alibi two days before trial in violation of the notice requirements of Ind. Code § 35-36-4-1, the trial court refused to permit defendant to present any alibi evidence. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the exclusion of defendant's own alibi testimony under the alibi statute was an impermissible infringement upon the defendant's right to testify guaranteed by Ind. Const. art. I, § 13. Where the crucial issue to be resolved was one of credibility, and the defense consisted of the assertion that the victim was mistaken in her identification, depriving defendant of the opportunity to testify as to his whereabouts at the time of the crimes prejudiced defendant's substantial rights. The court further held that because the victim's identification was not inherently unreliable even though uncorroborated, a retrial was appropriate. The court held that evidence of a subsequent burglary at the same address after defendant was arrested should be admitted and that it was not error to admit evidence of defendant's threats against the victim.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's convictions for burglary and assault and remanded for retrial.

The court determined that photographs of the victims' bodies were relevant and were admissible at the trial court's discretion. Affirming, the court held that the jury instructions as a whole did not create an unconstitutional presumption of intent that shifted the burden of proof to defendant.

Marshall v. State


No. 49S00-9108-CR-660


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


621 N.E.2d 308; 1993 Ind. LEXIS 116



August 31, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM MARION COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT CRIMINAL DIVISION, ROOM NO. 1. The Honorable John W. Tranberg, Judge. Cause No. CR81-007A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction in the Marion County Superior Court Criminal Division (Indiana) of two counts of murder, conspiracy, robbery, and nine counts of criminal confinement; and from his sentence of 60 years each on the murder counts to be served concurrently, and 30 years on the robbery count and 10 years for each criminal confinement, all to be served consecutively to the murder sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the state improperly charged him as a principal when its theory was accomplice liability, that the information lacked the specificity required for notice of that accusation, and that the trial court abused its discretion in its written order by sentencing him to consecutive sentences after finding that no aggravating or mitigating circumstances existed with respect to the conspiracy or confinement counts. The trial court held that defendant could be charged as a principal even if the evidence only established that he was an accomplice, and detailed the existence of aggravating circumstances. The court affirmed, finding that defendant was criminally liable for the acts of his confederate and could be held responsible as a principal. Nowhere in the transcript of the hearing did the trial court state that there were no aggravators or mitigators present in reference to the conspiracy or confinement charges. The misstatement was present in the written sentencing order. It was logical that the transcript created by use of notes taken during the proceeding was more accurate. The trial court's proper statement regarding sentencing was located in the transcript.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, conspiracy, robbery, and criminal confinement and his sentence of 60 years each on the murder counts to be served concurrently, and 30 years on the robbery count and 10 years for each criminal confinement, all to be served consecutively to the murder sentences.

Bartrom v. Adjustment Bureau, Inc.


No. 02S04-9307-CV-763


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


618 N.E.2d 1; 1993 Ind. LEXIS 100



July 20, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] No. 02A04-9204-CV-107 in the Court of Appeals. APPEAL FROM THEALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Paul D. Mathias, Judge. Cause No. 02D01-9012-CP-2051.

Original Opinion of October 20, 1992, Reported at: 1992 Ind. App. LEXIS 1588.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee assignee challenged a decision from the court of appeals (Indiana) reversing in favor of appellant ex-wife the summary judgment granted to appellee by the trial court and directing instead that summary judgment be granted to appellant. The court considered the validity of the doctrine of necessaries.


OVERVIEW: Appellee assignee contested the decision of the court of appeals reversing for appellant ex-wife the summary judgment rendered by the trial court for appellee and directing that summary judgment instead be rendered for appellant. The court vacated the court of appeals decisions on both parties' motions for summary judgment. The court remanded the cause for reconsideration according to the opinion. The court of appeals correctly declined to abolish the doctrine of necessaries and reformulated it in a gender-neutral manner. The court of appeals correctly held that each spouse should be primarily liable on the agreements that either of them made individually, if for necessaries. The court of appeals incorrectly ruled based on precedent by utilizing that precedent with an improper approach. The court of appeals decision disregarded the social, economic, and legal factors that made one spouse financially dependent. The court determined that the doctrine was not to impose a mutual obligation and its purpose was to protect dependent spouses to ensure their survival. The court determined that the doctrine incorrectly imposed secondary liability for financial debts on the dependent spouse.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the court of appeals decision challenged by appellee assignee, which reversed for appellant ex-wife the summary judgment entered for appellee by the trial court and ordered instead that summary judgment be entered for appellant. The court remanded the matter for reconsideration. The trial court improperly relied upon precedent that incorrectly determined that the doctrine of necessaries imposed secondary liability on appellee.

Appeal after remand at Azania v. State, 730 N.E.2d 646, 2000 Ind. LEXIS 533 (Ind., 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Vern E. Sheldon, Judge. Cause No. CR-81-401.
Averhart v. Indiana, 471 U.S. 1030, 105 S. Ct. 2051, 85 L. Ed. 2d 323, 1985 U.S. LEXIS 2706, 53 U.S.L.W. 3740 (1985)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Allen Superior Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief from his capital murder conviction and death sentence in which he alleged ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Following an unsuccessful appeal of his murder conviction and death sentence, defendant petitioned for post-conviction relief. On review from the denial of the petition, the court reversed the decision and remanded the case with instructions to set aside the sentence of death and to grant post-conviction relief in the form of a new sentencing hearing or the imposition of a sentence of years. No evidence of mitigating circumstances was presented by defense counsel at the sentencing hearing, defense counsel failed investigate defendant's background, and failed to investigate possible witnesses other than defendant and his mother. The proven existence and availability of proof presented at the post-conviction hearing, which included evidence of defendant's extreme disadvantage and his worthy habits and accomplishments, commanded the conclusion that defense counsel's performance in preparing for and conducting defendant's case at sentencing was deficient, and that the probability that his client would have received a lesser sentence, but for this deficiency was sufficient to undermine confidence in the outcome.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court denying post-conviction relief and remanded the case to grant post-conviction relief in the form of a new death sentence hearing or a sentence of years.

Holmes v. Randolph


No. 29S00-9210-CV-844


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


610 N.E.2d 839; 1993 Ind. LEXIS 40



March 16, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THEHAMILTON CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Judith S. Proffitt, Judge. Cause No. 29C01-8801-CP-29.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff car owner brought a class action against defendant, the commissioner of the Bureau of Motor Vehicles (BMV), alleging that her due process rights were violated when the BMV impounded and sold her car as an abandoned vehicle without affording her actual notice. The Hamilton Circuit Court (Indiana) declared the abandoned vehicle provisions unconstitutional and enjoined their enforcement. The BMV commissioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The car owner went into the hospital for five months. During that time, the BMV impounded and sold her car. The car owner brought a class action against the BMV commissioner, and the trial court declared the abandoned vehicle provisions, Ind. Code § 9-9-1.1 et seq., unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed. The notice provisions of the abandoned vehicle provisions did not violate the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The abandoned vehicle provisions provided two forms of notice, a pre-tow tag left on the car for at least 72 hours and a post-tow letter sent by first class mail. The use of certified mail would not necessarily increase the probability that the addressee would receive the post-tow letter.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision that found the abandoned vehicle laws unconstitutional.

Lockhart v. State


No. 45S00-8911-CR-851


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


609 N.E.2d 1093; 1993 Ind. LEXIS 35



March 8, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James E. Letsinger, Judge. Cause No. 45G02-8806-CF-134.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering a 16-year-old girl. Multiple stab wounds inflicted with a knife left the victim mutilated to the point of being partially eviscerated. The trial court sentenced defendant to death. The aggravating circumstances were intentional murder during the commission of a robbery and a conviction in Texas for murdering a police officer. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. The court held that evidence of the other crime was properly admitted because it was a signature crime that was highly probative of the killer's identity. The court held that it was proper for a pathologist to give an opinion based on the reports of two other doctors. The court found that it was erroneous for the trial judge to have read to the jury on several occasions the list of aggravating circumstances for the death penalty. However, the court held that it was harmless error which did not violate defendant's due process rights. The court held that it was proper to use a non-final Texas murder conviction as an aggravating circumstance because Indiana law and not Texas law determined what qualified as an aggravating circumstance under Ind. Code Ann. § 35-50-2-9(b)(7).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Lyon v. State


No. 79S00-9203-CR-179


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


608 N.E.2d 1368; 1993 Ind. LEXIS 25



February 12, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Ronald E. Melichar, Judge. Cause No. 79C01-9102-CF-4



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Tippecanoe Circuit Court (Indiana) for murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a janitor, was a Korean War veteran who suffered from Prost-Traumatic Stress Disorder. He had a long history of discontent concerning his supervisor, the victim. After his employment was terminated, defendant walked into the victim's office and fatally wounded her. Defendant's claim of insanity was rejected, and he appealed his conviction. Affirming, the court found that both medical experts testified that defendant had the ability to differentiate between right and wrong even though he was suffering from mental disability. Thus, there was ample evidence from which the jury could conclude that although defendant suffered from mental illness, he in fact knew right from wrong and had the capacity to consciously plan to kill the victim. Moreover, Ind. Code § 35-41-4-1(b) did not unconstitutionally shift the burden of proof to defendant on the issue of insanity. The court noted that insanity was an affirmative defense for which defendant had the burden of proof. Finally, there was no error in the trial court's ruling on the burden of proof concerning defendant's insanity defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

Baird v. State

106 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rendleman


No. 37S00-9202-CV-79


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


603 N.E.2d 1333; 1992 Ind. LEXIS 259



November 23, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE JASPER SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable J. Phillip McGraw, Judge. Cause No. 37D01-9004-CT-108



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we reverse the trial court's entry of partial summary judgment, and remand this matter for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff victim filed an action against defendant state for damages sustained in a motor vehicle accident involving plaintiff and a police officer. The Jasper Superior Court (Indiana) granted the victim partial summary judgment after finding that the Tort Claims Act, Ind. Code Ann § 34-4-16.5-3(7) (1992), which granted the state sovereign immunity against such claims, violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 12. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state argued that the Tort Claims Act, Ind. Code Ann § 34-4-16.5-3(7) (1992), did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, § 12. The court agreed and reversed the trial court's entry of partial summary judgment. The court stated that in cases involving injury to person or property, Ind. Const. art. I, § 12 did not prevent the legislature from modifying or restricting common law rights and remedies by granting sovereign immunity for such claims. In tort cases, the source of authority or lack thereof to sue the state originally arose from rights at common law, not from rights contained in the Constitution. Thus, it was within the legislature's authority to expand or restrict the scope of sovereign immunity through the Tort Claims Act. Finally, that the application of sovereign immunity would result in the victim bearing the full economic burden of his injuries and damages without the ability to insure himself against such losses. The court found that it was a matter of policy for the legislature, not for the court to address.


OUTCOME: The trial court's entry of partial summary judgment in favor of the victim was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Bellmore v. State


No. 55S00-8703-CR-328


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


602 N.E.2d 111; 1992 Ind. LEXIS 240



October 29, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 2, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MORGAN CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable James E. Harris, Judge. Cause No. C-85-S-50



DISPOSITION: We affirm the conviction for murder, but reverse the sentence of death and remand to the trial court for a new sentencing determination in accordance with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence from the Morgan Circuit Court (Indiana), which, after a jury found defendant guilty of murder and recommended the death penalty, sentenced defendant to death. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in considering a tattoo as an aggravating circumstance not included under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9(b) (1991).


OVERVIEW: After a jury trial, defendant was convicted of murder for the stabbing and strangulation death of a woman. The trial court accepted the jury's recommendation of the death penalty. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that the voir dire record supported the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for change of venue. The trial court did not err by admitting photographs of the victim to show the nature of her injuries and there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction. The penalty phase did not run afoul of the Due Process Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Defendant did not show that he received ineffective assistance of counsel where only one attorney represented him. The court reversed the sentence of death, holding that the trial court improperly considered defendant's tattoo of a knife with dripping blood, which defendant obtained after the trial, and its implied callousness, audacity, and lack of remorse as an aggravating factor under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9(b) (1991). The court remanded the case to the trial court for a determination, without considering the tattoo as an aggravating circumstance, whether to impose the death sentence or other sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder because there was sufficient evidence of the crime and the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for a change of venue. The court reversed the sentence for death and remanded the case for a new sentencing determination because the trial court erroneously relied on an aggravating factor not available for consideration under Indiana law.

Rouster v. State


No. 45S00-8710-CR-914


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


600 N.E.2d 1342; 1992 Ind. LEXIS 233



October 16, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 1, 1993.
Rehearing denied by, 03/01/1993
Post-conviction relief denied at Rouster v. State, 705 N.E.2d 999, 1999 Ind. LEXIS 66 (Ind., 1999)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Sub nomine at Williams v. State, 706 N.E.2d 149, 1999 Ind. LEXIS 67 (Ind., 1999)
Judgment entered by In re State v. Williams, 2003 Ind. LEXIS 567 (Ind., June 27, 2003)
Judgment entered by State v. Williams, 2004 Ind. LEXIS 474 (Ind., May 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James Letsinger, Judge. Cause No. 2CR-133-886-531



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgment from the Lake County Superior Court (Indiana) convicting them of felony murder under Ind. Code § 35-42-1-1(2) (1986) and sentencing them to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed that they were entitled to separate trials where each accused the other of the victims' murders. The court affirmed the felony murder convictions and death sentences. Defendants waived the right to separate trials where they failed to show their antagonistic defenses before the trial and they failed to raise the issue at the close of the evidence. There was no abuse of discretion in allowing one defendant a rebuttal in closing arguments to counter the other defendant's claim that the first defendant committed the murders where defendants had equal time. The death penalty statute was not unconstitutional under the Eighth Amendment. The state was allowed to raise defendant's participation in an attempted robbery in the penalty phase, though he was not charged with that crime, to disprove the mitigating circumstance that he had not participated in any other significant crimes. The aggravating circumstances to justify the death penalty were proven beyond a reasonable doubt, though one defendant was 18 years old. Though only one defendant committed the murders, the other's conviction and sentence was justified where he acted with reckless indifference to human life.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' felony murder convictions and death sentences.

Gallagher v. Indiana State Election Bd.


No. 49S02-9208-CV-646


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


598 N.E.2d 510; 1992 Ind. LEXIS 201



August 28, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT, Civil Division, Room 1. The Honorable Anthony M. Metz III, Judge. Cause No. 49D01-8810-CP-1489. On Petition to Transfer. No. 49A02-9007-CV-431 in the Court of Appeals.

Original Opinion of October 16, 1991, Reported at 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 1668.



DISPOSITION: The statutes do not violate equal protection guarantees. The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, state and county election boards and others (election boards), petitioned for transfer of a case from the Court of Appeals (Indiana), which reversed a decision of the trial court in favor of the election boards and held that a statute that limited voting rights of those who moved after the registration deadline violated the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Within 30 days of an election, one voter moved outside the county and the other moved to another precinct within the county. The election boards denied both voters the right to vote, except in the election for president and vice president as mandated by federal law. The voters filed a class action suit seeking full franchise. They argued that it was unconstitutional to prohibit those who moved to another county within 30 days of election day from voting while allowing those who moved to another precinct within the same county to vote in all elections provided they filed a timely registration transfer. The trial court upheld the voting statutes. The court of appeals reversed, holding the statutes unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the court of appeals and affirmed the trial court, holding that: (1) Ind. Const. art. II, § 2 required precinct residency for continuous days prior to an election; (2) the court of appeals' use of a strict scrutiny test was erroneous; (3) the appropriate inquiry was whether any state of facts reasonably could be conceived to justify the distinction in voting rights; and (4) viewed under this test, the voting statutes were constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals and affirmed the decision of the trial court in favor of the election boards.

City of Hobart v. Chidester


No. 45S04-9208-CV-610


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


596 N.E.2d 1374; 1992 Ind. LEXIS 195



August 6, 1992, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 4, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable James J. Richard, Special Judge. Cause No. 45D04-8909-CP-00558-0. No. 45A04-9010-CV-487 in the Court of Appeals


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged the Court of Appeals (Indiana), which affirmed the trial court's judgment that was entered in favor of appellee remonstrators, landowners from an annexed area, and that found an annexation ordinance invalid in the remonstrators' complaint against the city's annexation ordinances, which were adopted for the annexation of certain adjacent and contiguous portions of a township.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found for the city on some points but sustained the remonstrance because the city's fiscal plan did not set out which of its areas were similar in topography, patterns of land use, and population density to the annexed area. While there was evidence offered during trial about these comparisons, the trial court felt obliged to decide without such evidence. The lower court affirmed. On appeal, the court held that the effect of filing a remonstrance was to abate the culmination of annexation pending review in the courts, as the burden was on the municipality to sustain annexation by showing that it complied with statutory requirements. Because the city's authority to annex territory was limited by statute, the court's duty was to find whether the city exceeded its authority and met conditions imposed by statute. As to requirements that the city spell out what services it planned to provide to the annexed area, the city was not required to set out in the plan itself comparisons between the city and the annexed territory. A fiscal plan as to annexation needed to be in writing to protect the landowners' right to force the annexing city to provide the services promised.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed those portions of the trial court's findings on much of the remonstrance that were unchallenged on appeal. However, the court vacated that portion of the trial court's ruling about the adequacy of the city's fiscal plan and remanded to the trial court for reconsideration in light of all the evidence.

 

111 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Barco Beverage Corp. v. Indiana Alcoholic Beverage Comm.


No. 49S02-9207-CV-531


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


595 N.E.2d 250; 1992 Ind. LEXIS 183



July 7, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT ROOM 1. The Honorable Anthony J. Metz, Judge. Cause No. S187-1430. Court of Appeals No. 49A02-8809-CV-343

Original Opinion of May 14, 1991, Reported at 1991 Ind. App. LEXIS 784.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, alcoholic beverage brewers and distributors (collectively, brewers), appealed a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Indiana) that affirmed in part a trial court's decision that ruled that defendant, the Indiana Alcoholic Beverage Commission (commission), had authority to promulgate and enforce Ind. Admin. Code tit. 905, r. 1-28-1(3) (rule 28), which placed certain restrictions on the sales of the brewers' products.


OVERVIEW: Rule 28 prohibited distillers, brewers, rectifiers, and vintners from restricting the sale or resale of their alcoholic products to a given geographical area. The brewers brought suit against the commission in an attempt to have Rule 28 declared invalid. The brewers claimed that the rule was an unconstitutional violation of the separation of powers required by Ind. Const. art. 3, § 1. The trial court ruled that the commission did not exceed its authority when it promulgated Rule 28. The appellate court ruled that the commission possessed the authority to promulgate Rule 28 as it related to brewers, vintners, and wholesalers of beer and wine, but did not have the authority to include distillers, rectifiers, and liquor wholesalers within the scope of the rule. The court vacated the decision and ruled that applying principles of administrative law to statutes governing alcoholic beverages resulted in a determination that the legislature's grant of power to the commission was sufficiently comprehensive to grant the commission authority to promulgate and enforce Rule 28 as to distillers, brewers, rectifiers, and vintners and that the rule passed both constitutional and statutory muster.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appellate court's decision and affirmed the trial court's judgment that ruled that the commission had authority to promulgate and enforce the rule that restricted the sale or resale of the brewers' products to a given geographical area.

 

112 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Potts v. State


No. 45S00-8907-CR-536


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


594 N.E.2d 438; 1992 Ind. LEXIS 173



June 23, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM LAKE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Richard Conroy, Judge. Cause No. 3CR-170-1087-676



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lake Superior Court (Indiana) convicted defendant of two counts of murder and three counts of attempted murder. Defendant received the death penalty. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot several people in a bar after he had a heated discussion with his girlfriend. Defendant claimed the trial court erred when it failed to instruct the jury on the lesser-included offense of voluntary manslaughter. The court held that there was no evidence to support such an instruction. There was no evidence that defendant's disagreement with his girlfriend resulted in anything but an exchange of words. The court held that words alone were not sufficient provocation to reduce murder to manslaughter. There was also no evidence of heat of passion. Therefore, the trial court did not err. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred when it failed to properly credit existing mitigating factors that he was a good father and had no significant criminal record. The court held that the mitigating factors did not gainsay the circumstances of defendant's action in perpetrating the crimes. The court held that the trial court thoroughly examined and balanced both the mitigators and aggravators and fully justified the pronounced sentence.


OUTCOME: The trial court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

113 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Morse v. State


No. 82S00-9107-CR-517


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


593 N.E.2d 194; 1992 Ind. LEXIS 162



June 11, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM VANDERBURGH CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Robert S. Matthews, Special Judge. Cause No. 82C01-90-CF-8314


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana) that, following the jury trial, convicted him of dealing in cocaine within 1,000 feet of school property and dealing in a narcotic drug. He received an enhanced sentenced due to his status as a habitual offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was black, appealed from his conviction on drug-related charges. He asserted that the circuit court violated the Equal Protection Clause when it failed to require the prosecution to give racially neutral reasons for its peremptory strike of the only prospective juror who also was black. The court noted that prosecutors were prohibited from challenging potential veniremen solely on the basis of their race. The court held that although defendant showed that he was of the same race as the peremptorily challenged potential venireman, he did not offer any other evidence indicating the prosecutor's purposeful exclusion of the venireman on the basis of race. Therefore, the court concluded, defendant failed to establish a prima facie case of discrimination, and the burden did not shift to the prosecutor to provide a neutral explanation of the reasons for its use of the peremptory challenge. The presumption that the prosecution used its challenge to obtain a fair and impartial jury remained intact. The court also rejected defendant's other claims regarding the chain of custody and the sufficiency of evidence. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of dealing cocaine within 1,000 feet of school property and dealing in a narcotic drug.

 

114 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Scales


No. 82S01-9206-PC-414


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


593 N.E.2d 181; 1992 Ind. LEXIS 160



June 2, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Barbara C. Williams, Special Judge. Cause No. 82D05-9007-CM-9665. On Petition to Transfer. No. 82A01-9012-PC-516 in the Court of Appeals


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent state appealed the decision from the Court of Appeals (Indiana), which remanded the decision from the trial court granting petitioner former criminal defendant's request for post-conviction relief and denying the state's motion to dismiss. The state argued that Ind. R. Crim. P. 5 and Ind. R. Crim. P. 10 created a 10-year statute of limitations to filing post-conviction petitions challenging misdemeanor guilty pleas.


OVERVIEW: The former criminal defendant pled guilty to carrying a handgun without a license. The former criminal defendant did not present any record of the guilty plea in his petition. The trial court granted the petition based on the former criminal defendant's testimony. The lower appellate court held that a petition for post-conviction relief could be filed at any time, but it remanded for findings of fact, which were never entered by the trial court. The state supreme court vacated the trial court and remanded. The criminal rules did not create a statute of limitations. While Ind. R. Crim. P. 10 stated that misdemeanor court records had to be kept for 10 years, the loss of a record after that time did not require the denial of relief since the availability of the original record was only one factor to consider in granting relief. Neither that rule nor Ind. R. Crim. P. 5 created and implied limitations period. Whether relief should have been granted could not be resolved since the former criminal defendant did not adequately show that his record was unavailable or that it could not have been reconstructed and since findings of fact were not entered.


OUTCOME: The granting of the petition for post-conviction relief by the trial court was vacated and remanded for the entrance of findings of fact and conclusions of law. The lower appellate court did properly find that the criminal rules for the maintenance of court records did not create a 10-year statute of limitations for the filing of a petition for post-conviction relief for misdemeanor guilty pleas.

 

115 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Tyson v. State


Supreme Court Cause No. 49S02-9204-CR-311


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


593 N.E.2d 175; 1992 Ind. LEXIS 134



April 24, 1992, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Patricia J. Gifford, Judge. Cause No. 49G04-9109-CF-116245. Court of Appeals Cause No. 49A02-9203-CR-129


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of rape and criminal deviate conduct, sought review of a judgment of the Indiana Court of Appeals that denied his petition for bail pending appeal filed, pursuant to Ind. R. App. P. 6(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant received an executed sentence of six years for his convictions. The trial court denied his request for bail. Thereafter, the lower court denied his petition for bail pending appeal. On appeal, the court provided the courts of Indiana with guidance on the legal criteria governing petitions for bond pending appeal. The court found that a defendant had the burden of demonstrating that there were compelling reasons to allow a guilty defendant to remain free pending appeal of his conviction. In hearing such petitions, the appellate court was required to examine three factors: (1) the probability of reversible error at trial, (2) the risk of flight, and (3) the potential dangerousness of the defendant. The appellate court had to give the trial court appropriate deference, however, on those issues which the trial court was in the best position to judge. A defendant had to show that there was a likelihood that his conviction would be reversed on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court refused to overrule the lower court's judgment that denied defendant's petition for bail pending appeal.

 

116 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Platt v. State


No. 92S03-9203-CR-195


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


589 N.E.2d 222; 1992 Ind. LEXIS 120



March 24, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE WHITLEY SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Patricia McNagny, Judge. Cause No. 92D01-8905-CM-264. On Petition To Transfer. No. 92A03-9004-CR-146 in the Court of Appeals



DISPOSITION: We vacate the decision of the Court of Appeals and affirm the judgment of the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state petitioned to transfer the decision from the Court of Appeals (Indiana) that reversed defendant's conviction for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, and operating a motor vehicle with a blood alcohol content (BAC) of .10 percent or more pursuant to Ind. Code §§ 9-11-2-2, 9-11-2-1 because it held that an investigative stop of defendant's car was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, and operating a motor vehicle with a BAC of .10 percent or more pursuant to Ind. Code §§ 9-11-2-2, 9-11-2-1. The appellate court reversed, holding that an investigative stop of defendant's car was unconstitutional and the trial court had erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress the evidence. Plaintiff state sought transfer. The court reversed and reinstated the trial court's judgment. It noted that the facts known to the police officer at the time he stopped defendant's car were sufficient to warrant a man of reasonable caution in the belief that an investigation was appropriate. Defendant had been parked on the wrong side of the road, had taken flight when the officer had appeared, and the subsequent breathalyzer test showed that defendant had a BAC of .17 percent. There was substantial evidence of probative value to support the jury's conclusion that the defendant was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision of the appellate court and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

117 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Griffin v. Munco Assoc.


Supreme Court No. 29S00-8912-CV-923


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


589 N.E.2d 220; 1992 Ind. LEXIS 119



March 23, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE HAMILTON SUPERIOR COURT NO. 3. The Honorable William J. Hughes, Judge. Cause No. 29D03-8808-CP-57



DISPOSITION: We, therefore, reverse the entry of summary judgment and remand this case to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tax sale purchaser appealed an order from the Hamilton Superior Court No. 3 (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of certain mortgagees, thus invalidating a tax sale and tax sale deed issued defendant county auditor.


OVERVIEW: After taxes on certain commercial property fell delinquent, the county auditor mailed a notice to the property owner of record at its last known address. Although Ind. Code § 6-1.1-24-4.2 provided that any mortgagee or other interested party who wished to receive notices of delinquency and tax sale of property could do so by filing a request with the auditor's office and payment of a prescribed fee, neither one of the two mortgagees had done so. The property was sold at tax sale and two years later, the auditor mailed a notice of redemption to the property owner. Soon afterwards, the purchaser received a tax deed to the property that was recorded seven days later. Eighteen months later, the trial court entered summary judgment in favor of two mortgagees, invalidating the tax sale on the grounds that failure to notify the mortgagees of the tax sale was an unconstitutional deprivation of their due process rights. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the tax sale and tax deed were valid because the mortgagees, or any other interested party, could have received notice under § 6-1.1-24-4.2 and such a scheme satisfied the requirements of constitutional due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the entry of summary judgment in favor of the mortgagees and remanded the case, holding that the tax sale and tax deed were valid.

 

118 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Elizondo v. Read


Supreme Court No. 50S04-9203-CV-189


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


588 N.E.2d 501; 1992 Ind. LEXIS 122



March 23, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARSHALL CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Michael D. Cook, Judge. Cause No. 50C01-8710-CP-233. Court of Appeals No. 50A04-8902-CV-50

Original Opinion of July 18, 1990, Reported at 1990 Ind. App. LEXIS 861.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we grant transfer, vacate the opinion of the Court of Appeals, and reinstate the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of Thomas and Jacqueline Read and the Marshall County Auditor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, buyer and auditor, challenged a finding by the Court of Appeals (Indiana), that notice was constitutionally deficient to appellee owner prior to a tax sale, where the owner had not given the auditor his new address, but the address was available in the auditor's office on other documents.


OVERVIEW: Owners of a piece of property moved several times without notifying the auditor's office of their new address. Thus, all correspondence regarding taxes were returned. The auditor did have the owners' new address on other documents in his office and the new address was in the telephone directory. After all notices were returned, the property was sold at a tax sale to a buyer. The owner filed suit against the buyer and the auditor, alleging that notice was constitutionally deficient. The auditor and the buyer filed motions for summary judgment, which were granted. The owners challenged those rulings in the appellate court, which reversed, thereby invalidating the tax sale. The buyer and the auditor sought further review. The court found that the auditor was charged with knowledge of all information in his office. However, he had no way to know whether the owner was the same person listed at different addresses. Thus, the auditor fulfilled his obligations. Notice therefore was not constitutionally deficient. The court of appeals was reversed and the summary judgments were reinstated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals and reinstated the summary judgments granted the auditor and buyer in the trial court.
