Metro Holding Co. v. Mitchell


NO. 49S02-9203-CV-182


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


589 N.E.2d 217; 1992 Ind. LEXIS 88



March 19, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Honorable James S. Kirsch, Judge. Marion Superior Court 5. No. 59D05-8906-CP-846. Appeal from the Honorable William R. Fatout, Judge Pro Tem, Marion Superior Court 6. No. 49A04-9008-CV-380. Court of Appeals No. 49A02-9004-CV-207. Court of Appeals No. 49A04-9008-CV-380.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, plaintiff sought review of the order of the appellate court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant in plaintiff's quiet title action against defendant, and defendant sought review of the judgment of the same court in a different action which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff in plaintiff's quiet title action against that defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff holding company bought property at two tax sales. At that time, Ind. Code § 6-1.1-25-4 provided that a property owner whose property had been subjected to a tax sale could redeem that property during a two year period beginning on the date that the tax certificate was issued. Two months after the tax certificates were issued, amendments to the statute became effective, which reduced the redemption period to one year. The company filed quiet title actions against defendants, the former owners of the properties. In one suit, summary judgment in favor of owner was granted on the ground that application of the amendment to § 6-1.1-25-4 was unconstitutional. In the other, the trial court granted summary judgment in the company's favor finding the one-year period controlled. The court of appeals reversed both judgments, and both cases were appealed. The cases were consolidated, and the court held that although the amendment's reduction of the period of redemption did not unconstitutionally infringe upon the right of contract, application of that period in the instant cases represented an improper retroactive application of law. Both cases were remanded to the trial courts.


OUTCOME: Judgments of the appellate court were remanded to the trial court where application of the amendment to the statutory period of redemption to tax sales in which plaintiff purchased property from defendants was improper.

O'Laughlin v. Barton


NO. 82S01-9002-CV-131 Supreme Court


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


582 N.E.2d 817; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 244



December 12, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied February 14, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM VANDERBURGH CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Robert S. Matthews, Special Judge

Original Opinion of May 30, 1991, Reported at 1991 Ind. LEXIS 96.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state treasurer filed a petition for a rehearing in an appeal from a decision by the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana), which ordered that funds on deposit with the court clerk be paid to appellee victim, rather than forfeited to the state treasury.


OVERVIEW: In 1987, a criminal defendant charged with battery and attempted murder deposited $ 100,000 cash in lieu of bail and was released. Defendant never appeared for trial and his "bond" was revoked. Shortly thereafter, the victim filed a civil action against defendant. He failed to appear for that trial, and the victim was awarded damages. The victim attempted to execute the judgment by garnishing the revoked cash bond. The trial court ordered the bond released to the victim. The state treasurer sought review. In 1990, the court reversed the judgment and ordered the bond forfeited to the state. The victim filed a petition for a rehearing, during the pendency of which a statute was enacted that required the payment of a criminal defendant's deposit to the victim in the event the victim won a judgment against the defendant. The court denied the petition. The victim filed a motion in the criminal court to recover the cash deposit, which was granted. The treasurer sought review and the court affirmed. The court found that the victim's award did not constitute a retroactive use of the statute because the victim's motion for the funds was not filed until after the statute's effective date.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition for a rehearing and affirmed the trial court's judgment, which ordered that funds on deposit with the court clerk be paid to the victim, rather than to the state treasurer.

McCollum v. State


No. 79S00-9104-CR-296


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


582 N.E.2d 804; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 246



December 12, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 6, 1992.
Rehearing denied by, 05/06/1992
Post-conviction relief denied at McCollum v. State, 678 N.E.2d 1297, 1997 Ind. App. LEXIS 443 (Ind. Ct. App., 1997)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at McCollum v. State, 2009 Ind. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1663 (Ind. Ct. App., Oct. 6, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TIPPECANOE SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Kenneth L. Thayer, Judge. Cause No. 79D02-8704-CF-5547


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the Tippecanoe Superior Court (Indiana) for dealing in cocaine and for conspiracy and also challenged the total 110-year sentence that was imposed. Defendant argued that his constitutional rights were violated, that drug evidence was improperly admitted, that the evidence was insufficient to support the habitual offender determination, and that his sentence was incorrectly enhanced and excessive.


OVERVIEW: The evidence against defendant included testimony from drug offenders who cooperated in exchange for leniency. The court held that: (1) counsel's failure to call witnesses whose testimony had little value and to object on all possible grounds to damaging evidence was not ineffective assistance; (2) a non-custodial recording of a conversation between defendant and an informant witness was probative to show that defendant was the witness's dealer; (3) the absence of an evidence technician's name and testimony did not create a gap in the chain of custody relating to drug evidence; (4) the scope of cross-examination was not improperly limited, as the information defendant sought to elicit was not relevant to show bias; (5) the comment on defendant's post-arrest silence was harmless, as it was not used to prove guilt and was stricken; (6) it was irrelevant that the crime used to support the habitual offender determination was no longer considered a felony or that only a one-year sentence was imposed for its commission; (7) the sentence was not excessive in view of the current and prior offenses; and (8) the enhanced sentence was supported by specific aggravating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The judgment that convicted defendant of two counts of dealing in cocaine and two related conspiracy counts was affirmed. The 110-year enhanced sentence imposed upon defendant was also affirmed.

Daniel v. State


No. 49S00-8812-CR-982


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


582 N.E.2d 364; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 249



December 10, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied February 14, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION COUNTY SUPERIOR COURT CRIMINAL DIVISION, ROOM NO. 2. The Honorable Webster Brewer, Judge. Cause No. CR87-185B


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of burglary, a Class A felony. The Marion County Superior Court Criminal Division (Indiana) sentenced him to 20 years imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury and sentenced to imprisonment. An assistant band director at a high school went to the school for a meeting on a Sunday morning. When he arrived, he noticed light coming from an open classroom door. He stopped to say hello and saw defendant sitting on a table. Defendant produced a pistol and fired at the teacher but the gun misfired. The teacher ran away, and defendant chased him, shot him in the chin, and hit him with a claw hammer on the back of his head. It was discovered that several rooms in the school had been ransacked. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in granting the State's motion to waive him from juvenile court to stand trial as an adult. 124 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Clem v. Christole, Inc.


Supreme Court No. 53S04-9112-CV-950


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


582 N.E.2d 780; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 232



December 4, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MONROE SUPERIOR COURT, DIVISION III. The Honorable John G. Baker, Judge and APPEAL FROM THE MADISON SUPERIOR COURT, III. The Honorable Robert L. Barnet, Special Judge ON JOINT PETITION TO TRANSFER.

Consolidated Court of Appeals No. 53A04-8712-CV-393


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners filed actions against appellee developers alleging that the developers' group homes for disabled persons violated certain restrictive covenants. The trial court granted the developers' motion for summary judgment, holding that Ind. Code § 16-13-21-14(a) (1988) prohibited enforcement of such restricted covenants. The Court of Appeals (Indiana) reversed the trial court's order, and the developers petitioned for transfer.


OVERVIEW: The primary issue before the court was whether retroactive application of § 16-13-21-14(a) violated the contract clause in Ind. Const. art. 1, § 24. The court ruled that the retroactive application of a statute to a contract entered into before the effective date of the statute could have withstood scrutiny under the contract clause only if it was necessary for the general public and reasonable under the circumstances. Applying that standard, the court held that the legislative justification for § 16-13-21-14(a) did not fall within the necessary police power exception to the contract clause because it was not reasonably necessary for the protection of the health, safety, and welfare of the general public, and did not address a broad problem general to society. Moreover, the statute's effect was permanent, irrevocable, and retroactive in altering the contractual relationships created in restriction covenants, and it imposed statutory regulation in a field not traditionally subject to legislation. The court held that in seeking to alter the enforceability of restrictive covenants, the statute represented a considerable impairment of contractual obligations.


OUTCOME: The court granted the developers' petition for transfer, and reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the developers. The case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Conner v. State


No. 49S00-8904-CR-00314


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


580 N.E.2d 214; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 197



October 24, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Conner v. Indiana, 503 U.S. 946, 117 L. Ed. 2d 640, 112 S. Ct. 1501, 1992 U.S. LEXIS 1867 (1992)
Post-conviction relief denied at Conner v. State, 711 N.E.2d 1238, 1999 Ind. LEXIS 344 (Ind., 1999)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Conner v. Anderson, 259 F. Supp. 2d 741, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 3036 (S.D. Ind., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division, Room One; The Honorable John W. Tranberg, Judge; Cause No. 49G91-8801-CF-8449.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division, Room One (Indiana) that convicted him of three counts of murder following a jury trial. The jury recommended that he suffer the penalty of death for the murders. The trial court accepted the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death for two of the three murders.


OVERVIEW: During a time span of several hours, defendant killed three of his acquaintances. On appeal from his convictions for the murder, defendant contended that 15 errors occurred in connection with his murder trial. The court reviewed the transcript in light of the alleged errors and affirmed defendant's convictions for murder and sentence of death. The court rejected defendant's five arguments that the Indiana death penalty statute was unconstitutional. Defendant's challenges to evidentiary rulings and to the sufficiency of the evidence were also rejected. The court determined that defendant's confession and its corroboration clearly showed sufficient evidence to support convictions for each of the three murders charged. After reviewing the record of the penalty phase of the trial as well as the trial court's sentencing order, the court held that the trial court properly considered both aggravating and mitigating circumstances and properly imposed the death penalty in accordance with Indiana law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder. The court also affirmed the sentence of execution imposed by the trial court against defendant.

Holderfield v. State


No. 49S00-9006-CR-389


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


578 N.E.2d 661; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 185



September 30, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 21, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Marion County Superior Court; Criminal Division Room No. VI; The Honorable Monica Foster, Special Judge; Cause No. 49G00-8904-CF-040140.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment entered by the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division (Indiana), which convicted him of the offenses of rape, a Class A felony, and confinement, a Class B felony, after a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: The victim was carrying empty bottles to a storage shed that was located behind her place of employment. Defendant grabbed the victim at knifepoint, shoved her into the shed, and proceeded to rape her. Thereafter, she selected defendant's picture from a photographic array. Defendant filed a notice of alibi. He subsequently filed a second notice, which referred to a different witness than the first one. One month later, he filed a third notice, which mentioned the same witness as the first notice. At trial, the State introduced the notices as rebuttal evidence attacking the credibility of defendant's alibi witness. A jury found him guilty of rape and confinement. The trial court entered a judgment to that effect. On appeal, that judgment was affirmed. The court stated that the alibi notices could be used to attack the alibi witness's credibility. Moreover, their admission did not interfere with defendant's self-incrimination privilege and did not impermissibly call attention to that fact that he had not testified. The court also found that the evidence warranted convictions for both rape and confinement and the imposition of consecutive sentences.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

127 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


In re Tina T.


Nos. 49S00-9008-JV-576, 49S00-9001-CV-11


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


579 N.E.2d 48; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 187



September 30, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Marion Superior Court, Juvenile Division; The Honorable James W. Payne, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee juvenile wards brought suit against appellant state seeking injunctive relief, declaratory relief, and class certification. The Marion Superior Court, Juvenile Division, certified appellees as a class and determined that Ind. Code Ann. §31-6-14-1 violated the Indiana Constitution and the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution. State appealed.


OVERVIEW: State argued that since juvenile wards were no longer under the age of 18, the appeal was moot. The court determined that although the state could not have enforced the provisions of Ind. Code. Ann. § 31-6-14-1 against the named class members, the statute would certainly be enforced against members of the class that they sought to represent. Therefore, the case was not moot. Juvenile wards argued that the challenged statute violated the separation of powers clause of the Indiana Constitution. The court found that the presence of one member of the executive branch of government on a multi-member committee that served an advisory role to the judicial branch, did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. The court concluded that the statute did not impose an unconstitutional delay in contravention of the speedy trial clause of the Indiana Constitution. Furthermore, the court held that a stay in an interim house pending the determination of the best permanent placement of juvenile wards did not compromise the child's constitutional right to due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

 

128 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Kennedy v. State


Supreme Court No. 16S00-8808-CR-785


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


578 N.E.2d 633; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 166



September 19, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Decatur Circuit Court, The Honorable John A. Westhafer, Judge; Cause No. 16C01-8704-CF-45.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Decatur Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of murder, felony murder, kidnapping, and robbery. Defendant also challenged the trial judge's decision to sentence him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was implicated in a robbery, as well as the kidnapping and murder of a woman. Defendant's girlfriend gave the police permission to search her gym bag, which was being used by defendant. Defendant was convicted, but the jury recommended that the death penalty not be imposed. The trial judge determined that the death penalty was appropriate and defendant sought review. The court affirmed the convictions, but reversed and remanded the case for re-sentencing. The trial judge did not use the proper standard in overriding the jury's recommendation and sentencing defendant to death. The search was not invalid because the police had a reasonable belief that defendant's girlfriend had the authority to consent to a search of the bag. Forensic evidence was admissible where the state established a "reasonable assurance" that the evidence passed through various hands in an undisturbed condition. The state was not required to establish a perfect chain of custody. Defendant was not denied a meaningful access to justice by the trial court's denial of his motion to retain an expert. Finally, the court held that photographs admitted in the case were not unduly prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, but reversed the sentence of death. The case was remanded to the trial court.

Benefiel v. State


No. 84S00-8906-CR-483


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


578 N.E.2d 338; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 164



September 18, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Vigo Superior Court, Division I; The Honorable Michael H. Eldred, Judge; Cause No. 84D01-8705-CF-34.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Vigo Superior Court (Indiana) convicted defendant of criminal confinement, rape, criminal deviate conduct, and murder. The defendant was sentenced to death. The defendant brought an appeal.


OVERVIEW: The defendant contended that the trial court erred in refusing to quash search warrants, and that certain evidence that was obtained was inadmissible as fruits of the illegal searches. The court agreed with the defendant that the affidavits presented to the trial judge contained secondhand hearsay information, and that they were insufficient as far as a search for property was concerned. However, the court held that the policy reasons established for the exclusionary rule did not apply. The court held that one of the well-recognized exceptions to the warrant requirement was an entry under emergency circumstances involving injury or imminent danger to a person's life for the purpose of preventing further injury or aiding those injured. The court held that the danger to the victim certainly outweighed the defendant's reasonable expectations to privacy. The court rejected the defendant's contention that the trial court erred in failing to find him incompetent before or during trial, holding that the trial court's determination that the defendant was competent to stand trial was supported by the record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Neudecker v. Neudecker

131 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Brady v. State


No. 71S03-9106-CR-498


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


575 N.E.2d 981; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 128



June 28, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from St. Joseph Superior Court; The Honorable Jerome Frese, Judge; No. 71A03-8809-CR-266 Court of Appeals.

Original Opinion of June 21, 1989, Reported at 540 N.E.2d 59, 1989 Ind.App. LEXIS 475.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Indiana), which affirmed defendant's conviction for child molesting, a Class C felony, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-42-4-3(b), and his subsequent seven-year sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that Ind. Code § 35-37-4-8, which authorized the use of videotaped testimony of child witnesses at trial, was unconstitutional. The court agreed and reversed defendant's conviction. The court held that that statute was constitutional under the federal constitution. The statute satisfied the requirements of the federal confrontation right. However, the court held that the statute was not constitutional under the Indiana constitution. Ind. Const. art. I, § 13 provided that in all criminal prosecutions, the accused had the right to have met the witnesses face to face. The court determined that Indiana's confrontation right therefore contained both the right of cross-examination and the right to have met the witnesses face to face. Therefore, the statute infringed upon defendant's right to confront the witness against him face to face and the videotaped testimony was erroneously admitted into evidence. The court finally held that there was no double jeopardy restraint in retrying defendant because the evidence was sufficient.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for child molesting and remanded the matter back to the trial court for retrial.

Bayh v. Sonnenburg


No. 37S03-9106-CV-437


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


573 N.E.2d 398; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 113; 121 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P56,880



June 12, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 17, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Jasper Circuit Court; The Honorable William W. Andersen, Jr., Special Judge; Cause No. C-44-88; On Petition to Transfer. No. 37A03-8801-CV-4 in the Court of Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State challenged the decision of the Jasper Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered judgment for plaintiffs, state mental patients, for work they performed while confined in state mental hospitals. Patients' claims were based on 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, Ind. Code §§ 16-12-12.8 1 to -10, the Fair Labor Standards Act (FLSA), unjust enrichment, the Thirteenth Amendment, and Ind. Const. art. I, § 21.


OVERVIEW: After the appellate court affirmed patients' judgment under Ind. Const. art. I, § 21, the State appealed. The court reversed and held that the judgment could not be affirmed on any grounds. The court held that: 1) neither the State, nor its officers in their official capacities, were "persons" under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983; 2) patients' had no right under Indiana's patient remuneration law because the pay schedule never became "effective" pursuant to 1971 Ind. Acts 2124, 2126 (Pub. L. No. 474, § 3(d)) and 1972 Ind. Acts 10, 12 (Pub. L. No. 3, § 3(d)); 3) the State was not liable with respect to the maximum hours provision of 29 U.S.C.S. § 207; 4) the United States Supreme Court's Garcia decision did not apply retroactively to hold the State liable for its failure to pay minimum wage; 5) patents' claims for unjust enrichment failed because they did not expect to be paid; 6) although patients' could bring a claim directly under the Thirteenth Amendment, the work they performed fit squarely within the "civic duty" exception; and, 7) the services performed were not "particular services" within the meaning of Ind. Const. art. I, § 21 and patients were not denied "just compensation."


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and appellate court with instructions to enter judgment for the State on all counts.

O'Laughlin v. Barton

SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


571 N.E.2d 1258; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 96



 May 30, 1991, Filed

DISPOSITION: The trial court is reversed. CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a state treasurer, sought review of a judgment from the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana) entered in favor of appellee, an injury victim, in the injury victim's action that sought to have a forfeited cash bond paid to her in satisfaction of a judgment.


OVERVIEW: A criminal defendant was charged with the battery of the injury victim. The criminal defendant was released on a $ 100,000 cash bond which was ultimately forfeited. The injury victim filed a civil action against the criminal defendant and she obtained a substantial verdict. The trial court ultimately entered an order ordering the cash bond paid to the injury victim. The state treasurer's appeal from the trial court's order was dismissed and the court in an earlier decision reversed the trial court's decision, and ordered that the funds be transmitted to the state treasurer. L. No. 36-1990 retroactively and improperly considered four affidavits by members of the legislature. The language of the bill was unambiguous and did not mention retroactive application. The affidavits did not explain any ambiguities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the matter to the trial court with directions to enter an order that directed the cash bond transmitted to the state treasurer.

Indiana Dep't of State Revenue v. Felix


Nos. 49S00-8905-CV-388, 49S02-8906-CV-499


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


571 N.E.2d 287; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 81



 May 16, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court; Consolidated Cause No. S186-0406; The Honorable Anthony J. Metz, III, Judge.

Appeal from the Marion Circuit Court; Cause No. C85-0801; The Honorable John M. Ryan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed in part and reversed in part. We remand this case to the trial court with instructions to enter summary judgment in favor of the defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee taxpayers brought actions against appellant Indiana Department of State Revenue (department) challenging the constitutionality of Indiana's intangibles tax, asserting the tax violated U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3 and the uniform taxation provisions of Ind. Const. art. 10, § 1. The department sought review of the order of the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana), which held the tax unconstitutional under federal and state constitutions.


OVERVIEW: In a consolidated case, the court certified the class, but denied a motion for an escrow account to hold taxes collected. Subsequently, the legislature repealed the intangibles tax retroactively. The court found that the recently-repealed intangibles tax did not violate the Commerce Clause under the substantial equivalent test, because it required all property, foreign or domestic, to contribute a pro rata share of taxes so far as practicable to avoid double taxation. The legislature could discriminate within the intangible personal property tax class consistently with the uniformity requirement of Ind. Const. art. 10, § 1. Although Commerce Clause violations were cognizable under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, defendants were granted summary judgment on the § 1983 claim because states and state officials acting in their official capacities are not persons under § 1983. The retroactive refund of the intangibles tax and class certification claims were mooted by the determination that the intangibles tax did not violate the Commerce Clause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that held the intangibles tax unconstitutional, finding that it did not violate the Commerce Clause and it satisfied the uniformity requirement of the state constitution. The court denied class certification and retroactive refunds. Further, the court found that no claims existed under § 1983. The court remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to enter summary judgment in favor of the department.

Supreme Court No. 64S00-8807-CR-00643


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


569 N.E.2d 952; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 69

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Porter Superior Court (Indiana) of attempted criminal deviate conduct, a Class B felony, battery, a Class A misdemeanor, and battery, a Class B misdemeanor, and resulting sentence of 18 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was detained while riding his bicycle by police, after two teenage girls reported that a man on a bicycle had grabbed them and tried to force one of them to perform a sexual act. While defendant was standing with officers and his bicycle, the girls, who were brought to the scene by other officers, identified him as their attacker. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for attempted criminal deviate conduct and two counts of battery, and resulting 18-year sentence.

SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


567 N.E.2d 803; 1991 Ind. LEXIS 40



March 13, 1991, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Lake County Superior Court; Criminal Division; The Honorable T. Edward Page, Judge Pro Tempore; Cause No. 1CR-17-175-75.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Lake Superior Court, Criminal Division (Indiana), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief from his conviction for murder in the perpetration of a robbery upon a guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: After studying a pending U.S. Supreme Court case and the Indiana death penalty statute, defendant's original trial counsel advised him to accept the prosecution's plea agreement if he wished to avoid the death penalty. Defendant pled guilty to murder in the perpetration of a robbery. Some 10 years later, defendant filed a post-conviction relief petition. The trial court granted the prosecution a continuance to pursuit the defense of laches. Thereafter, defendant's petition was denied. The court noted that trial counsel had no way of predicting the outcome of pending cases. The court would not speculate as to what might have been the most advantageous strategy. Defendant failed to show ineffective representation by trial counsel. Further, the court found no error in permitting the prosecution to present laches. Moreover, the trial court was justified in finding that given the passage of time, the absence of certain witnesses, and the possibility of a known codefendant recanting his prior statement, the prosecution was in a poor position to reprosecute defendant. Finally, the record did not disclose actual bias and prejudice of the post-conviction judge against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

Flinn v. State


No. 49S00-8805-CF-507


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


563 N.E.2d 536; 1990 Ind. LEXIS 240



November 27, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at Flinn v. Knight, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 116768 (S.D. Ind., Sept. 6, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Marion County Superior Court; Criminal Division, Room Three; The Honorable John R. Barney, Judge; Cause No. CR86-19C.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision by the Marion County Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of one count of corrupt business influence, a Class C felony, seven counts of theft, a Class D felony, and three counts of unlawful loan brokering, a Class D felony. Defendant was sentenced to enhanced terms of 8 years for the Class C felony count and 4 years for each of the 10 Class D felony counts, all terms to be served consecutively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motions to dismiss the corrupt business influence and unlawful loan brokering counts, that his sentence totaling 48 years, representing the maximum possible term for his convictions, was unjustifiably severe, and that the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions. The trial court properly denied defendant's motions to dismiss the counts of corrupt business influence and unlawful loan brokering. The court determined that the trial court did not err in imposing defendant's sentence because the history and scope of defendant's criminal activities revealed little chance for rehabilitation such that the maximum sentence was called for in order to prevent recurrence of his activities. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to prove the "unauthorized control" element of theft under Ind. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant convictions for one count of corrupt business influence, seven counts of theft, and three counts of unlawful loan brokering.

First Nat'l Bank v. Gabonay


No. 20S04-9011-CV-724


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


562 N.E.2d 719; 1990 Ind. LEXIS 228



November 13, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Elkhart Superior Court; The Honorable Worth N. Yoder, Judge; Cause No. 20D03-8712-CP-200; On Petition To Transfer; No. 20A04-8904-CV-147 in the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: The opinion of the Court of Appeals is vacated. We affirm the judgment of the trial court in part and reverse in part. We remand with instructions to enter summary judgment for the employees as to both real and personal property.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Elkhart Superior Court (Indiana), entered in judgment in favor of appellee company employees and held that, pursuant to Ind. Code § 22-2-10-1, the company employees, who were owed wages form the company, had a limited preferred debt that took priority over appellant bank's mortgage on company real estate and its security interest in accounts receivable and other personal property. The bank appealed.


OVERVIEW: The bank held a mortgage on the company's real estate and a security interest in the company's accounts receivable, personal property, and after-acquired assets. The bank seized all assets of the company under the terms of the mortgage and security agreements, and the company ceased to operate. Pursuant to Ind. Code § 22-2-10-1, the company employees filed a complaint demanding payment from the bank for wages and fringe benefit contributions. The trial court held that the bank's liens based on the real estate mortgage took priority over the employees' claims, but that the employees' claims took preference over the bank's seized security interest in the personal property. The intermediate appellate court reversed, holding that the bank's mortgage and its security interests took priority over the employees' claims. On further appeal, the court vacated the intermediate appellate court's judgment and affirmed in part and reversed in part the trial court's judgment. According to the court, pursuant to the clear intent of § 22-2-10-1, the employees had first priority, limited only by time and amount, to the proceeds of the defunct company.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the intermediate appellate court's judgment and affirmed the judgment of the trial court in part and reversed in part. The court directed that summary judgment be entered for the employees.

 

141 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Kellogg v. Gary


Supreme Court No. 45S03-9011-CV-710


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


562 N.E.2d 685; 1990 Ind. LEXIS 226



November 8, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Lake County Superior Court Civil Division, Room Three; The Honorable James Danikolas, Presiding Judge; Cause No. 380-163; Court of Appeals Number 3-983 A 291.

Original Opinion of February 17, 1988, Reported at 1988 Ind. App. LEXIS 248.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a class of citizens, filed an action against defendants, city, officials, and state police superintendent, for violations of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the Indiana Firearms Act, codified at Ind. Code § 35-47-2-3, by denying citizens handgun application forms. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the citizens. The Third District Court of Appeals (Indiana) reversed. The citizens petitioned to transfer.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found the failure of the citizens to wait until their claim had been denied before bringing suit against the city violated § 12 of the Indiana Tort Claims Act, codified at Ind. Code § 34-4-16.5-12. The court held that states could not apply such an outcome-determinative law when entertaining substantive federal rights. The citizens had a cause of action for damages pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the city and its officials were not immune from suit. The evidence demonstrated arbitrary and wrongful government action and an abuse of power. City officials exceeded their authority when they suspended the handgun license application process by mayoral decree with no pre-deprivation hearing. The citizens were deprived of a federally protected, state created, substantive right to carry a handgun with a license when the application process was terminated. After trial, the city's policy was to distribute the handgun license applications, but to systematically recommend them for denial. That delay did not constitute a deprivation of a liberty or property interest without due process, but was an aggravating circumstance sufficient to warrant punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The court granted transfer, vacated the order of the appellate court, and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings. The court held that the trial court erred when it certified the class, and the court reversed and modified the compensatory and punitive damages awarded to the class of citizens. The court affirmed the award of attorney's fees to the citizens, with modifications.

In re Public Law No. 154-1990


Cause No. 49S00-9006-OR-388


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


561 N.E.2d 791; 1990 Ind. LEXIS 210



November 2, 1990, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney brought a declaratory action to determine whether the Attorney Trust Account Act, Pub. L. No. 154-1990, §§ 15-24 (as codified at Ind. Code §§ 33-20-1-1 to 33-20-9-2), which contained a provision that shielded attorneys from disciplinary action for participation in a statutory attorney trust account program, did not contravene Ind. Const. art. III, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The Indiana legislature enacted the Attorney Trust Account Act, Pub. L. No. 154-1990, §§ 15-24 (as codified at Ind. Code §§ 33-20-1-1 to 33-20-9-2). A portion of the act, Ind. Code § 33-20-2-1, provided absolute immunity to attorneys from the disciplinary rules and procedures adopted by the judicial department. Upon consideration of the issue of the legislation's constitutionality, the court held that the provision that provided immunity from disciplinary proceedings contravened Ind. Const. art. III, § 1 by violating separation of powers, and contravened the exclusive jurisdiction of the Indiana Supreme Court as granted by Ind. Const. art. VII, § 4 to regulate professional legal activity. The court further determined that the unconstitutional immunity provision was not severable from the rest of the act because, without it, attorneys could not participate in the program, which would allow interest earned on their clients' funds to be redirected for other purposes without the clients' consent.


OUTCOME: The court found the Attorney Trust Account Act unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers doctrine of the Indiana Constitution and the exclusive jurisdiction of the court to regulate attorneys.

 

143 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Clark v. State


No. 29S00-8810-CR-861


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


561 N.E.2d 759; 1990 Ind. LEXIS 212



November 1, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Hamilton County Court; The Honorable Harry L. Sauce, III, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions for driving while suspended, operating while intoxicated, and operating with a .10 percent blood alcohol level from the Hamilton County Court (Indiana), which ordered defendant's elevated and enhanced sentences to run consecutively due to multiple violations and for being a habitual offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that his convictions must be reversed because he was denied effective assistance of counsel and because his felony conviction and habitual offender sentence were constitutionally infirm as the jury instructions were incomplete. Also, defendant maintained that his habitual offender sentence should be vacated because the information upon which the State proceeded was defective. Next, he argued that his sentence of 35 years for operating while intoxicated and driving while suspended was excessive and disproportionate, and thus his sentence must be revised. The court partially agreed, remanding the case to the lower court to modify the judgment to reflect sentences of one year and four years for the two convictions, the sentences to run consecutively for a total of five years. The court reversed the trial court's decision to further enhance defendant's sentence. Defendant's sentence of two years for operating while intoxicated, plus an additional two years for aggravating circumstances, was the maximum sentence allowed. The penalty imposed, 35 years, was not proportionate to his offense and therefore violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 16.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and corresponding sentences for driving while suspended, a one-year sentence, and operating while intoxicated, a two-year sentence, plus an additional two years for aggravating circumstances ordered to run consecutive to the driving while suspended sentence. The court remanded the case to the lower court to modify the judgment to reflect the new sentence.

Coleman v. State


No. 45S00-8610-CR-937


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


558 N.E.2d 1059; 1990 Ind. LEXIS 171



August 24, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 23, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Lake Superior Court; The Honorable Richard Maroc, Judge; Cause No. 1CR-203-1184-842.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), for murder, attempted murder, and child molesting. The jury also recommended the death penalty and the trial court sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to his conviction, defendant appealed and the court affirmed. Defendant alleged that the state presented evidence of the impact of his crimes on the victims and testimony by a family member concerning the propriety of the death penalty. The grandmother testified that her daughter had become withdrawn as a result of watching her niece killed and being sexually assaulted herself. The court found that those were hardly factors about which the defendant was unaware. The grandmother's statement about her own attempt at suicide and her opinion as to defendant's sentencing were not relied on by the trial court in sentencing and the testimony did not violate the eighth amendment. The court affirmed the conclusion that a prosecutor's note only minimally affected defendant's ability to decide whether to testify and found that the victim's pre-trial identification was not the product of improperly suggestive procedures. The court found that as defendant was convicted of murders in another state, he enticed two young girls, bound them, stomped and strangled one of them to death, and repeatedly molested the other, and there were no mitigating factors, the death penalty was justified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in all matters relating to defendant's conviction and sentence of death. The court directed the trial court to enter a sentence for the prosecutor's contemptuous actions adequate to deter such conduct.

Burris v. State


No. 49S00-8610-PC-917


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


558 N.E.2d 1067; 1990 Ind. LEXIS 170



August 24, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 23, 1990.
Writ of habeas corpus denied Burris v. Farley, 845 F. Supp. 636, 1994 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 1162 (N.D. Ind., 1994)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Marion Superior Court; The Honorable Roy F. Jones, Special Judge; Cause No. CR80-53A.
Burris v. State, 465 N.E.2d 171, 1984 Ind. LEXIS 854 (Ind., 1984)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the affirmation of his sentence of death entered by the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which denied defendant's petition for post-conviction relief from his conviction of murder.


OVERVIEW: On direct appeal from defendant's conviction for murder, his conviction and sentence of death were affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed the death sentence and otherwise affirmed his denial of post-conviction relief. The court ruled that the jury was not misled, but was simply informed that the responsibility for sentencing ultimately rested with the judge. The court found that defense counsel was ineffective at the guilt phase when he made reprehensible comments, which were likely to have lingered in the jurors' minds and prejudiced their decision concerning the death penalty. Defense counsel was also ineffective when he failed to present and investigate mitigating evidence. The court held that defense counsel's comments at the guilt phase entitled defendant to relief under the Strickland test. The court concluded that defendant's representation fell below the reasonable standards and the failure to investigate mitigation fell below prevailing norms in the profession. Substantial mitigation was available and would have helped create a more sympathetic portrait of defendant. The cumulative effect of counsel's acts and omissions rendered the result of the penalty phase unreliable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's sentence of death and otherwise affirmed the trial court's denial of his petition for post-conviction relief from his conviction of murder.

147 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Thompson v. State


No. 31S00-8902-PC-167


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


552 N.E.2d 472; 1990 Ind. LEXIS 59



April 11, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Thompson v. State, 2015 Ind. App. LEXIS 388, 31 N.E.3d 1002 (Ind. Ct. App., 2015)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Thompson v. Superintendent, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 68075 (S.D. Ind., May 4, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Harrison Circuit Court, The Honorable Henry N. Leist, Judge, Cause No. 81-S-62.
Thompson v. State, 492 N.E.2d 264, 1986 Ind. LEXIS 1125 (Ind., 1986)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Harrison Circuit Court (Indiana), which imposed two enhanced sentences of 60 years on defendant for murders committed during a burglary, ordered that these sentences be served consecutively, and imposed a 30-year sentence to run concurrently therewith for conspiracy to commit burglary of a dwelling resulting in bodily injury, a Class A felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice burglarized a home and, during the course thereof, killed the homeowners. Testimony at trial indicated that both victims died of wounds inflicted by a knife wielded by defendant. Defendant initially received the death penalty for the two murders, but the court set the death sentence aside in a previous appeal and remanded the case for resentencing. In imposing the two 60-year enhanced sentences, the trial court stated as aggravating factors that the victims were aged, were virtually unknown to defendant, and were murdered in an unnecessary and brutal manner. The court held that: (1) sentencing was within the discretion of the trial court, and a sentence that was authorized by statute would not be revised on appeal unless it was manifestly unreasonable; (2) the fact that defendant's accomplice received a lesser sentence for the same crime was not sufficient in and of itself to invalidate defendant's sentence; (3) it was not unconstitutionally disproportionate to sentence a "trigger man" to a greater sentence than that of his accomplice; and (4) there was nothing in the record to indicate that the trial court exceeded its statutory authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

148 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Costas


No. 64S00-8705-CV-494


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


552 N.E.2d 459; 1990 Ind. LEXIS 58



April 9, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Porter County Superior Court, The Honorable Gary S. Germann, No. 2-86-CI-1308.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a judgment from the Porter Superior Court (Indiana), which granted defendant's motion to dismiss a Class C infraction, under Ind. Code § 13-1-1-9, for failure to have his automobile emissions tested, pursuant to Ind. Admin. Code tit. 325, r. 13-1.1.


OVERVIEW: In a direct appeal, pursuant to Ind. R. App. P. 4(A)(8), the State argued that the trial court erred when it concluded that the statute and its implementing regulations were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charge. Specifically, the court rejected defendant's contention that Ind. Admin. Code tit. 325, r. 13-1.1, as incorporated in Ind. Code § 13-1-1-9, violated the Privileges and Immunities Clause of the Indiana Constitution or the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution. Instead, the court held that, after treating the motion to dismiss as a motion for summary judgment, neither the trial court findings nor defendant's motion directed the court's attention to any evidence showing that defendant was entitled to a judgment as a matter of law upon the grounds that the regulations and statute were unconstitutionally applied. Rather, the court noted that there was no evidence that officials administered the program, declared by the trial court to have been constitutional on its face, in a discriminatory manner against a protected class.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had dismissed the charges against defendant. As a result, the court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

149 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


National Rural Utils. Coop. Fin. Corp. v. Public Serv. Coop.


No. 93S02-9003-EX-215 Supreme Court


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


552 N.E.2d 23; 1990 Ind. LEXIS 47



March 21, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Indiana Utility Regulatory Commission (formerly the Public Service Commission of Indiana), No. 93A02-8702-EX-00058 Court of Appeals, The Honorable Leslie Duvall, Frederick L. Corban, Karl O'Lessker, Willis Zagrovich and Vicky Bailey, Commissioners.



DISPOSITION: Summary affirmance ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The government challenged the decision of the Court of Appeals (Indiana), which affirmed a decision dismissing a petition for a rate increase intended to generate funds to pay debts related to an abandoned nuclear plant construction project.


OVERVIEW: On review of the dismissal of the petition, the court ordered summary affirmance. The court found that the Public Service Commission of Indiana (commission) had acted within its jurisdiction when it entered its order because the order constituted neither an advisory opinion nor a declaratory judgment. The court also found that the commission did not abuse its discretion by dismissing the petition on the merits rather than for lack of prosecution. The court determined that it was not error to conclude that a rate increase was not available because allowing a cooperatively-owned utility to generate funds to repay debts incurred in pursuit of a failed nuclear power plant by way of a rate increase produced the intolerable result of subjecting its "stockholders" to unlimited liability for investment decisions into which they had no input and from which they had no recourse in the marketplace. The court also determined that, because the nuclear plant never became "used or useful" in the production of energy, none of the operation expenses associated with the project were properly chargeable to the ratepayers.


OUTCOME: Summary affirmance of the dismissal of the petition for a rate increase was ordered.

Shepherd v. State


No. 71S00-8805-CR-472


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


547 N.E.2d 839; 1989 Ind. LEXIS 382



December 18, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from St. Joseph Superior Court, The Honorable Jerome Frese, Judge, Cause No. 26475.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the St. Joseph Superior Court (Indiana), which found him guilty of murder but mentally ill and sentenced to him to prison for 50 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lived with his mother and her boyfriend. Defendant had a troubled past and killed the victim. He was convicted of murder with a finding that he was mentally ill. On appeal, the court upheld the conviction and sentence. Under Ind. Code § 33-4-5-7, the trial court properly excluded prospective jurors who resided in the home of their parents. There was no error in the admission of testimony about defendant's prior bad acts because his insanity plea opened the door to evidence about defendant's entire life. Photographs of the victim and videotape of the crime scene were properly admitted to orient the jury to the facts of the crime. Ind. Code § 35-36-2-3, concerning the guilty but mentally ill verdict, was not an unconstitutional deprivation of due process and equal protection under the law. The trial court had not improperly enhanced defendant's statutorily authorized sentence in light of the many aggravating factors and the paucity of mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for murder.

French v. State


No. 33S00-8810-PC-890


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


547 N.E.2d 1084; 1989 Ind. LEXIS 381



December 18, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Henry Circuit Court, The Honorable John J. Kellam, Judge, Cause No. 74-CR-29.
French v. State, 266 Ind. 276, 362 N.E.2d 834, 1977 Ind. LEXIS 396 (1977)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of the decision from the Henry Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied his application for post-conviction relief after he was convicted of first degree murder, kidnapping, commission of a crime while armed with a deadly weapon; robbery, commission of a crime while armed with a deadly weapon, rape; and carrying an handgun without a license.


OVERVIEW: After a jury convicted petitioner of several crimes, he filed an application for post-conviction relief. The trial court denied the petition. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that appellant was not denied his right to a fair trial when the trial court submitted certain instructions to the jury because the trial court gave thorough instructions regarding the burden of proof on all material issues. The court found that petitioner was not denied effective assistance of counsel because he did not show that his counsel's performance was so deficient as to prejudice him and deprive him of a fair trial. The court held that the trial court's finding that petitioner was guilty of laches in bringing his post-conviction relief petition was appropriate because petitioner was aware of available remedies and his delay was unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which denied petitioner's application for post-conviction relief.

Smith v. State


No. 02S00-8805-PC-489


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


547 N.E.2d 817; 1989 Ind. LEXIS 366



December 13, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: State's Rehearing Denied, Appellant's Rehearing Granted March 7, 1990 and Reported at: 1990 Ind. LEXIS 31.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Allen Superior Court, The Honorable Alfred W. Moellering, Judge, Cause No. CR-83-86.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of an order of the Allen Superior Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief based on his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. He argued that the trial court erred in finding that he was not denied effective assistance of counsel. At trial, defense counsel failed to include an alibi witness on his pretrial notice, failed to tender any jury instructions to the effect that an alibi was an affirmative defense under the law, failed to prepare and conduct impeachment of the state's key witness, failed to counter improper testimony regarding a polygraph test of the state's witness, and introduced no evidence of mitigating factors at the sentencing hearing despite the availability of positive character evidence. The court reversed the trial court's decision, holding that defense counsel's representation fell below the prevailing norm for reasonably competent counsel and that his failure to function undermined confidence in the guilty verdict as well as the sentencing. The court concluded that the prisoner was denied a fair trial due to the ineffective assistance of his counsel.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision denying the prisoner post-conviction relief based on the ineffective assistance of counsel and remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial.

Woods v. State


No. 885 S 343


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


547 N.E.2d 772; 1989 Ind. LEXIS 336



November 28, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Granted August 13, 1990. Reported at: 1990 Ind. LEXIS 157.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Boone Superior Court, The Honorable Donald R. Payton, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Boone County Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of the knowing and intentional killing of a victim, and with robbery and serious bodily injury of the same victim, and imposed a death sentence and a 50-year sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged, with the participation of co-defendants, in the robbery and killing of a victim in his apartment. A jury convicted defendant of the charges, and recommended imposition of the death penalty. On appeal, the court held that: (1) defendant's seizure to be transported from the victim's apartment house to the police station for further intensive interrogation was justified by probable cause; (2) statements made by the trial prosecutor concerning a witness' testimony and the jurors' duty did not constitute cause for mistrial or undermine the reliability of the jury's death sentence recommendation contrary to the requirements of the Eighth Amendment; (3) the death sentence was not arbitrary, capricious, or manifestly unreasonable because all mitigating circumstances were accurately determined and evaluated and they were outweighed by the lone aggravating circumstance; (4) there was no legal basis for the trial court to bar the testimony of a co-defendant; and (5) the 50-year sentence for robbery was vacated because it rested upon the commission of the same robbery upon which the death sentence rested.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's convictions for robbery and murder, and imposition of the death sentence, but vacated the 50-year sentence for robbery.

Wills v. State


No. 09S00-8812-CR-983


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


545 N.E.2d 571; 1989 Ind. LEXIS 322



November 2, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Cass Superior Court, The Honorable Douglas A Cox, Judge, Cause No. 09D01-8720-CF-23.



DISPOSITION: This cause is remanded to the trial court for proper sentencing pursuant to this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Cass Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of voluntary manslaughter, as a Class A felony, and which sentenced him to 35 years, pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-42-1-3.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant, on his guilty plea, of voluntary manslaughter and sentenced him to 35 years as a Class A felony for use of a deadly weapon, pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-42-1-3. On defendant's appeal, the court affirmed the conviction but remanded for a resentencing under the statute as it existed at the time of the commission of the crime. The court determined that § 35-42-1-3 was amended to provide that voluntary manslaughter with a deadly weapon was a Class A felony, but that the act was committed under the older version of the statute, which considered voluntary manslaughter to be a Class B felony. The sentencing based on the amended statute was an unconstitutional ex post facto application. On remand, the trial court could sentence defendant to any term under the original statute as long as it did not exceed the original sentence and any enhancement of the sentence was supported on the record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for voluntary manslaughter, but remanded the cause to the trial court for resentencing under the statute that was in effective at the time of the trial.

 

155 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Covalt v. Carey Canada, Inc.


No. 98 S00-8811-CQ-922


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


543 N.E.2d 382; 1989 Ind. LEXIS 321; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P12,257



September 8, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended September 21, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certified Question from the United States Court of Appeals for the Seventh Circuit, No. 88-1828.



DISPOSITION: The certified question answered, this cause is remanded to the United States Court of Appeals for the Seventh Circuit for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a products liability action by plaintiffs, tort victim and his wife, against defendant tort feasors, the United States Court of Appeals for the Seventh Circuit certified a question to the court as to whether a plaintiff could bring suit within 2 years after discovery of a disease and its cause, notwithstanding that the discovery was made more than 10 years after exposure to the product that caused the disease.


OVERVIEW: In a products liability action brought by plaintiffs, tort victim and his wife, for damages as a result of having asbestosis, the federal court certified a question as to whether plaintiffs were able to bring a suit within 2 years after discovering the asbestosis and its cause, notwithstanding that the discovery was made more than 10 years after the last exposure to asbestos. The court answered the question in the affirmative and held that plaintiffs were allowed to bring the suit more than 10 years after the last exposure to the asbestos. Because the was a case of disease, plaintiff tort victim's cause of action accrued on the date he discovered or should have discovered the alleged injury and that the injury was caused by the asbestos manufactured by defendant tort feasors. Accordingly, plaintiffs' action was timely, as the action was brought within the two years after discovery and thereby within the statute of limitations contained in Ind. Code § 33-1-1.5-5. The court held that to have limited the period in which, even with due diligence, plaintiffs could have discovered that the cause of action existed, would have been inconsistent with the system of jurisprudence.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question affirmatively and remanded the cause for further proceedings, as plaintiffs, tort victim and his wife, timely brought their products liability action within two years after discovery of the asbestosis and its cause.

 

156 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Huffman v. State


No. 49S00-8602-CR-207


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


543 N.E.2d 360; 1989 Ind. LEXIS 278



September 7, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Marion County Superior Court, Criminal Division, Room 6, The Honorable Thomas E. Alsip, Special Judge, Cause No. CR84-106C.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Marion County Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of robbery, murder, felony murder, conspiracy to commit robbery, and conspiracy to commit murder. He was sentenced to multiple consecutive sentences and he also received the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: After defendant and some friends robbed and killed a another man, defendant was convicted of robbery, conspiracy, murder, and felony murder. Defendant appealed his convictions and the imposition of the death penalty. The court remanded the action with instructions to vacate defendant's convictions for robbery and conspiracy to commit robbery because robbery was a lesser included offense that merged into the conviction for felony murder. The charge for conspiracy to commit robbery was vacated because it involved the same acts as the conspiracy to commit robbery and it was improper to impose multiple punishments for a single offense. The remaining convictions and the death sentence, however, were affirmed. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the motion for separate trials, in allowing into evidence defendant's statement, in denying the motion for a change of venue, in allowing photographs of the victim's corpse, and in refusing to give an instruction on a lesser included offense. Further, the trial court was allowed to exclude irrelevant evidence during the penalty phase, and it was not required to believe defendant's proposed mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the action with instructions to vacate defendant's convictions for robbery and conspiracy to commit robbery, and it affirmed the imposition of the death sentence and the convictions for murder, conspiracy to commit murder, and felony murder.

 

157 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Department of Natural Resources v. Indiana Coal Council, Inc.


No. 19S00-8802-CV-263


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


542 N.E.2d 1000; 1989 Ind. LEXIS 267; 108 Oil & Gas Rep. 240



August 31, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Dubois Circuit Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Indiana Department of Natural Resources (DNR), archaeological society, and conservation council, challenged a decision of the Dubois Circuit Court (Indiana), which set aside the DNR's director's order. Appellees, coal council and landowner, contended that the order violated U.S. Const. amend. V because Ind. Code § 13-4.1-1-1 et seq., and its regulations, 310 Ind. Admin. Code § 12-2-1 et seq., as applied here constituted a taking.


OVERVIEW: The landowner's land contained artifacts. The archaeological society petitioned the DNR to have the land designated unsuitable for coal mining under Ind. Code § 13-4.1-14-2. The director's final order designated the land unsuitable for surface coal mining. The director included in the order a mitigation plan, which provided a way for the "unsuitable" designation to be removed through site testing and data recovery conducted by a DNR-approved archaeological contractor. The court vacated the lower court's decision. The court found that because the mitigation plan provided a means for the land to be designated suitable, a taking did not occur. It also found that the mitigation plan did not require the landowner to expend any money or convey property or property rights to the state. The plan also did not prevent the landowner from continuing to extract coal by means other than strip mining. Only two percent of the landowner's land would have been affected, assuming alternative mining methods were not used. The landowner's investment-backed expectations and present land use, therefore, were not significantly affected. Protection of cultural resources was a legitimate state interest.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision that set aside the director's order finding that a taking of the landowner's property had occurred. The court remanded the action for a decree denying relief from the director's order.

Livingston v. State


No. 49S00-8701-CR-23


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


542 N.E.2d 192; 1989 Ind. LEXIS 251



August 15, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division Room IV, The Honorable Thomas E. Alsip, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The conviction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division (Indiana), which, after ruling that defendant had no standing to challenge the search, entered drug convictions against him for violations of Ind. Code §§ 35-48-4-1, -6, dealing and possession of heroin, respectively.


OVERVIEW: At trial, when the state attempted to introduce the evidence it found in a search of a house for which it had a warrant, defendant's counsel objected and moved to suppress, claiming the search violated Indiana's knock and announce statute, Ind. Code § 35-33-5-7(d). After a hearing outside the presence of the jury, the trial court denied the motion to suppress the evidence on the grounds that defendant lacked standing to challenge the search under U.S. Const. amend. IV. The jury then found defendant guilty on both charges of dealing and possession of heroin and, after the two convictions were merged, defendant was sentenced to 30 years. On appeal, defendant argued that, as the one who was charged with a possession offense, he must risk admitting guilt to the crime of drug possession to establish standing to challenge the search which produced the narcotics he was charged with possessing. The court reviewed the record and affirmed the convictions, concluding that defendant failed to demonstrate that he had any legitimate expectation of privacy in the premises searched, a home that was neither owned nor controlled by defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, concluding that defendant had not shown that his interests that were invaded by the search were protected under the Fourth Amendment.

Canaan v. State


No. 82S00-8705-CR-521


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


541 N.E.2d 894; 1989 Ind. LEXIS 240



July 28, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Vanderburgh Circuit Court, The Honorable William H. Miller, Judge, Cause No. 5215.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed and this case is remanded in order for the court to set a date for execution.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him of murder, burglary, and attempted criminal deviate conduct, found him to be a habitual offender, and sentenced him to death by electrocution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, burglary, and attempted criminal deviate conduct, was determined to be an habitual offender, and was sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that: (1) Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9, which provided for the jury to make a recommendation to the sentencing judge regarding imposition of the death penalty, leaving to the trial judge the option to follow or not follow the recommendation, did not violate defendant's due process rights; (2) defendant's double jeopardy rights were not violated; (3) the trial court did not err in its admission of evidence, refusal and allowance of instructions, exclusion of testimony, and denial of a mistrial; and (4) the convictions were supported by sufficient evidence. The court further held that the record supported the trial judge's conclusion that defendant murdered the victim, burglarized her apartment, and attempted acts of criminal sexual deviancy. The record also showed defendant to be an habitual offender. The court therefore found that the death penalty as provided for under Indiana statutes was not arbitrarily or capriciously imposed upon defendant and was reasonable and appropriate in his case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, which convicted defendant of murder, burglary, and attempted criminal deviate conduct, found him to be an habitual offender, and sentenced him to death. The court also remanded the case in order for the court to set a date for execution.

 

160 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Cooper v. State


No. 45S00-8701-CR-61


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


540 N.E.2d 1216; 1989 Ind. LEXIS 216



July 13, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Lake Superior Court, The Honorable Richard J. Conroy, Judge, Cause No. 3CR-109-685-433.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the death sentence imposed by the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) following her pleas of guilty to knowing or intentional murder and murder in the commission or attempt of a robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that her death sentence violated the Indiana Constitution and the United States Constitution because she was 15 years old when she committed the crime. The court agreed and reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court observed that Indiana's death penalty statute was revised, as the result of this case, to specify that the death penalty could not be imposed upon a defendant below the age of 16. The court found that defendant would be both the first and last person ever to be executed in Indiana for a crime committed at the age of 15. Accordingly, the court determined that defendant's sentence failed to comply with the Indiana Constitution in that it was unique and disproportionate to any other sentence for the same crime. The court also determined that the Indiana death penalty statute, at the time defendant committed her crime, did not specify a minimum age and, therefore, failed to comply with the requirements of the Eighth Amendment. The court concluded that entry of a final judgment, rather than a remand to the trial court, was appropriate and imposed the maximum sentence permitted under Indiana law.


OUTCOME: That part of the trial court's judgment that ordered execution was vacated and the case was remanded with instructions that defendant be sentenced to the maximum prison sentence available under Indiana law for murder.

Kindred v. State

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant by information with forgery and attempted theft. Following a jury trial, the Putnam Circuit Court (Indiana) entered judgment that convicted defendant of class C forgery and class D theft and that sentenced him as a habitual offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised numerous issues on appeal concerning: the appropriateness of the venue of his prosecution; the lower court's unfavorable rulings on various motions raised during trial; the lower court's rulings concerning the admissibility of evidence defendant contended was prejudicial; the sufficiency of the evidence to support the theft conviction; and the lower court's rulings on discovery issues. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's theft conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting and sentencing defendant as a habitual offender was affirmed.

Powers v. State


No. 23S00-8803-CR-339


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


539 N.E.2d 950; 1989 Ind. LEXIS 184



June 21, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Fountain County Circuit Court, The Honorable Vincent F. Grogg, Judge, Cause No. 85-S-87.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Fountain County (Indiana), which had convicted him of escape and sentenced him to a 32-year term as an habitual offender under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-8(e). He argued in part that there was insufficient evidence to support conviction and that the habitual offender sentencing was improper.


OVERVIEW: While incarcerated waiting sentencing on a burglary conviction, defendant was boosted up along the fencing around the exercise yard and left the area. He was later caught and tried for escape. On review, he argued that the habitual offender sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment and that the charge had been double jeopardy brought on by prosecutorial vindictiveness. The court found that: (1) there had been sufficient proof of defendant's lawful detention on the burglary charge at the time of his escape; (2) the fact that defendant had gone over the wall and fled the area was sufficient evidence to permit a finding of the requisite intent; (3) the habitual offender sentencing had not been improper where the enhancement had been mandatory under the statute; and (4) there had been no showing of any prosecutorial vindictiveness or double jeopardy where the habitual offender punishment was imposed for the new crime rather than for the earlier crimes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Games v. State


No. 185 S 7


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


535 N.E.2d 530; 1989 Ind. LEXIS 406



March 14, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARION SUPERIOR COURT, CRIMINAL DIVISION. The Honorable John W. Tranberg, Judge. No. CR83-126A



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed. This cause is remanded to the trial court for the purpose of setting a date for the death sentence to be carried out.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana). The trial court convicted defendant of murder, conspiracy to commit murder, robbery, and conspiracy to commit robbery, and the trial court imposed the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Based in part on testimony by defendant's accomplice, defendant was convicted of murder, robbery, and conspiracy to commit each offense and sentenced to death. The court affirmed. The belated filing of the death penalty information and the ensuing four-month delay before trial did not prejudice defendant's opportunity for a fair trial. The trial court did not err in limiting defendant's discovery motion for all police reports of homicide investigations as of a certain date within the entire state. The burden upon the state was a proper consideration, and limiting the request to police reports only within the county for a four-year period was a reasonable compromise. The jury was able to discharge its duty notwithstanding the state's failure to disclose the details of the accomplice's plea agreement prior to the accomplice's substantive testimony. The jury was capable of reevaluating the credibility of a witness's testimony following the disclosure of facts indicating witness bias. The trial court did not err in imposing disparate sentences on defendant and his accomplice because of the special nature of a plea agreement and the roles each played in the robbery and murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for murder, robbery, and conspiracy to commit each substantive offense.
