Townsend v. State


No. 885 S 339


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


533 N.E.2d 1215; 1989 Ind. LEXIS 37



February 14, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Lake Superior Court, Criminal Division, The Honorable Richard W. Maroc, Judge, Cause No. 1CR-227-1283-898.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from a judgment of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which jointly tried defendants for murder, found them guilty, and sentenced them to death.


OVERVIEW: A husband and a wife were found stabbed to death. Defendants were found guilty of the murders. The trial court found as aggravating circumstances that both murders were committed intentionally while defendants were committing or attempting to commit robbery, and that the murders were committed while having previously committed another murder. Defendants were sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the record amply supported the trial court's findings. The trial court did not err in admitting co-defendants' statements. There was evidence proving beyond a reasonable doubt that defendants were guilty of the murders. Further, the aggravating circumstances were proven beyond a reasonable doubt and outweighed the mitigating circumstances. No reasonable person could find that the death penalty in each case was arbitrarily or capriciously applied, or that it was unreasonable or inappropriate. The aggravating factor that defendants each previously committed another murder was not unconstitutional. There was no ineffective representation of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted the defendants for murder and sentenced them to death. The court remanded to the trial court for the purpose of setting a date for the imposition of the death penalty.

Daniels v. State


No. 85S00-8712-PC-1186


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


531 N.E.2d 1173; 1988 Ind. LEXIS 362



December 29, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Wabash Circuit Court, The Honorable Daniel Vanderpool, Judge, Cause No. CR 78-19.



DISPOSITION: The post conviction court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment by the Wabash Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief. Defendant had alleged that his guilty plea was not entered knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to second degree murder in exchange for the State's dismissal of a felony murder count and a life sentence. Defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief alleging that his guilty plea was not entered into knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily. The trial court denied the petition. The court affirmed on appeal. The court held that defendant was entitled to a reversal only if the evidence was without conflict and led unerringly to a conclusion contrary to the one reached by the trial court. The court found no such error by the trial court. The court noted that when defendant entered his plea, he indicated that he was doing so voluntarily and that the plea was not the result of any undue influence, coercion, or promises. The court held that there was no evidence supporting defendant's claim that the prosecutor implied that he would receive the death penalty if he did not make a plea. The court found that the plea agreement provided defendant with the benefit of an increased possibility of earlier clemency or parole and was within the bounds of the charging statute. Defendant received exactly what he agreed to.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

168 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. Irving Materials, Inc.


No. 27S02-8811-CV-933


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


530 N.E.2d 730; 1988 Ind. LEXIS 311



November 23, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Grant Circuit Court, The Honorable Thomas R. Hunt, Judge, Cause No. C-85-191, No. 27A02-8604-CV-116 in the Court of Appeals, On Petition to Transfer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city filed a petition to transfer and challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Indiana), which affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment for appellees, vendee and vendors, entered in appellees' action for a judgment declaring that an amendment to the city's zoning ordinance was enacted by operation of law because the city council failed to take action under Ind. Code §§ 36-7-4-500 - 36-7-4-512 (1981) (500 series).


OVERVIEW: Appellees filed a petition with the city's planning commission seeking rezoning of the vendor's land. The plan commission recommended passage of the amendment to the city council. The council rejected the amendment. Neither the plan commission nor the council took any further action. Appellees then sought a judgment declaring first that the council's rejection of the amendment was arbitrary and second, that the amendment was enacted by operation of law because the council failed to take action under the 500 series. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees on their second claim, and the appellate court affirmed the judgment. The court granted the city's petition to transfer and reversed the trial court's judgment. While amendments to the master plan required compliance with the 500 series, an amendment to a zoning ordinance, which allowed rezoning of a particular tract of land, required compliance with Ind. Code §§ 36-7-4-600 - 36-7-4-612 (1981) (600 series). Because appellees sought to have the vendor's land rezoned, the 600 series applied; therefore, the amendment was not enacted by operation of law based on the council's failure to take action under the 500 series.


OUTCOME: The court granted the city's petition to transfer and reversed the trial court's order of summary judgment for appellees that declared that the city's zoning ordinance was enacted by operation of law because city council failed to take action under the 500 series. The case was remanded to the trial court with directions to grant the city's motion for summary judgment as to that count of appellees' complaint.

Daniels v. State


No. 49S00-8601-PC-33


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


528 N.E.2d 775; 1988 Ind. LEXIS 266



September 23, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 21, 1988.
Vacated by Daniels v. Indiana, 491 U.S. 902, 109 S. Ct. 3182, 105 L. Ed. 2d 691, 1989 U.S. LEXIS 3001 (1989)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion County Superior Court Criminal Division VI, The Honorable Thomas E. Alsip, Special Judge.
Daniels v. State, 453 N.E.2d 160, 1983 Ind. LEXIS 940 (Ind., 1983)



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Marion County Superior Court Criminal Division VI (Indiana), which denied defendant's petition for post-conviction relief. Defendant claimed that the admission of a witness's identification testimony violated his rights to cross-examination and confrontation as a result of the hypnosis of the witness.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery, attempted robbery, and felony murder. His convictions were affirmed on appeal. In his petition for post-conviction relief, defendant claimed that the admission of a witness's identification testimony violated his rights to cross-examination and confrontation as a result of the hypnosis of the witness and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel. The trial court denied his petition. The court affirmed, holding that there was no persuasive evidence that the witness's identification of defendant as the triggerman was the result of hypnosis. The witness made a positive identification of defendant when he viewed defendant in a line-up. Defendant's counsel's decision to concentrate on discrediting one of the participants in the crime instead of the witness who identified defendant as the triggerman was trial strategy that did not rise to the level of ineffective assistance of counsel. Although defendant's counsel should have presented additional evidence in mitigation besides the testimony of defendant's mother, that testimony itself emphasized that there may have been tactical reasons why more witnesses were not called.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Superior Court of Porter County (Indiana) that convicted him of aiding in the delivery of cocaine and dealing in a sawed-off shotgun.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of aiding in the delivery of cocaine and dealing in a sawed-off shotgun. The conviction was followed by an incident in which the passenger in defendant's vehicle delivered a kilo of cocaine to an undercover officer. At the time of defendant's arrest, a semi-automatic pistol and a sawed-off shotgun were found inside his vehicle. Defendant alleged numerous errors on appeal, including that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, that certain evidence was erroneously admitted, and that the superior court abused its discretion in sentencing him. The court concluded that due to the nature of the crime and defendant's character, the sentences imposed were not manifestly unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's order that entered a conviction against defendant on charges of aiding in the delivery of cocaine and dealing in a sawed-off shotgun.

Fassoth v. State


No. 64S00-8612-CR-1068


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


525 N.E.2d 318; 1988 Ind. LEXIS 201



July 7, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Porter Superior Court, The Honorable Roger V. Bradford, Judge, Cause No. 85 PSCr-114.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from a judgment of the Porter Superior Court (Indiana) that convicted them after a jury trial on charges of dealing in cocaine, a Class A felony and possession of marijuana with the intent to deliver, a Class C felony. One defendant was convicted of aiding in the delivery of cocaine, a Class A felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendants challenged their convictions for drug sale offenses on various grounds. The court held that: (1) the trial court did not improperly restrict the cross-examination of a state's witness, who was also involved in the drug transactions at issue, because while defendants were not permitted to inquire about alleged plea agreements between the witness and the state, they were permitted to inquire about his prior theft conviction and about the witness's grant of immunity for his testimony; (2) the trial court's failure to instruct the jury on exclusive control as an element of constructive possession of illegal drugs was harmless because the court found that defendants were in fact in exclusive control over the drugs at the time of their arrest; (3) a tape recording of defendants was admissible despite static on the tape because it was a recording by a "bug" rather than in an interrogation room where equipment is expected to be of high quality, and because the recording was sufficiently clear to show that a drug transaction was taking place; and (4) there was sufficient separate evidence to convict all defendants, and therefore separate trials were not necessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for dealing in cocaine, a Class A felony, possession of marijuana with the intent to deliver, a Class C felony, and aiding in the delivery of cocaine, a Class A felony.

Halbig v. State


No. 82S00-8708-CR-763


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


525 N.E.2d 288; 1988 Ind. LEXIS 203



July 5, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Vanderburgh Superior Court, The Honorable William J. Brune, Judge, Cause No. 86-CR-286.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Vanderburgh County (Indiana), which convicted him of attempted murder, a class A felony.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction of attempted murder. Specifically, he argued that he had no intent to kill the victim and he merely shot toward him to scare him away. However, the court disagreed and affirmed his conviction finding sufficient evidence to support it. Defendant also argued that certain photographs were erroneously admitted into evidence because they failed to establish any element or fact surrounding the shooting and they were introduced to prejudice and inflame the passions of the jury. The court again disagreed and held that the evidence was properly admitted to show defendant's anger and jealousy of the victim, which proceeded the shooting. Furthermore, the evidence tended to complete the story of the crime. Therefore it was admitted under the res gestae exception to the rule prohibiting evidence of a separate crime. Defendant also argued that he was denied a fair trial. The court found that defendant offered no evidence of actual harm resulting from the jurors seeing him in handcuffs and was thus had not been denied a fair trial. The court also held there was no evidence of self-defense.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for attempted murder was affirmed.

Lake County Council v. Allen


No. 45S03-8802-CV-237


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


524 N.E.2d 771; 1988 Ind. LEXIS 154



June 6, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied September 26, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Lake Superior Court, Room 2 Sitting in East Chicago, Indiana The Honorable Morton B. Kanz, Presiding Judge Cause No. 286-773.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county council appealed an order of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) granting summary judgment in favor of defendant utility, effectively denying the county its requested declaratory relief in its action against defendants, township trustees, poor relief recipients, and utility creditors. The county had sought a declaration that the Distressed Township and Poor Relief Acts were unconstitutional under the circumstances.


OVERVIEW: The county claimed that all debt incurred by the township in excess of two percent of its assessed valuation was in violation of Ind. Const. art. XIII, § 1, and that the obligation of such debts was therefore void and the statutes requiring the county to pay them were unconstitutional. The township trustees had declared the township distressed, thus triggering the provisions of the Distressed Township Act of 1986. Despite funding from the State, the county refused to institute any plan claiming that poor relief was the obligation of the township and not the county. The issue for review was the finding by the trial court that poor relief was ultimately the responsibility of the county and thus was governed by its constitutional debt limit rather than that of the township. Affirming, the court agreed that the county had an affirmative duty to fund the township poor relief whether it was to be reimbursed by the township or not. The obligation of the county to be ultimately responsible for poor relief was not initiated by the Distressed Township Act in 1986, but had been in effect since 1935. Therefore the obligations resulting from the distress of the township did not become void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Eddy v. McGinnis


No. 20S03-8703-CV-302


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


523 N.E.2d 737; 1988 Ind. LEXIS 155



May 31, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Interlocutory Appeal from the Elkhart Superior Court Division III The Honorable Worth N. Yoder, Judge Cause Number 715.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is reversed and this cause is remanded with instructions to deny defendant's motion for partial summary judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured driver challenged a judgment from the Elkhart Superior Court (Indiana), which granted appellee drunk driver's motion for partial summary judgment on the issue of punitive damages, certifying an order for an interlocutory appeal on whether Ind. Code § 34-4-30-2 violated the double jeopardy clause of the state constitution. The injured driver sought compensatory and punitive damages.


OVERVIEW: The injured driver's car was struck when the drunk driver's blood alcohol content was .25 percent. The police ticketed the drunk driver for driving while intoxicated, and the prosecutor later charged him with driving while intoxicated. The injured driver brought a negligence action. The court found that the most it could say about precedent on the subject was that it had prohibited the unlimited imposition of punitive damages on the grounds that such violated the spirit of the state constitution, but absent a constitutional prohibition, the legislature was free to reform the state's substantive law in this field, and it had done so; therefore the drunk driver was not entitled to partial summary judgment on the issue of punitive damages. The court instructed that Ind. Code § 34-4-30-2 did not violate double jeopardy and that the drunk driver could not assert the possibility of criminal punishment as a defense to a claim for punitive damages. The judgment was reversed and the cause was remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded with instructions to deny the drunk driver's motion for partial summary judgment, as the statute at issue did not violate the double jeopardy clause of the state constitution, and the injured driver could maintain her civil action for compensatory and punitive damages.

In re Young


Cause No. 94S00-8801-JD-108


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


522 N.E.2d 386; 1988 Ind. LEXIS 363



May 5, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As amended May 5, 1988.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Indiana Commission on Judicial Qualifications (commission) charged respondent judge with willful misconduct in office in violation of the Model Code of Judicial Conduct Canons 1 and 2. The matter was before the court on the judge's motion to dismiss the statement of charges and his alternative motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The commission charged the judge with willful misconduct in office, in violation of the Model Code of Judicial Conduct (code) Canons 1 and 2. The judge filed a motion to dismiss the statement of charges and an alternative motion to dismiss. The court denied the motions. In rejecting the judge's claim that the charges were unconstitutionally vague, the court found that a greater degree of flexibility was permitted with respect to judicial disciplinary rules than was allowed in criminal statutes and that the charges were sufficiently precise to provide the judge, who had lengthy legal experience, with notice. The court treated the alternate motion to dismiss as a motion to dismiss, pursuant to Ind. R. Civ. P. 12(B)(6), and held that it was not convinced that the commission could not prove a set of facts that would support the willful misconduct charge. The court rejected the judge's claim that he could only be disciplined pursuant to Ind. Const. art. 7, § 11. According to the court, the code was an enhancement of the provisions set forth in Ind. Const. art. 7, § 4 and, thus, the code was a proper basis to charge misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court denied the judge's motion to dismiss the statement of charges filed against him by the commission and his alternative motion to dismiss.

Baxter v. State


No. 385 S 77


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


522 N.E.2d 362; 1988 Ind. LEXIS 108



April 25, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 26, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Noble Superior Court The Honorable Roger B. Cosbey, Judge Cause Number SCR-84-10.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Noble Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of two counts of child molesting under Ind. Code § 35-42-4-3 (1985 Repl.) and two counts of incest under Ind. Code § 35-46-1-3 (1985 Repl.). The trial court also determined that defendant was a habitual offender under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-8 (1985 Repl.).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexually abusing his two stepdaughters and sentenced as a habitual offender based on prior felony convictions. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that: (1) the evidence at trial was sufficient to support the convictions where the victims, who testified that defendant had forced them to have sexual relations, were cross-examined at trial and their out-of-court statements, related by other witnesses, were admissible; (2) the trial court did not err in refusing to grant defense counsel's motions for continuance to allow more time to prepare for trial where defense counsel had nearly four months to prepare, the only discovery left uncompleted was depositions, and the trial court ensured that defense counsel would be able to take the depositions and review them immediately after they were taken; (3) the trial court properly excluded defendant's alibi evidence where the notice of alibi was both tardy and incomplete, none of defendant's explanations constituted just cause for the delay in submitting the notice of alibi, and the risk of fabrication was considerable; and (4) the victims were properly determined to be competent to testify.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for child molestation and incest.

 

179 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Sims v. State


No. 1185 S 444


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


521 N.E.2d 336; 1988 Ind. LEXIS 52



April 6, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Marion County Superior Court, Criminal Division One, The Honorable John W. Tranberg, Judge, Cause No. CR76-076A.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the denial of his petition for post-conviction relief by the Marion County Superior Court, Criminal Division One (Indiana).


OVERVIEW: A jury trial resulted in appellant's conviction for armed robbery, involuntary manslaughter, and first degree murder. The trial court vacated the involuntary manslaughter conviction. On direct appeal, appellant's conviction and sentence for felony murder were affirmed and his conviction for armed robbery was vacated. Appellant's petition for post-conviction relief was denied. The court affirmed. The court found that appellant's argument that he should have been convicted of involuntary manslaughter rather than felony murder was available to him at the time of his direct appeal. Because it was not raised at that time, the argument was waived for post-conviction review. Similarly, his argument that the felony murder rule was unconstitutional had been waived. The court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in its grant of a continuance to the prosecution and that appellant failed to identify any specific examples that lead unmistakably and unerringly to the conclusion that his appellate counsel was ineffective.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of appellant's petition was affirmed.

 

180 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Stroud v. State


No. 64S00-8611-CR-1008


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


517 N.E.2d 780; 1988 Ind. LEXIS 3



January 8, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Porter County Superior Court, The Honorable Roger V. Bradford, Presiding Judge, Cause No. 85-PSCr-50.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is in all things affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Porter County Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of one count of dealing in a narcotic drug and two counts of possession of a narcotic drug, specifically, cocaine. Defendant also appealed his sentence of 30 years, of which 10 years would be suspended.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of one count of dealing in a narcotic drug and two counts of possession of a narcotic drug, specifically, cocaine. On the felony of dealing in a narcotic drug, the trial court sentenced him to 30 years' imprisonment, with 10 years suspended. On appeal, the court affirmed. The 20-year minimum mandatory sentence that defendant received for his cocaine dealing was constitutional because the sentence was not excessive or manifestly unreasonable. Defendant had no right to probation. Although evidence was admitted that had been obtained from the warrantless installation of a pen register on the phone of defendant's dealer, the phone did not belong to defendant, and therefore he lacked standing to question the necessity of a warrant. Even though the prosecutor did not reveal the existence of the pen register to defendant before the trial, no reversible error occurred. The prosecutor himself had not known of the pen register's existence until midway through the trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

181 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Van Cleave v. State


No. 384 S 109


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


517 N.E.2d 356; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 1196



December 30, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 26, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division IV, The Honorable Patricia Gifford, Judge, Cause Number CR 82-153D.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which entered a conviction based on appellant's plea of guilty to murder under Ind. Code § 35-42-11 (1985), and which sentenced him to death under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-9 (1985).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested and charged with murder and conspiracy to commit robbery, and under a plea agreement, the state agreed to forego prosecution on the conspiracy charge in exchange for a plea of guilty to felony murder. The parties agreed to litigate the sentence as to death or a set term of imprisonment. During appellant's cross-examination on his sentencing hearing, he voluntarily testified that he had confessed to 20 or 25 burglaries as a clean-up statement. The trial court sentenced appellant to death and he sought review. The court affirmed, holding that the use of his clean-up statement did not constitute reversible error because there already was an aggravating factor, it was discovered after he had negotiated his plea, and it was not exculpatory evidence. The court held that the statement was properly used for impeachment purposes, together with other impeachment evidence. Further, an amended discovery order which was not overly oppressive to the prosecution was not error because he had a reasonable opportunity to discover a discriminatory practice. The court held that appellant received effective assistance of counsel and all other errors raised lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of appellant for felony murder based on entry of a guilty plea, and of his sentence to death.

 

182 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. State


No. 63S01-8712-CR-1180


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


517 N.E.2d 64; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 1195



December 29, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Pike County Circuit Court, The Honorable Marvin D. Stratton, Judge, Cause Number 84 CR 27, No. 1-1285 A 327 in the Court of Appeals, On Petition to Transfer.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is reversed and this case remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Court of Appeals (Indiana), which affirmed her conviction on two counts of attempted child molesting and two counts of confinement. Defendant contended that admission of a videotaped statement of one of the molested children violated the confrontation clauses of both the federal and state constitutions, because the child was never subject to cross-examination.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of molesting several grandchildren. The state filed a motion seeking to admit a videotaped statement of one of the molested children into evidence at trial. A statement was then videotaped without notifying defendant or giving her counsel the opportunity to attend. After a hearing pursuant to Ind. Code § 35-37-4-6 (1987 Supp.), the trial judge admitted the statement and found the child competent but unavailable to testify at trial. Defendant was not allowed to cross-examine the child. The court of appeals held that admission of the videotape was proper. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for a new trial. The court held that § 35-37-4-6 was not unconstitutional per se under either the Sixth Amendment or Ind. Const. art. 1, § 13. However, the court also held that: (1) by enacting § 35-37-4-6, the legislature did not intend to restrict defendant's right of cross-examination but only to require that it occur in an atmosphere less traumatizing to the child victim; and (2) in order to comply with the Indiana Constitution, use of a statement videotaped under § 35-37-4-6 had to be accompanied by some opportunity for cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that the admission of the videotaped statement of one of the molested children was not harmless error. Therefore, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

183 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Greene v. State


No. 1185 S 457


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


515 N.E.2d 1376; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 1145



December 4, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the LaPorte Superior Court, No. 2, The Honorable Don. E. Harner, Judge, Cause No. SC2-1008.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed in every respect.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the LaPorte Superior Court, No. 2 (Indiana), for kidnapping, a class A felony, Ind. Code § 35-42-3-2(a)(4) and the sentence of a 30-year term to run consecutively to his previous sentence on unrelated charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was an inmate who, during a prison riot and hostage-taking, was seen sitting with a guard in a cell holding an iron bar with a hook on top. On appeal following his conviction for kidnapping, the court affirmed, holding that administrative segregation in prison before and after the kidnapping charge did not impede his defense as he had unlimited access to his attorney. In the absence of any deprivation that affects his fair trial rights, the trial court did not have authority to order his release into the general prison population. The evidence was sufficient to support the conviction as the jury could reasonably infer from defendant's actions he intended to use the guards as hostages. Although hearsay testimony should not have been admitted, he suffered no prejudice from the statements. Earlier testimony established that the prisoners threatened to kill the guards if their demands were not met and admitting the hearsay was harmless. The trial court did not err when it sentenced defendant as the trial court imposed the presumptive sentence allowed under Ind. Code § 35-50-2-4.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for kidnapping was affirmed.

 

184 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Fleenor v. State


No. 1184 S 458


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


514 N.E.2d 80; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 1085



October 13, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 26, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Johnson County Circuit Court, The Honorable Larry J. McKinney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed in all things; the cause is remanded to the trial court for the purpose of fixing a date for the sentence to be carried out.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Johnson County Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him of murder and burglary. The trial court imposed the death sentence for defendant's murder conviction.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of murder and burglary. The jury recommended the death sentence for the murder conviction and the trial court ordered a death sentence. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court found the trial court did not error by excluding prospective jurors who could not conscientiously consider the death penalty where there was sufficient evidence the prospective jurors were irrevocably committed to voting against the death penalty. The court held there was sufficient evidence defendant had the requisite intent to commit the offenses where he purchased a gun within six hours of the offenses, prior to the offenses he told various people he intended to kill someone, and defendant's action during the commission of the killings indicated he possessed a knowing state of mind. The court determined the jury instructions regarding the death penalty, when read as a whole, were not misleading. The court concluded the trial court properly considered mitigating circumstances during its sentencing of defendant. The court found the death penalty statute, Ind. Code 35-50-2-9 (1979 Repl.), provided clear and specific guidance for imposing the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that convicted defendant of murder and robbery and that sentenced defendant to the death penalty. The court remanded to the trial court for the purpose of fixing a date for the sentence to be carried out.

 

185 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Minniefield v. State


No. 485 S 133


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


512 N.E.2d 1103; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 1067



September 24, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Lake Superior Court, The Honorable James E. Letsinger, Judge, Nos. 2CR-115-684-472, 2CR-43-384-170, 2CR-47-384-189.



DISPOSITION: We find no reversible error. The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant, following a jury trial, of burglary and conspiracy to commit murder.


OVERVIEW: The victim observed two men going around her house. One of the men, whom the victim knew, was carrying a television. Prior to trial, defendant tried to convince the victim to drop in the charges in exchange for a sum of money. When this failed, defendant hired a man to kill the victim. Defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction. However, the court determined that the in-court identification of defendant as one of the robbers was sufficient to support his conviction. Defendant contended that he did not commit bribery, but offered the victim money as a form of restitution. The court found that a reasonable juror could have determined that defendant had bribed the victim. Further, defendant asserted that there was insufficient evidence to demonstrate that he was guilty of conspiracy to commit murder. The court determined that because defendant and his brother directed a third party to the victim's residence for the purpose of killing her. The court determined that the fact that his brother was acquitted of conspiracy to murder did not render the verdicts inconsistent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for burglary and conspiracy to commit murder.

 

186 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Mills v. State


No. 385 S 82


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


512 N.E.2d 846; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 1054



September 10, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Porter Superior Court, Criminal Division, The Honorable Roger V. Bradford, Cause No. 81-PSCR-122.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Porter Superior Court (Indiana), which convicted him of theft, a class D felony, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-43-4-2 (1985), found him to be a habitual offender, in violation of Ind. Code § 35-50-2-8 (1985), and sentenced him to two years for the theft conviction enhanced by 30 years for the recidivist determination.


OVERVIEW: Defendant used a valid credit card to rent a car from a car rental company. The credit card belonged to an individual, and defendant presented a driver's license with his picture but the individual's name. He gave the individual's correct telephone number on the rental agreement and took possession of a car. The car rental company's manager later discovered that the car was overdue and contacted the individual at the number provided by defendant. Defendant was later charged with theft and with being a habitual criminal. The car was never returned. At the trial, defendant testified that the individual authorized the use of his credit card and that he left the vehicle in the individual's garage. The individual was not present at the trial to corroborate or disprove defendant's testimony. He was later convicted of the charged offenses. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the jury had sufficient evidence before it to conclude that defendant intended to deprive the car rental company of the value or use of the car because he used the individual's credit card to rent the car and he presented identification that falsely identified him as the individual.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

187 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Calhoun v. Jennings


No. 29S02-8607-CV-652


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


512 N.E.2d 178; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 1026



August 27, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 29, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Hamilton Circuit Court, The Honorable Paul H. Johnson, Jr., Special Judge Presiding, No. C84-375.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tax sale purchaser (purchaser) challenged the decision of the Hamilton Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant mortgagee upon finding that state tax sale notice provisions violated the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: A mortgagee purchased a property at a foreclosure sale and recorded the deed subsequent to the property's acquisition at tax sale by the purchaser. The court reversed the decision of the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of the mortgagee because tax sale notice requirements did not violate Fourteenth Amendment due process protections, and after the expiration of the two-year redemption period, the purchaser was entitled to a tax deed under Ind. Code § 6-1.1-25-4. The court found that the mortgagee's claim was extinguished when the purchaser presented his tax sale certificate and demanded a deed, and the refusal of the county auditor to issue the deed did not give the mortgagee any additional rights to the property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the mortgagee, and held that the purchaser was entitled to a deed to the property.

 

188 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


No. 584 S 163


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


511 N.E.2d 1036; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 1031



August 21, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Tippecanoe County Court, The Honorable Kenneth L. Thayer, Cause No. TC-MT-305-83.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the trial court's judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Tippecanoe County Court (Indiana), which convicted him of theft and determined that he was a habitual offender, Ind. Code § 35-50-2-8 (1985 Repl.). The trial court imposed a two-year term for the theft and enhanced that sentence by 30 years for the recidivist finding. Defendant argued that a 32-year sentence for the theft of $ 50 worth of merchandise violated both federal and state constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the conviction. It held that defendant's sentence did not violate U.S. Const. amend. VIII. Because defendant was sentenced to a term of years, the court was not required to undertake a proportionality analysis. It found the sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment. The court also held that while Ind. Const. art. I, § 16 required it to determine proportionality, defendant's sentence was not a disproportionate penalty in light of his prior criminal record. His four previous felonies reflected a person who committed nonviolent crimes when not incarcerated. The trial court did not err in ordering defense counsel not to mention before the jury the possible penalty for the habitual offender finding. The jury had the right under Ind. Const. art. I, § 19 to determine the law and the facts. The habitual offender finding was a means of sentencing and was not a determination of law. The trial court properly refused to allow defendant to testify about why he did not deserve to be considered a habitual criminal. The only relevant evidence in a habitual offender proceeding was evidence that proved or disproved defendant's prior felony convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

189 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Linthicum v. State


No. 585 S 188


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


511 N.E.2d 1026; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 1019



August 20, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Lawrence Superior Court, The Honorable Don A. Erdmann, Cause No. S 81 CR 39.



DISPOSITION: The habitual offender finding is vacated and remanded to the trial court for a correction of sentence. In other all respects, the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to robbery. He was sentenced to an enhanced term of 20 years. He sought post-conviction relief, alleging that his plea had not been voluntary and intelligent. The trial court denied his petition, but the court reversed and remanded the action. On retrial, defendant was convicted of robbery and found to be a habitual offender. He was sentenced to an term of 20 years for the robbery and 30 years for being a habitual offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to the robbery of a grocery store. He sought post-conviction relief, and the case was remanded so that defendant could withdraw his plea. On retrial, the state added an habitual offender charge, and the trial court sentenced defendant to a greater sentence than the original plea. On appeal, the court vacated the habitual offender finding and remanded the case for resentencing. The court held that Ind. R. P. Post-conviction Remedies 1, § 10 did not allow the trial court to impose a more severe penalty on defendant than originally imposed. Defendant was not prejudiced by the police's actions of returning defendant to the crime scene so that a witness could identify him. One-man showups were not always violative of due process. Because defendant showed no abusive conduct by police, his statement did not require suppression under the Fifth Amendment. Defendant's intoxication jury instruction was properly denied. The trial judge did not abuse his authority by denying the change of venue.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the habitual offender finding and remanded the action to the trial court for resentencing. In all other respects the case was affirmed.

 

190 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State Bd. of Tax Comm'rs v. Lesea Broadcasting Corp.


No. 29S05-8703-TA-350


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


511 N.E.2d 1009; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 1022



August 18, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Indiana Tax Court, The Honorable Thomas G. Fisher, Judge, Cause No. 29T05-8612-TA-00057.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, State Board of Tax Commissioners (Board), sought review of the judgment from the Indiana Tax Court that denied its motion to dismiss appellee taxpayer's complaint. The Board also filed a petition for instructions for taking an interlocutory appeal and asked the court to instruct the parties as to the proper procedures to be followed in order to properly appeal an interlocutory order of the tax court.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer filed a petition with the Board for exemption under Ind. Code § 6-1.1-15-5(c)(1) (Supp. 1986). After the Board denied its petition, the taxpayer filed a complaint with the tax court and deposited the notice of appeal to the Board in the mail. The Board filed a motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction and the tax court denied the motion. In sustaining the tax court, the court held that the notice to the Board as required by Ind. Code § 6-1.1-15-5 was timely filed when it was deposited into the United States Mail, addressed to the Board with postage prepaid, within the time specified under Ind. Code § 6-1.1-15-5. The court found that because Ind. Code § 6-1.1-15-5 was silent both as to the method of filing and as to any definition of "filing" and because the Trial Rules were available, Ind. R. Trial P. 5(B)(2) applied.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the ruling of the tax court that dismissed the Board's motion to dismiss the taxpayer's complaint.

 

191 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Thomas v. State


No. 685 S 262


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


510 N.E.2d 651; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 995



July 28, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Delaware Circuit Court The Honorable Steven Caldemeyer, Judge, No. C 84/43.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by jury in the Delaware Circuit Court (Indiana) of voluntary manslaughter and was sentenced to 16 years incarceration. Defendant appealed, claiming that his motion for mistrial was improperly denied, that certain jury instructions were erroneous, that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction, and that the district court erred in imposing sentence.


OVERVIEW: After defendant, his accomplice, and another person were involved in a barroom brawl with several others, defendant drove his friends to his house, retrieved two weapons, and returned to the bar. Defendant and the accomplice both fired shots in the air; the accomplice shot and killed the bar's owner. On appeal, the court ruled that: (1) defendant did not show how he was harmed by a police officer's alleged coaching of witnesses at trial and thus his motion for a mistrial was properly denied; (2) the circuit court properly instructed the jury on accessory liability because defendant was charged as a principal, and on self-defense, even though he did not assert self-defense at trial; (3) there was substantial evidence of probative value to support the jury's finding, beyond a reasonable doubt, that defendant aided, induced, or caused another person to commit voluntary manslaughter; (4) the sentence imposed was not grossly disproportionate to defendant's crime under Ind. Const. art. I, § 16; and (5) because the circuit court complied with Ind. Code § 35-50-2-5 (1985) and gave reasons for the sentence imposed, the sentence was not manifestly unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the sentence imposed thereon.

 

192 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Whitehead v. State


No. 485 S 142


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


511 N.E.2d 284; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 986; 71 A.L.R.4th 173



July 22, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the LaGrange Circuit Court, The Honorable Howard E. Peterson, Judge No. SV-84-4.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the LaGrange Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised several grounds of error. Except for the restitution and fine orders, the court rejected each claim and affirmed the conviction. The court found that the lower court improperly ordered restitution and that its order imposing a fine failed to provide that defendant should not be imprisoned for failing to pay the court-ordered fine. The court reversed the restitution order and directed the lower court to amend its order regarding the fine. The court rejected defendant's claim of double jeopardy because the granting of his motion for mistrial removed any barrier to re-prosecution and did not implicate the constitutional protections against double jeopardy. The court also held that the lower court's time limitations on voir dire and closing arguments were not an abuse of its discretion. The court found that Miranda was inapplicable to the statements made to the police when they arrived at the crime scene or to statements made to a youth care worker while defendant was in custody and that were voluntary and not given under the influence of any drugs. The court also upheld the sentence because it was within the lower court's discretion and it was supported by the record.


OUTCOME: The court remanded for the purpose of vacating the trial court's restitution order and to add language to the order indicating that defendant should not be imprisoned for failing to pay the court-ordered fine. In all other respects, the court affirmed the lower court's order.

4447 Corp. v. Goldsmith


No. 29S04-8703-CV-270


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA

194 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Resnover v. State


No. 1285 S 515


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


507 N.E.2d 1382; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 934



May 27, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division One, The Honorable John W. Tranberg, Special Judge, Cause No. CR 80 442A.



DISPOSITION: The trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of Murder and Conspiracy to Commit Murder. The Marion Superior Court (Indiana) imposed the death penalty. The convictions and sentences were affirmed on direct appeal. Defendant appealed from an order denying his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering a police officer. The court affirmed the denial of defendant's post appeal petition. The court refused to consider arguments that were heard on direct appeal under Ind. R. Crim. P. 1, § 1(b). The court held that defense counsel's failure to file a trial brief, present a witness, dispute culpability, and failure to object to hearsay was not ineffective assistance of counsel because counsel's decisions were legitimate trial strategy, defendant was not prejudiced by those decisions, and the failure to present mitigating evidence resulted from defendant's boycott of the sentencing stage of trial. A prosecutor's comment during the close of the post conviction evidentiary hearing did not violate defendant's right to remain silent because it was made in response to defense counsel's statement and was directed to defendant's absence, not his silence. There was no error in denying a witness use immunity, because defendant had no right to have use immunity granted. Finally, the claim of judicial bias failed because there was no direct evidence of bias.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant's post conviction petition was affirmed.

 

195 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Munn v. State


No. 384 S 98


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


505 N.E.2d 782; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 863



March 25, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division Five, The Honorable Roy F. Jones, Judge, No. CR83-35E.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division 5 (Indiana), which convicted defendant of rape. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in barring testimony concerning defendant's past sexual conduct with the victim, in not recessing the trial prior to defendant's presentation of evidence, in allowing an officer to testify as to defendant's statements, and that the evidence could not sustain the verdict.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought to bring in evidence of his past sexual relations with the victim, which was denied by the trial court. Defendant offered an alibi defense to the rape charge. Defendant was convicted. On appeal the court affirmed. The court held that Ind. Code § 35-37-4-4 required that in order for evidence concerning the victim's past sexual conduct with defendant to be admissible, the evidence had to be material to a fact at issue and its inflammatory or prejudicial nature could not outweigh its probative value. The court found that the past sexual conduct the victim had with defendant was not material because defendant claimed he didn't have intercourse with the victim at the time she was raped. Defendant claimed alibi, and thus, no issue of consent was presented. The court had found that the relationship the victim had with defendant was material to the issue of motive, and the trial court had properly allowed the victim to be cross-examined on the issue of the relationship, but not the sexual part of the relationship. The court found that defendant waived the issue of the trial court not recessing prior to the defense case because defendant failed to provide a complete record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

196 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Cobb v. State


No. 1084 S 388


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


505 N.E.2d 51; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 860



March 16, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Hancock County Superior Court, The Honorable Richard T. Payne, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of the Hancock County Superior Court (Indiana), which denied the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief after the inmate was convicted of second degree murder and was sentenced to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of second degree murder. The trial court accepted the jury's recommendation and imposed a life sentence. The inmate argued that the trial court erred when it sentenced him because it believed that it was bound by the jury's recommendation. On review, the court found that the jury's decision regarding sentencing was a recommendation, which was not binding on the trial court. The court also found that the jury's sentence did not exceed constitutional boundaries and that the jury was provided with guidelines. The court concluded that the trial court's mistake was not reversible error. The inmate also claimed that he received ineffective assistance of counsel at the trial and appellate level regarding the applicability of the death penalty. The court found that trial counsel warned the inmate that a recent decision regarding the death penalty could make it applicable in his case. Even though it was not applicable, the court found that counsel properly assessed the risk in the inmate's favor. Therefore, the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision that denied the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief was affirmed.

 

197 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


4447 Corp. v. Goldsmith


No. 29S04-8703-CV-270


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


504 N.E.2d 559; 1987 Ind. LEXIS 844



March 2, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Interlocutory Appeal from Hamilton Circuit Court, The Honorable Judith S. Proffitt, Judge, Cause No. C83-346. Interlocutory Appeal from Allen Circuit Court, The Honorable Thomas L. Ryan, Judge, Cause No. CC-84-446. No. 4-1283 A 415 in the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Transfer is granted and the opinion of the Court of Appeals is vacated. The causes are remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated interlocutory appeal, appellee prosecutors sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals, Fourth District (Indiana), which found the Racketeer Influence and Corrupt Organizations Act (RICO), Ind. Code § 35-45-6-1 et seq and the Civil Remedies for Racketeering Activity (CRRA), Ind. Code § 34-4-30.5-1 et seq, unconstitutional as applied to the seizure of appellant bookstore owners' property.


OVERVIEW: The bookstore owners were accused of selling obscene material and the prosecutors filed CRRA petitions for the forfeiture of the owners' property. In these consolidated cases, the trial courts found probable cause of RICO violations and ordered the forfeitures. The court of appeals vacated the orders, finding CRRA and RICO unconstitutional as applied to obscene material. The court reversed, and vacated the court of appeals' opinion, finding that (1) whether the materials seized were obscene was irrelevant as the seizure was a remedy for a RICO violation and not an effort to seize obscene material and, therefore, the CRRA and RICO were not unconstitutional as applied to obscene materials, (2) prior convictions for the underlying offenses were not required to prove a pattern of racketeering activity under Ind. Code § 35-45-6-2, and (3) the application for seizure did not violate due process where there was a judicial determination of probable cause and Ind. Code § 34-3-30.5-3 was interpreted to require a hearing within a reasonable time.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the court of appeals and remanded to the trial courts as the RICO and CRRA were not unconstitutional as applied to obscene material.

 

198 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Carpenter v. State


No. 784 S 284


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


501 N.E.2d 1067; 1986 Ind. LEXIS 1432



December 23, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Perry Circuit Court, The Honorable Max W. Apple, Special Judge, Cause No. 77-CR-33.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of a judgment from the Perry County Circuit Court (Indiana) denying his petition for post-conviction relief. Defendant was convicted upon a retrial of kidnapping and rape while armed, and these convictions were upheld on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The inmate kidnapped his victim at knife point and raped her. The court rejected the inmate's contention that the post-conviction relief court erred in denying his petition without issuing specific findings of fact and conclusions of law. The court held that although Ind. R. Crim. R. P. 1, § 6 required a trial court considering a petition for post-conviction relief to make specific findings of fact and conclusions of law, automatic reversal for failure to do so was not required because the rule functioned primarily for the benefit of an appellate court. The court found the inmate failed to meet his burden of demonstrating he was denied his right to effective assistance of counsel. The court noted that representing the inmate (then defendant) and a co-defendant did not constitute ineffective representation per se. The court found no errors with respect to sentencing despite the fact that the sentence imposed upon retrial for the same charges was considerably more severe because the sentence was within the permissible scope. Finally, the court determined that because the inmate was a violent offender, he was not subject to treatment under the criminal sexual deviant statute.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

199 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Woodson v. State


No. 185 S8


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


501 N.E.2d 409; 1986 Ind. LEXIS 1414



December 16, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 10, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division VI, The Honorable Thomas Alsip, Judge, Cause No. CR83-155F.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Marion Superior Court, Criminal Division VI (Indiana), which convicted defendant of possession of a controlled substance with intent to distribute. Defendant was convicted of a Class A felony based on the total weight of 100 bindles of heroin seized from his home. Defendant argued that the evidence supported no more than a Class D felony conviction for the possession of less than three grams of heroin.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that because the total mixture of each bindle contained trace amounts of heroin and since the police conducted only preliminary tests on some of the separate bindles, it was improper for police to empty the contents of each of the bindles seized to determine the total heroin content. On appeal, the court disagreed. The separate bindles were uniform in size, the contents were uniform in appearance, and there was no issue as to what the precise quantity was in each individual bindle. Moreover, the statutes involving controlled substance dealing intentionally utilized the weight of the entire substance delivered. Thus, the method of ascertaining the quantity was proper and it resulted in evidence sufficient to support the Class A felony charge. Further, the State's evidence negating defendant's claim that the large quantity of heroin seized was for his own use was a sufficient basis from which the jury could infer that defendant intended to sell the heroin. Finally, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to allow defendant to withdraw his jury trial waiver because there was nothing to support defendant's claim that the waiver was not knowingly made.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

200 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


B & M Coal Corp. v. United Mine Workers


No. 74S04-8612-CV-1036


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


501 N.E.2d 401; 1986 Ind. LEXIS 1421



December 12, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Spencer Circuit Court, The Honorable Edward C. Theobald, Special Judge, No. C 77-261, No. 4-884 A 231, In the Court of Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenors-appellees, county clerk, county auditor, county council, and county board of commissioners (county), sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Indiana), which held that appellee litigants retained a protectable property right in the interest accrued on funds invested by the county and the retention of the interest was an unconstitutional taking.


OVERVIEW: The mine suffered damage at the hands of union members and the mine ultimately was granted a judgment against the union members involved. While pending appeal, the union members paid moneys into a fund held by the trial court. The county clerk, pursuant to Ind. Code § 5-13-1-3.5(b), invested the fund and retained the interest received on the fund for the benefit of the county. The lower court held that the litigants were not entitled to the interest and the appellate court reversed. The court affirmed the appellate court's decision and held that because the appeal bond was clearly private, the clerk's retention of the interest was an unconstitutional taking under U.S. Const. amend. V and Ind. Const. art. 1. The court determined that the statute involved was not unconstitutional and determined that the statute had to be read to differentiate between private and public funds. The court held that public funds could be invested by the clerk for the benefit of the county and private funds could not.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court and held that the litigants were entitled to the interest on their fund.
